Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
Methodological Shift: Early vs Later Hanafi Usul
Methodological clarification on proof structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the methodological approach of the early Hanafi shuyukh from that of the later scholars regarding the use of logical rules in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi scholars structured proofs as syllogisms (sughra-kubra), unlike early shuyukh who focused only on the purpose.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawzih wa al-Talwih explains why the author adopts a rational framework for presenting proofs. It clarifies the difference between two eras in Hanafi usul: the early shuyukh, who were content with clarifying the objective without formal logical structure, and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin), who insisted on building proofs on the rules of ilm al-mizan (logic). Understanding this shift is essential for reading later Hanafi texts where arguments are presented in syllogistic form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Methodological Approaches
The passage contrasts the approach of the early shuyukh (qudama' al-mashayikh) with that of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin). Pinpoint the key difference: early shuyukh only aimed 'to achieve the purpose' (iqtisaran 'ala husul al-maqsud), while later scholars base proofs on the rules of logic (qawa'id al-mizan).
2
Understand the Role of Logical Syllogisms
The later scholars present proofs in the form of syllogisms (sughra and kubra). Recognize that this means each argument has a premise, a conclusion, and logical structure. This is borrowed from ilm al-mizan (the science of logic).
3
Recognize the Significance for Reading the Text
Knowing that the author follows the later method, you must read arguments as formally structured syllogisms. Do not expect a mere statement of the ruling; look for the logical chain supporting it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله مؤسسة على قواعد المعقول اي مبنية على الوجوه والشرائط المذكورة في علم الميزان لاكما هو داب قدماء المشائخ من الاقتصار على حصول المقصود . کر ہمہ، موسسہ یعنی بنی ہیں ان وجود اور شرائط پر جو مذکور ہے علم المیزان میں نہ کہ ایسے جیسا کہ عادت ہے قدماء مشائخ کی یعنی اکتفاء کر لینا مقصود کے حاصل ہونے پر ۔ غرض تحقیق لغرر ! اور متقدمین و متاخرین کے طریق میں فرق کا بیان - مؤسسة کا معنی مبنیہ کیا ہے یہ شتق من الاساس ہے بمعنی بنیاد مقصد عبارت یہ ہے کہ میری کتاب میں قدماء مشائخ کا طرز اختیار نہیں کیا گیا جو صرف تبیین مقصد پر اکتفاء کیا کرتے تھے اور قواعد وضوابط منطقیہ کی طرف التفات نہ کرتے تھے بلکہ متاخرین کا انداز اختیار کیا گیا ہے کہ دلائل علم المیز الن- کے قواعد پر مشتمل ہوں گے دلائل کو صغری و کبری کے ضمن میں بیان کیا جائے گا وغیرہ۔
His statement: 'Founded on the rules of the rational' meaning built upon the aspects and conditions mentioned in the science of logic, not as is the practice of the early shuyukh of restricting themselves to achieving the purpose. The purpose is that in my book the method of the early shuyukh is not adopted, who used to suffice with clarifying the purpose and did not pay attention to logical rules and principles, but rather the method of the later scholars is adopted, such that the proofs will be based on the rules of the science of logic, and the proofs will be presented in the form of premises and syllogisms, etc.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification from the commentator. It explains the author's approach in writing the book: rather than following the early shuyukh who were content with mere clarification of objectives without strict logical structure, the author builds his proofs on the formal rules of logic (ilm al-mizan). This means arguments will be presented as syllogisms (sughra and kubra) following the method of the muta'akhkhirin (later scholars). The term 'mu'assasah' is derived from 'asas' meaning foundation, emphasizing that the entire work is constructed on these rational principles.

Key Terms
مؤسسة (mu'assasah): Built or founded upon, derived from 'asas' (foundation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's methodological departure from the early shuyukh?
A) He ignores logical rules
B) He relies solely on logical syllogisms
C) He builds proofs on logical rules and presents them as syllogisms
D) He does not use proofs at all

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi usul scholars adopt formal logical syllogisms to structure proofs, distinguishing their method from the early shuyukh who focused only on the purpose.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Commentator's Method and the Path of Ijtihad
Commentator explains his methodology and defines key terms from the matn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of steps a mujtahid follows in qiyas according to the Hanafi method and explain the importance of lexical precision in identifying the ‘illah.

Core Idea
The mujtahid begins with the word, then its apparent meaning, then its legal meaning, and finally seeks the ‘illah.

This lesson unpacks the commentator's introduction to a major Hanafi usul text. The passage explains the rationale behind the Lawgiver's signs and indicators, the structured approach to deriving rulings, and the meticulous lexical analysis required in Hanafi usul. You will learn the precise order of investigation that a mujtahid undertakes when performing qiyas, and see how careful attention to language is the foundation of sound legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of indicators
The Lawgiver placed signs (amārāt) in the texts to guide the mujtahid. These are the ‘illal that allow analogical deduction.
2
Trace the mujtahid's sequence
The humble scholar first looks at the word (lafẓ), then its apparent lexical meaning (maʿnā lughawī ẓāhirī), then its legal meaning (maʿnā sharʿī bāṭinī), and finally searches for the ‘illah placed by the Lawgiver.
This sequence is the core of Hanafi qiyas methodology.
3
Analyze the lexical example
The commentator examines the word 'jadd' showing how vowelization changes meaning (grandfather/fortune vs. effort). This highlights the precision needed.
4
Understand the metaphor for engagement
The term 'akbba' (to fall on one's face) metaphorically describes the mujtahid's total focus—as if falling onto the text.
5
Relate to the commentator's own work
The commentator explains he selected al-Bazdawi's text for its authority and combines insights from al-Mahsul and Ibn al-Hajib, showing the layered nature of usul scholarship.

Source Text

مسک المليح شرح التوضيح والعلوي في علامات و امارات إلى كہ ركھا هے ان کو شارع نے تا كہ ہدایت حاصل كریں ان كے ساتھ مقاصد كی طرف جہ نے بنی علی اربعہ اركان كہا تو پھر ان اركان اربعہ كو ترتیب شمارع كے مطابق ذكر كیا۔ تشریح ! جب ماقبل میں مصنف نے اركان اربعہ كا ذكر كیا تو اب ان كو اسی ترتیب سے ذكر كر رہے ہیں جو شارع نے بیان فرمائی حاصل اینكہ اللہ تعالی كی كتاب میں جو مجملات و مہمات تھے انہوں نے اپنے نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی سنت اور خطاب فاصل سے ان كو كھول دیا پھر دعا کی جب تك دین كے جھنڈے اجتماع مجتہدین کے ساتھ بلندر ہیں اللہ کی رحمت نبی کریم نے پر نازل ہوتی رہے پھر اللہ تعالی نے قیاس کرنے كرتے ہیں پھر ان کی عمل کی تلاش كی طرف متوجہ ہوتے ہیں جو شارع نے رکھی ہوتی ہیں پھر ان عمل كے ذریعہ سے مقیس كا حكم معلوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ وبعد فان العبد المتوسل - حل مفردات اجده از ضرب مصدر جدہ نیا ہونا مصدر جدا كوشش كرنا تحقیق كرنا سخت الجده از ہونا عظیم ہونا جد سعده، بمعنی عظم سعادته و تخته وسعد جده سمع نیك بخت ہوتا جداگر بفتح الجیم ہو تو اس کے دو معنی ہیں (۱) دادا (۲) نصیبہ اگر بکسر الجیم ہو تو اس کا معنی كوشش تو سعد جعدہ بمعنی این جدہ ہو گاف حول جمع محل قومی ور آدمی مكبین ا كباب سے ہے معنی لغوی چہرے کے بل گر نا مجازی و مرادی معنی كسی ٹی كی طرف غایت توجہ كیساتھ متوجہ ہونا مناسبت یہ ہے كہ جو آدمی كسی شیء كی طرف غایت توجہ كرتا ہے تو گو پاوہ اس پر گر جاتا ہے۔ بواءه الله معنی انزل و اسكن ۔ جلیل الشان اى تعظيم الامر رفيع القدر با ہر البرہان - ای غالب الجد و فائق الجهد البربان هو الجهة القطعية التقنيه - مركوزای مدفون (از نصر) زمین میں گاڑ نا دفن كرنا ۔ كنوز جمع كنز خزینه از ضرب جمع كرنا ذخیرہ كرنا اضافہ كنوز الى المعانی من قبیل اضافة المشبہ بہ الی المشبہ ہے ۔ صخور جمع صحر سخت پتھر اس جگہ بھی اضافت المشهر بد الی المشبہ ہے۔ مرموز (نفر ضرب ) اشارہ كرنا۔ غوامض جمع غامضہ (از نصر و كرم ) كلام كا دقیق ہونا۔ نكت جمع نكتہ دقیقہ لطیفہ جس كو ذہین آدمی معلوم كر سكے لحدة نظره دقائق جمع رقیقہ - اسرار جمع اشارات جمع اشارہ اضافته الغوامض الی نكت من قبیل اضافه الصلة الى موصوف اصل عبارت الثلث الغامضه الحافظ جمع لحظ فتح السلام النظر الى شي بمنو خر العین آنكھ کے كونے سے دیکھنا زبدة خلاصه منيعة بمعنی مضبوط (بلند) ای محكتم متشباً باب تفعل متعلق ہونا چھٹنا اهداب جمع هدب وهو الورقة الدقيقة وطرف الثوب كنارا جسے (پھندن ) كہا جاتا ہے والمراد اطراف السحر وانواعہ والمقصد ان الكلام باعتبار الاشتمال على انواع البلاغة والفصاحة ووجوه البيان وطرق تحسین الکلام كانه انواع السحر، العروة عروة كل شئ قبضہ كا الكوز والسيف والسكین۔ تركيب ! فحول العلماء مفعول اول ريتملكين مفعول دوم وعلى قواعد المعقول جار مجرور تاسیس کے متعلق ہے، تاسیسة وتقسیمہ حاولت ، كا مفعول ہے مور دا حال ہے حاولت سے زبدۃ مفعول ہے موردا كا سالكا وكذا متشباً ومتمسكا احوال من حاولت ۔ ترجمہ ! اور بعد الحمد والصلوۃ پس عبد متوسل الی الله با قوی الذریعة ( ایمان كامل یا نبی كریم ع عبید اللہ بن تاج الشریعہ عظیم ہو اس کی سعادت و نیك بخت اور سعید ہو اس کا داد یا اچھا ہو اس كا نصیبہ (ان كان الجد بفتح الجیم) اگر بکسر الجیم ہوتو معنی ہوگا كامیاب ہو اس کی كوشش كہتا ہے وہ عہد جب دیکھا میں نے ماہر علماء كو كہ وہ گرنے والے تھے ہر عہد وزمانہ میں اصول فقہ کے مباحثہ پر ای مقبلین سے مكین كا مجازی معنی بیان كیا یعنی متوجہ ہونے والے تھے اس مباحثہ اصول فقہ پر من اك سے تحقیق اشتقاقی بیان كی كہ مكین اك سے ہے اك علی وجہ بمعنی سقط علی وجہ فان من اقبل سے حقیقی و مجازی معنی میں مناسبت كا بیان ہے كہ جو شخص كسی چیز پر غایت توجہ كے ساتھ متوجہ ہوتا ہے گویا وہ اس پر گر جاتا ہے اصول فقہ كتاب ہونے والی ہے شیخ امام كیلئے جو ائمہ عظام کے مقتدی میں فخر الاسلام ہیں ان كا اسم گرامی علی بزودی ہے اللہ تعالی انكو دار السلام میں جگہ عطا فرائے اور یہ كتاب عظیم الشان اور غالب فائق البرھان تھی اس كے معانی كے خزینے مدفون تھے اس کی عبارت کی چٹانوں میں اور اس کے نقاط غامضہ ( گہرے و باریك ) کی طرف اشارہ كیا گیا ہے اس كتاب كے اشارات کے اسرار كی باریکیوں میں اور پایا میں نے بعض علماء كو كہ وہ طعنہ کرنے والے تھے اس كتاب کے ظاہری الفاظ پر بوجہ كوتاہ ہونے ان كی نظر کے اس علی بزودی کی آنكھوں كے كونوں سے دیکھی ہوئی جگہوں سے ۔ ای لابد ركوع سے اسی عبارت كا مقصد بیان كر رہے ہیں كہ نہیں حاصل كر سكتے وہ علماء كرام گہری نظر كے ساتھ ان چیزوں كو جن كو حاصل كر لیتا ہے علی بزودی اپنی آنكھوں کے كونوں وكناروں كے ساتھ بغیر اس کے كہ وہ دیکھے اس کی طرف بالقصد تو میں نے ارادہ كیا اس اصول بزودی کی چھان بین کرنے کا اور اسكی تنظیم و ترتیب كا اور (حاولت ای طلبت ) میں نے طلب كیا اس کی مراد كی وضاحت كرنے كو اور اسكو سمجھانے كو اور میں نے ارادہ كیا اس کی تاسیس اور تقسیم كا قواعد معقول کے مطابق در انحالیکہ وارد کرنے والا ہوں میں اس کتاب میں محصول (امام رازی کی کتاب) كے مباحث کے خلاصہ كو اور امام محقق و مدقق جمال اعراب علامہ ابن الحاجب کی (الاصول كتاب) كے خلاصہ كو ساتھ تحقیقات عجیبہ كے اور تدقیقات مخفیہ محكمہ و مضبوط كے ایسی تحقیقات جن سے كتب خالی ہیں میں چلنے والا ہوں اس كتاب میں ضبط اور اختصار كے راستہ پر میں چھٹنے والا ہوں سحر كے اطراف كے ساتھ اور پکڑنے والا ہوں اعجاز كے (كڑے) كو ۔ تشریح ! اس عبارت میں مصنف علت تعیین متن علت تصنیف و كیفیت مصنف بیان فرما رہے ہیں لمارئیت سے علت تعیین متن ہے جس كا حاصل یہ ہے علامہ فخر الاسلام علی بزودی کی تصنیف شدہ كتاب اصول الفقہ لوگوں كی توجہ كا مركز تھی اور جلیل الشان و یا ہر البرھان تھی اس بناء پر میں نے شرح لکھنے كیلئے اس كو منتخب كیا مركوز ومرموز میں علت تصنیف ہے كہ كتاب مشکل ترین تھی اس کے
Misk al-Maleeh, commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: In signs and indicators that the Lawgiver placed so that guidance may be obtained through them towards the objectives. He said it is based on four pillars, then he mentioned these four pillars according to the order of the Lawgiver. Explanation: When the author mentioned the four pillars previously, he now mentions them in the order that the Lawgiver stated. The gist is that what was ambiguous and difficult in the Book of Allah, He clarified through the Sunnah of His Prophet and decisive address. Then he supplicated as long as the banners of religion remain raised with the consensus of the mujtahids, the mercy of Allah continues to descend upon the Prophet. Then Allah placed signs and indicators in the texts for those who perform qiyas, which are the 'illal (causes), so that by seeing them, those who perform qiyas can derive the ruling for the analogized case. So the humble first look at the word, then its apparent lexical meaning, then its internal legal meaning, then they attend to the search for the 'illal placed by the Lawgiver, and by means of these 'illal the ruling for the analogized case becomes known. And after that, the servant who seeks nearness - vocabulary analysis: ajad from d-r-b, meaning newness, jidd meaning effort, research, strictness; jadd meaning greatness; jaddu meaning his grandfather; he explained that if jadd is read with fatha, it has two meanings: (1) grandfather, (2) fortune; if with kasra, meaning effort, then sa'da jaddahu means his luck was good. akb from k-b-b, literal meaning falling on the face, metaphorical meaning focusing extreme attention on something, because one who focuses extremely on something nearly falls upon it. buwwa'ahu Allah means He settled him. jaleel al-shaan means great in status. zahir al-burhan means evident proof. murkaz means buried. kunuz means treasures. sukhur means rocks. mirmaz means signalled. ghawamid means subtle points. nukat means fine points. dawa'iq means minute details. asrar means secrets. isharat means indications. al-ghawamid ila nukat is an addition of something similar to the described. The original phrase is 'third subtle point'. al-hiz meaning glancing from the corner of the eye. zubdah means essence. manee'ah means strong. mutashabbih means clinging. ahdab means fringe of garment, metaphorically the types of magic. The purpose is that the speech, because it contains types of eloquence and rhetoric and aspects of clarity and ways of improving speech, is like types of magic. al-urwah means handle. Syntactic parsing: 'fuhool al-ulama' is first object, 'yamtalikun' is second object, 'ala qawa'id al-ma'qool' is prepositional phrase related to 'ta'sis'. 'ta'sisahu wa taqsimahu' is object of 'hawaltu'. 'murda' is a state from 'hawaltu'. 'zubdah' is object of 'mawrida'. 'salikan' and 'mutashabbihan' and 'mutamassikan' are states from 'hawaltu'. Translation: After praise and salutation, the servant seeking nearness to Allah through the strongest means (complete faith or the Prophet) - Ubaidullah ibn Taj al-Shari'ah - may his happiness and good fortune be great, and his grandfather be prosperous or his luck good (if jadd is with fatha), if with kasra then may his effort succeed - says that he saw the scholars falling in every age into the discussion of usul al-fiqh; he explained the metaphorical meaning of mukibbun as turning their attention to the discussion of usul al-fiqh. He gave the etymological analysis that mukibbun is derived from akbba, akbba ala wajh meaning to fall on the face; the appropriateness between literal and metaphorical meaning is that one who focuses extreme attention on something nearly falls upon it. The book of usul al-fiqh will be for the Shaykh and Imam, who among the great imams is Fakhr al-Islam, his noble name is Ali al-Bazdawi, may Allah grant him a place in Dar al-Salam. This book was great in status and dominant with clear evidence; its meanings were buried treasures, its expression like rocks, and its subtle points were hinted at in the intricacies of the book's allusions. He found some scholars criticizing its apparent words due to the weakness of their sight, while al-Bazdawi could see with the corners of his eyes. He intended to scrutinize and organize al-Bazdawi's usul, and sought to clarify its meaning, and intended to establish and divide it according to rational principles, while incorporating into this book the essence of the discussions of al-Mahsul (by Imam al-Razi) and the essence of the book of al-Usul by the confirming Imam Jamal al-Arab Allamah Ibn al-Hajib, along with wonderful investigations and hidden refined points that are strong, such that books are devoid of them. He will proceed on the path of conciseness and brevity, clinging to the edges of magic and grasping the handle of inimitability. Explanation: In this expression, the author explains the reason for selecting the text and the reason for authorship and the method. From 'lima ra'aytu' is the reason for selecting the text: that the book of usul al-fiqh by Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi was the center of people's attention and was great in status and clear in proof; for this reason he chose it to write a commentary. In 'murkaz wa mirmaz' is the reason for authorship: that the book was extremely difficult.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is from the beginning of a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a renowned Hanafi usul text. The commentator opens by explaining the purpose of the Lawgiver's signs and indicators in the texts, which are the 'illal (causes) used in qiyas. He emphasizes that the mujtahid must first consider the word, then its apparent meaning, then its legal meaning, and then search for the 'illah to derive rulings for analogous cases. This method reflects the Hanafi approach of combining textual analysis with rational inference (istihsan, qiyas). The commentator then provides a detailed lexical analysis of key Arabic terms from the matn: 'jadd', 'akbba', 'murkaz', etc., showing the precision required in usul terminology. For example, 'jadd' can mean grandfather or effort depending on vocalization; 'akbba' literally means to fall on one's face but metaphorically means to focus intensely, which is appropriate for the mujtahid's engagement with the text. The commentator also explains his methodology: he selects al-Bazdawi's work for its authority and clarity, and incorporates insights from al-Mahsul and Ibn al-Hajib's usul works, while adding unique investigations. This demonstrates the intertextuality of Hanafi usul scholarship, where commentaries build upon earlier authoritative texts, and the commentator's role is to clarify and systematize. The passage is typical of a sharh, where the commentator expands on the matn by defining terms, analyzing syntax, and justifying the choice of text.

Key Terms
جد (jadd): Depending on vowelization: with fatha on jīm means grandfather or fortune; with kasra means effort and striving.
اکب (akbba): Literally 'to fall on one's face'; metaphorically 'to focus extreme attention on something'.
قواعد معقول (qawāʿid al-maʿqūl): Principles of reason; the rational foundations upon which the commentator bases his tasīs (establishment) and taqsīm (division) of the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul mandates a structured sequence: word → apparent meaning → legal meaning → 'illah, ensuring that analogy (qiyas) is grounded in precise textual understanding.

The Hierarchical Position of Usul al-Fiqh
Explains the status of usul al-fiqh relative to fiqh and kalam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hierarchical relationship among usul al-fiqh, fiqh, and kalam according to the Hanafi school, and identify the dependency of usul on kalam.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh sits between theology and law: it depends on kalam and serves fiqh.

The science of usul al-fiqh is not an independent discipline; it has a defined position within the Islamic sciences. This passage clarifies that usul is above fiqh (because it provides the universal evidences for deriving rulings) but below kalam (because its foundations rest on theological premises). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for grasping the role and authority of usul al-fiqh in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sciences mentioned
Locate in the passage where fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and kalam are referred to. Note how each is defined.
Fiqh deals with detailed rulings; usul deals with universal evidences; kalam deals with theological foundations.
2
Trace the dependency chain
The passage states that usul depends on kalam for its foundations (mabani), and that fiqh depends on usul for its evidence methodology. Outline this dependency in one sentence.
Kalam → Usul → Fiqh.
3
Define the key components
Using the passage, write definitions for usul al-shari'ah, mabani al-usul, and furu' al-shari'ah.
These terms are explicitly defined in the Arabic text.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a sample issue
Consider a specific fiqh ruling (e.g., validity of a sale). Map how usul provides the universal rule (e.g., 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha') and kalam provides the groundwork (e.g., that Allah's commands are binding).
This step reinforces the practical relevance.

His statement: 'since he made the attachment of mahamid (praiseworthy things) to some favors an indication of the greatness of the science that is the subject of this book' — and an indication of its lofty status. The Shari'ah encompasses fiqh and other matters established by revealed evidence, such as the issue of seeing Allah (ru'yah), the afterlife, the authority of consensus and analogy as proofs, and similar matters. The principles (usul) of the Shari'ah are its universal evidences. The foundations of usul (mabani al-usul) are what they are built upon: the knowledge of the essence and attributes (of Allah), prophethood, etc. Their consolidation (tamhid) is to straighten and reform them by being in accordance with truth and the right path. The branches (furu') of the Shari'ah are its detailed rulings explained in the science of fiqh. Their meanings (ma'ani) are the particular, detailed causes (ilal juz'iyyah) for each and every issue. Their precision (diqqat) is that they are subtle, not attainable easily by everyone. All of these are favors that deserve praise, for through the Shari'ah is the order of this world and the reward of the Hereafter, and through the precision of the meanings of fiqh are the elevation of the ranks of scholars and their attainment of reward in the abode of recompense. In this statement is an indication that the science of usul is above fiqh and below kalam. Because knowledge of particular rulings through their detailed evidences depends on knowledge of the universal states of the evidences in terms of how they lead to legal rulings, and that depends on knowledge of the Creator, His attributes, the truthfulness of the messenger, the indication of his miracles, and similar matters encompassed by the science of kalam, which investigates the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, the afterlife, and what is connected to that according to the law of Islam.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses the hierarchy of Islamic sciences. The author states that usul al-fiqh is above fiqh because it provides the universal evidences and methods that fiqh uses to derive detailed rulings. However, usul is below kalam (theology) because the foundations of usul—such as the existence and attributes of God, the truthfulness of prophets, etc.—are established by kalam. Thus, usul depends on kalam. The passage also describes the components: usul al-shari'ah (universal evidences), mabani al-usul (theological foundations), furu' al-shari'ah (detailed fiqh rulings), and their causes. All these are favors that deserve praise. This is a typical Hanafi usul view that distinguishes the hierarchy clearly.

Key Terms
اصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The universal evidences of the Shari'ah, i.e., the proofs and principles from which rulings are derived.
مباني الاصول (mabani al-usul): The foundations of usul, i.e., the theological premises that usul al-fiqh depends on.
فروع الشريعة (furu' al-shari'ah): The branches of the Shari'ah, i.e., the detailed rulings of fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Usul al-fiqh is below kalam.
C) They are independent disciplines with no overlap.
D) Usul al-fiqh is part of kalam.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh occupies a middle position in the hierarchy of Islamic sciences: it is above fiqh but below kalam, depending on theology for its foundations.

Praise (Hamd): The Necessity of Belief and Action
Explanation of hamd with scriptural proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why hamd requires belief, speech, and righteous action, and apply the Quranic verse 35:10 to demonstrate the role of action.

Core Idea
Praise without action is like a tree without fruit—it does not ascend.

This lesson explores the Hanafi understanding of praise (hamd) as taught by the commentator on Al-Tawdih. True praise involves not only intellectual assent and verbal expression but also righteous deeds. The Quranic verse 'To Him ascends goodly speech, and righteous action raises it' is the key proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of hamd
The commentator states that hamd is composed of belief (i'tiqad), speech (qawl), and action ('amal). List these three.
2
Analyze the Quranic dalil
Read the verse 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب والعمل الصالح يرفعه' and note how the pronoun 'يرفعه' (raises it) refers to righteous action (العمل الصالح).
The verb 'يرفعه' is singular masculine, but 'العمل' is masculine, 'الكلم' is masculine. The phrasing indicates action causes speech to ascend.
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The verse shows that goodly speech ascends to Allah, but only through the raising of righteous action. Without action, speech does not ascend.
This demonstrates that hamd requires action for acceptance.
4
Consider the hadith
The Prophet said: 'Whoever has no action, it is not accepted.' This reinforces the same point.
5
Apply to a real scenario
A person who verbally praises Allah but neglects obligatory deeds—his praise is incomplete and does not gain acceptance.
This links usul to fiqh practice.

Praise is said to be either belief in the essence of Allah Most High characterized by perfect attributes, or it is verbal expression, or it is action with the limbs. So in this sense, Muhammad is also composed of these three things, becoming like a good tree: belief is like a firm root for the tree of praise; if belief is not correct, then it becomes like a bad tree with no root, as stated. And righteous action for the tree of praise is like branches; if there is no righteous action, then praise will not ascend to Allah nor be accepted by Him, and praise will be like a tree with no branches, a barren tree bearing no fruit, because action is the means to attain Paradise and elevation of ranks, as the divine saying: 'and righteous action raises it.' The pronoun 'raises' refers to righteous action, and the pronoun 'it' refers to goodly word. And the Prophet said: 'Whoever has no action, it is not accepted.' Thus it is proven that praise without action is useless. So the author indicated that the tree of praise has a firm root, which is firm Islamic belief based on knowledge of tawhid and attributes, and for the tree of praise there is a branch that ascends to Allah and is accepted by Him, and that is righteous action in accordance with the Sharia, built upon knowledge of the laws and rulings. And he pointed to specificity... the purpose is explanation of points: In 'إليه يصعد', the advancement of the word 'إليه' indicates specificity and restriction because advancing what should be delayed indicates restriction, and mentioning the imperfect verb 'يصعد' indicates continuous renewal of ascent.

His statement: 'on that making praise attached to some blessings is an indication of the greatness of the science in which this authorship occurred and a proof of its high status, and Sharia encompasses fiqh and other matters established by revelatory proofs, like the issue of seeing Allah, resurrection, consensus and analogy being proofs, and the like. And the principles of Sharia are its universal proofs, and the foundations of the principles are what they are built upon from knowledge of the Essence, Attributes, prophethoods, and their establishment, rectification, being in accordance with truth and the path of correctness. And the branches of Sharia are its detailed rulings explained in the science of fiqh, and their meanings are the particular, detailed causes for each individual issue, and their subtlety being so deep and delicate that not everyone can easily reach them. And all of that are blessings that necessitate praise, because through Sharia is the order of the world and the reward of the Hereafter, and through the subtlety of the meanings of fiqh is the elevation of the ranks of scholars and their attainment of reward in the abode of recompense. And in this speech is an indication that the science of usul is above fiqh and below kalam, because the knowledge of particular rulings with their detailed proofs depends on knowing the conditions of the universal proofs in terms of how they lead to legal rulings, and that depends on knowing the Creator Most High, His attributes, the truthfulness of the messenger, the indication of his miracles, and the like, which is included in the science of kalam, which investigates the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, resurrection, and what is connected to that according to the law of Islam.'

His statement: 'on that making the attachment' etc. - The purpose of the commentator is to answer an objection. The objection is: There are millions of blessings in the world, and 'praise' is a collective inclusive term requiring that praise be in return for all blessings. So why did the author (Sadr al-Shariah) specifically limit praise to the science of Sharia and make that alone the object of praise? What is the point? The answer: The commentator replied that Sadr al-Shariah, by making the blessing of knowledge the object of praise, is indicating the greatness, honor, and high status of knowledge, as if the real blessing is this knowledge; other blessings are virtually non-existent in comparison. 'And Sharia encompasses fiqh... up to the end of this speech' - the purpose of the commentator is to explain and clarify the various words of the text. Regarding 'Sharia', the commentator clarifies that Sharia does not only mean the science of fiqh, but rather both fiqh and non-fiqh are meant. However, by non-fiqh are meant those matters and issues that are established by revelatory proofs (sam'i proof) like the issues of seeing Allah, resurrection, consensus being a proof, analogy being a proof. Matters that are established by rational proofs are not intended by Sharia. Question: Why specify revelatory proofs? Why are matters established by rational proofs not included in Sharia? Answer: The reason for the specification is that the word 'Sharia' in the text is the mudaf ilayh of 'usul', and the rule is...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening lines of Al-Tawdih, explaining the nature of praise (hamd) and its relation to belief and action, and then discussing the scope of Sharia and the hierarchy of Islamic sciences. The commentator first explains that true praise of Allah involves belief, speech, and action, and uses the Quranic verse 'To Him ascends goodly speech, and righteous action raises it' to show that praise without righteous deeds is like a tree without fruit. This guards against the misunderstanding that mere verbal or intellectual acknowledgment is sufficient. Then the passage addresses why the author (Sadr al-Shariah) attached praise specifically to the science of Sharia, explaining that this highlights the supreme value of sacred knowledge—without which worldly and otherworldly order cannot be achieved. The commentator then clarifies that 'Sharia' in this context includes not only fiqh (jurisprudence) but also other matters established by revelatory proofs (sam'i), such as the beatific vision (ru'ya), resurrection (ma'ad), and the authority of consensus and analogy. This excludes matters known purely by reason (aqli). The passage further arranges the sciences hierarchically: usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) is above fiqh because it provides the universal proofs from which fiqh derives, but it is below kalam (theology) because kalam deals with the foundational beliefs about God, prophethood, and the afterlife upon which usul depends. This hierarchy is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi usul tradition, which positions kalam as a prerequisite for usul al-fiqh, unlike some other approaches. The commentator also answers a potential objection: why restrict praise to the science of Sharia when there are countless blessings? The answer is that the blessing of knowledge is the greatest and most fundamental, so it is the proper focus of praise. Throughout, the commentary underscores the centrality of sacred knowledge and the interconnectedness of belief, action, and the various Islamic disciplines.

Key Terms
حمد (Hamd): Praise of Allah, which requires belief, speech, and righteous action to be complete and accepted.
شريعة (Shari'a): Sharia encompasses fiqh and other matters established by revelatory proofs (sam'i), such as the beatific vision, resurrection, consensus, and analogy.
عمل صالح ('Amal salih): Righteous action in accordance with Sharia, which is essential for the acceptance of praise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They are independent and both ascend equally.
B) Goodly speech ascends by itself, and righteous action ascends separately.
C) Righteous action raises goodly speech to Allah.
D) Goodly speech is more important than righteous action.

Key Takeaway
True praise of Allah requires belief, speech, and righteous action to ascend and be accepted.

Sharia: Its Scope and the Hierarchy of Islamic Sciences
Definition of Sharia and hierarchy of sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sharia in the Hanafi usul sense and explain the hierarchy of fiqh, usul al-fiqh, and kalam.

Core Idea
Sharia includes both fiqh and other revelatory matters; usul al-fiqh is above fiqh but below kalam.

This lesson clarifies that Sharia is not limited to fiqh but encompasses all matters established by revelatory proofs, such as the beatific vision, resurrection, and the authority of consensus and analogy. It also describes the hierarchy of Islamic sciences, positioning usul al-fiqh between fiqh and kalam, which is a distinctive feature of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Sharia
The commentator says Sharia includes fiqh and other matters established by revelatory proofs (sam'i). List examples: ru'ya, ma'ad, ijma, qiyas.
2
Identify the components of usul al-Sharia
Usul al-Sharia are the universal proofs (adilla kulliya).
3
Identify furu' al-Sharia
Furu' are detailed rulings in fiqh with their particular causes ('ilal juz'iyya).
4
Understand the hierarchy
Furu' depends on usul, which depends on kalam (theology). Thus usul is above fiqh but below kalam.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
5
Apply the hierarchy
When studying a fiqh ruling, one should trace its evidence through usul principles and ultimately to theological foundations.

کو حمد کہا جاتا ہے خواہ ذات باری تعالی کے متصف باوصاف کمالیہ کا اعتقاد ہو خواہ اس کا مقال باللسان ہو خواہ عمل بالا ر کان [؟] والاعضاء ہو تو بایں معنی محمد بھی مرکب من الاشياء الثلاثہ ہو گیا بمنزلہ شجرہ طیبہ اعتقاد شجر حمد کیلئے بمنزلہ اصل ثابت کے ہے اگر اعتقاد صحیح نہ ہوگا تو پھر جمہ بمنزلہ شجرہ خبیثہ کے ہو گا لا اصل لھا و بالعا من قرار اور عمل صالح شجر حمہ کیلئے بمنزلہ فرع اور شاخوں کے ہے اگر عمل صالح نہ ہوگا تو حمد کیلئے نما الی اللہ اور قبولیت عند اللہ نہ ہوگی اور حمد ایسے دوحہ اور منہ کی طرح ہوگا جس کی کوئی شاخ نہ ہو اور بینہ شجرہ ہوگا جس پر کوئی پھل نہ ہو کیونکہ عمل ہی وسیلہ ہے حصول جنت ورفع درجات کا جیسا کہ ارشاد خداوندی ہے والعمل الصالح پرفتہ۔ یرفع کی ضمیر کا مرجع عمل صالح ہے اور انمیر کا مرجع کلم طیب ہے و قال النبی منانے او الم یکن لہ عمل لم يقبل اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ حمد بلا عمل بے کار ہے تو مصنف نے اشارہ کیا کہ شجر حمد کا اصل ثابت ہے اور وہ اعتقاد راسخ الاسلامی ہے جو مبنی ہے تو حید وصفات کے علم پر اسی طرح شجر مہ کیلئے فرع ( شا تھیں) ہے جو نام الی اللہ اور مقبول عند اللہ ہے اور وہ عمل صالح ہے جو شریعت رہ کے موافق ہے جو منی علی علم الشرائع والاحکام ہے۔ واشار الى الاختصاص الخ غرض بيان نکات ! الیہ یصعد میں اللہ کی ظرف کی تقدیم میں نکتہ اختصاص وحصر ہے کیونکہ تقدیم ما حقه التاخير يفيد الحصر اور يصعد فعل مضارع ذکر کر کے اشارہ کیا صعود کے استمرار تجددی کی طرف۔
قوله على أن جعل تعليق للمحامد ببعض النعم اشارة الى عظم امر العلم الذي وقع التصنيف فيه ودلالة على جلالة قدره والشريعة تعم الفقه وغيره من الامور الثابتة بالادلة السمعية كمسئلة الروية و المعاد وكون الاجماع والقياس حجة وما أشبه ذلك و اصول الشريعة ادلتها الكلية و مبانى الاصول ما يبتنى هى عليه من علم الذات والصفات والنبوات و تمهيدها تسويتها و اصلاحها بكونها على وفق الحق و نهج الصواب و فروع الشريعة احكامها المفصلة المبينتة في علم الفقه و معانيها العلل الجزئية التفصيلية على كل مسئلة مسئلة ودقتها كونها غا مضته لطيفة لا يصل اليها كل احد بسهولة وجميع ذلك نعم تستوجب الحمد اذ بالشريعة نظام الدنيا وثواب العقبى وبدقة معاني الفقه رفعة درجات العلماء و نيلهم الثواب في دار الجزاء وفى هذا الكلام اشارة الى ان علم الاصول فوق الفقه ودون الكلام لان معرفة الاحكام الجزئية بادلتها التفصيلية موقوفة على معرفة احوال الادلة - الكلية من حيث انها توصل الى الاحكام الشرعية وهي موقوفة على معرفة البارى تعالى وصفاته وصدق المبلغ ودلالة معجزاته ونحو ذلك مما يشتمل عليه علم الكلام الباحث عن احوال الصانع
والنبوة والامامة والمعاد وما يتصل بذلك على قانون الاسلام .


قوله على أن جعل التعليق الخ غرض شارح ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے اشکال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ دنیا میں کروڑوں نعم ہیں اور محامد جمع مستغرق ہے جو مقتضی ہے کہ محامد تمام نعمتوں کے مقابلہ میں ہوں تو کیا وجہ ہے علامہ صدر نے مجاہد کو مختص کر دیا صرف علم شریعت کے ساتھ اور صرف اس کو محمود علیہ بنا دیا اس میں کیا نکتہ ہے ۔ جواب : شارح نے جواب دیا کہ علامہ صدر الشریعہ نعمتہ علم کومحمودعلیہ بنا کر اشارہ کر رہے ہیں عظمت و شرافت و جلالت علم کی طرف گو یا اصل نعمت یہی علم ہی ہے باقی نعمتین اس کے مقابلہ میں کالعدم ہیں۔ والشريعة تعم الفقه إلى قوله وفى هذا الكلام - غرض شارح متن کے الفاظ مخلفہ کی توضیح و تشریح الشریعہ ، سے شارح لفظ شریعت کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ شریعت سے فقط علم فقہ مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ فقہ وغیر فقہ دو نو مراد ہیں لیکن غیر فقہ سے وہ امور و مسائل مراد ہیں جو دلائل سمعیہ و دلائل نقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں جیسے مسئله رویت باری تعالی و مسئله معاد و مسئلہ کون الاجماع حجتہ وکون القياس حجتہ وہ امور جو دلائل سمعیہ سے ثابت نہیں بلکہ دلائل عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں وہ شریعت سے مراد نہیں ہیں۔ سوال! اولہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص کیوں کی گئی وہ امور جواد یہ عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں شریعت میں شامل کیوں نہیں ۔ جواب اتخصیص کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ شریعت متن میں اصول کا مضاف الیہ ہے اور ضابطہ یہ
Praise is said to be either belief in the essence of Allah Most High characterized by perfect attributes, or it is verbal expression, or it is action with the limbs. So in this sense, Muhammad is also composed of these three things, becoming like a good tree: belief is like a firm root for the tree of praise; if belief is not correct, then it becomes like a bad tree with no root, as stated. And righteous action for the tree of praise is like branches; if there is no righteous action, then praise will not ascend to Allah nor be accepted by Him, and praise will be like a tree with no branches, a barren tree bearing no fruit, because action is the means to attain Paradise and elevation of ranks, as the divine saying: 'and righteous action raises it.' The pronoun 'raises' refers to righteous action, and the pronoun 'it' refers to goodly word. And the Prophet said: 'Whoever has no action, it is not accepted.' Thus it is proven that praise without action is useless. So the author indicated that the tree of praise has a firm root, which is firm Islamic belief based on knowledge of tawhid and attributes, and for the tree of praise there is a branch that ascends to Allah and is accepted by Him, and that is righteous action in accordance with the Sharia, built upon knowledge of the laws and rulings. And he pointed to specificity... the purpose is explanation of points: In 'إليه يصعد', the advancement of the word 'إليه' indicates specificity and restriction because advancing what should be delayed indicates restriction, and mentioning the imperfect verb 'يصعد' indicates continuous renewal of ascent.

His statement: 'on that making praise attached to some blessings is an indication of the greatness of the science in which this authorship occurred and a proof of its high status, and Sharia encompasses fiqh and other matters established by revelatory proofs, like the issue of seeing Allah, resurrection, consensus and analogy being proofs, and the like. And the principles of Sharia are its universal proofs, and the foundations of the principles are what they are built upon from knowledge of the Essence, Attributes, prophethoods, and their establishment, rectification, being in accordance with truth and the path of correctness. And the branches of Sharia are its detailed rulings explained in the science of fiqh, and their meanings are the particular, detailed causes for each individual issue, and their subtlety being so deep and delicate that not everyone can easily reach them. And all of that are blessings that necessitate praise, because through Sharia is the order of the world and the reward of the Hereafter, and through the subtlety of the meanings of fiqh is the elevation of the ranks of scholars and their attainment of reward in the abode of recompense. And in this speech is an indication that the science of usul is above fiqh and below kalam, because the knowledge of particular rulings with their detailed proofs depends on knowing the conditions of the universal proofs in terms of how they lead to legal rulings, and that depends on knowing the Creator Most High, His attributes, the truthfulness of the messenger, the indication of his miracles, and the like, which is included in the science of kalam, which investigates the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, resurrection, and what is connected to that according to the law of Islam.'

His statement: 'on that making the attachment' etc. - The purpose of the commentator is to answer an objection. The objection is: There are millions of blessings in the world, and 'praise' is a collective inclusive term requiring that praise be in return for all blessings. So why did the author (Sadr al-Shariah) specifically limit praise to the science of Sharia and make that alone the object of praise? What is the point? The answer: The commentator replied that Sadr al-Shariah, by making the blessing of knowledge the object of praise, is indicating the greatness, honor, and high status of knowledge, as if the real blessing is this knowledge; other blessings are virtually non-existent in comparison. 'And Sharia encompasses fiqh... up to the end of this speech' - the purpose of the commentator is to explain and clarify the various words of the text. Regarding 'Sharia', the commentator clarifies that Sharia does not only mean the science of fiqh, but rather both fiqh and non-fiqh are meant. However, by non-fiqh are meant those matters and issues that are established by revelatory proofs (sam'i proof) like the issues of seeing Allah, resurrection, consensus being a proof, analogy being a proof. Matters that are established by rational proofs are not intended by Sharia. Question: Why specify revelatory proofs? Why are matters established by rational proofs not included in Sharia? Answer: The reason for the specification is that the word 'Sharia' in the text is the mudaf ilayh of 'usul', and the rule is...
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening lines of Al-Tawdih, explaining the nature of praise (hamd) and its relation to belief and action, and then discussing the scope of Sharia and the hierarchy of Islamic sciences. The commentator first explains that true praise of Allah involves belief, speech, and action, and uses the Quranic verse 'To Him ascends goodly speech, and righteous action raises it' to show that praise without righteous deeds is like a tree without fruit. This guards against the misunderstanding that mere verbal or intellectual acknowledgment is sufficient. Then the passage addresses why the author (Sadr al-Shariah) attached praise specifically to the science of Sharia, explaining that this highlights the supreme value of sacred knowledge—without which worldly and otherworldly order cannot be achieved. The commentator then clarifies that 'Sharia' in this context includes not only fiqh (jurisprudence) but also other matters established by revelatory proofs (sam'i), such as the beatific vision (ru'ya), resurrection (ma'ad), and the authority of consensus and analogy. This excludes matters known purely by reason (aqli). The passage further arranges the sciences hierarchically: usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence) is above fiqh because it provides the universal proofs from which fiqh derives, but it is below kalam (theology) because kalam deals with the foundational beliefs about God, prophethood, and the afterlife upon which usul depends. This hierarchy is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi usul tradition, which positions kalam as a prerequisite for usul al-fiqh, unlike some other approaches. The commentator also answers a potential objection: why restrict praise to the science of Sharia when there are countless blessings? The answer is that the blessing of knowledge is the greatest and most fundamental, so it is the proper focus of praise. Throughout, the commentary underscores the centrality of sacred knowledge and the interconnectedness of belief, action, and the various Islamic disciplines.

Key Terms
شريعة (Shari'a): Sharia encompasses fiqh and other matters established by revelatory proofs (sam'i), such as the beatific vision, resurrection, consensus, and analogy.
اصول الشريعة (Usul al-Sharia): The universal proofs (adilla kulliya) that lead to legal rulings.
فروع الشريعة (Furu' al-Sharia): The detailed rulings explained in fiqh, along with their particular causes ('ilal juz'iyya).
علم الكلام ('Ilm al-Kalam): Theology that investigates the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, resurrection, and related matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rank of usul al-fiqh relative to fiqh and kalam?
A) It is above both fiqh and kalam.
B) It is below fiqh but above kalam.
C) It is above fiqh but below kalam.
D) It is equal to fiqh and independent of kalam.

Key Takeaway
Sharia encompasses fiqh and other revelatory matters; the hierarchy of sciences is kalam > usul al-fiqh > fiqh.

Method of Learning
intermediate

The Blessing of Knowledge and the Definition of Sharīʿah
Commentator answers an objection and defines Shari'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why knowledge of Sharīʿah is the greatest blessing and define Sharīʿah as including both fiqh and non-fiqh matters proven by samʿī proofs, distinguishing it from matters proven by reason alone.

Core Idea
Sharīʿah is broader than fiqh; it includes creedal matters if proven by transmitted proofs, not by reason.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih addresses a fundamental question: why does the author praise only the blessing of knowledge? The answer reveals the preeminence of knowledge, and then the commentator defines Sharīʿah with precision, clarifying its scope and its relationship to the sources of law (usūl). Understanding this definition is essential for grasping the subject matter of usūl al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector asks: why does Sadr al-Shari'ah associate all praises solely with knowledge of Shari'ah, when there are countless blessings? Read the commentator's framing.
The objection arises from the comprehensive plural 'mahamid'.
2
Understand the answer
The commentator explains that knowledge is the greatest blessing; all other blessings are insignificant in comparison. This establishes the honor of this science.
3
Define Shari'ah technically
Shari'ah is defined as encompassing both fiqh and non-fiqh matters proven by sam'i (transmitted) proofs, such as the Beatific Vision, Resurrection, and the authority of consensus and analogy.
Non-fiqh matters are creedal issues established by transmitted evidence.
4
Analyze why sam'i proofs are specified
The phrase 'usul al-shari'ah' uses idafah (construct), which implies that Shari'ah is that which is derived from the usul (the sam'i sources). Matters proven by reason alone are not derived from these sources; rather, the sources themselves depend on rational proofs. Hence, they are excluded.
Rational proofs validate the usul, not vice versa.
5
Summarize the scope of Shari'ah
Conclude that Shari'ah in this context includes only those matters that are directly derived from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. This sets the boundaries for usul al-fiqh.

مسک الملیح شرح التوضيح والتلويح
ترجمہ ! علی ان جعل یہ معلق کرتا ہے محامد کو بعض نعمتوں کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنے کے لئے علم کے امر کے عظیم ہونے کی طرف جسمیں تصنیف واقع ہوئی ہے اور دلالت کرنے کے لئے اسکی جلالت قدر پر اور شریعت عام ہے فقہ اور غیر فقہ کو ان امور سے جو ثابت ہیں ادلہ سمعیہ کے ساتھ مثل مسئلہ رویت کے اور معاد اور اجماع کے حجت ہونے کے اور قیاس کے حجت ہونے کے اور اس کے مشابہ اور اصول شریعت وہ ادلہ کلیہ ہیں اور مبانی اصول وہ ہیں جس پر وہ اصول بنی ہوں علم ذات اور صفات اور نبوات سے اور ان کی تمہیدان کو برابر کرنا اور ان کی اصلاح کرنا حق کے موافق اور صواب کے طریق اور فروع شریعت اس شریعت کے احکام ہیں تفصیلی جو بیان کئے گئے ہیں علم الفقہ میں۔ اور ان کے معانی وہ عمل جزئیہ تفصلیہ ہیں پر مسئلہ پر اور ان معانی کا دقیق ہونا ان کا گہرا اور باریک ہوتا ہے کہ ان تک ہر ایک سہولت کیساتھ نہیں پہنچ سکتا اور یہ تمام نعمتیں ہیں جو شکر وحد کو واجب کرتی ہیں اس لئے کہ شریعت کے ساتھ ہی دنیا کا نظام ہے اور آخرت کا ثواب ہے اور فقہ کے معانی کے دقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے علماء کے درجات کی بلندی ہے اور ثواب کو حاصل کرتا ہے دار الجزاء میں اور اس کلام میں اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ علم اصول فقہ فقہ سے اوپر اور کلام سے کم ہے اس لئے کہ احکام جزئیہ کی معرفت اولہ تفصیلیہ کے ساتھ موقوف ہے ادلہ کلیہ کے احوال کی معرفت پر اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ پہنچا دیں احکام شرعیہ تک اور وہ موقوف ہے باری تعالیٰ اور اسکی صفات کی معرفت پر اور صدق مبلغ اور اسکے معجزات کی دلالت پر اور اسکی مثل پر ان چیزوں میں سے جن پر علم کلام مشتمل ہے جو بحث کرنے والا ہے صانع نبوت امامت معاد کے احوال سے اور ان چیزوں سے جو ان کیساتھ متصل ہو قانون اسلام کے مطابق۔
قوله على أن جعل التعليق الخ غرض شارح ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے اشکال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ دنیا میں کروڑوں نعم ہیں اور محامد جمع مستغرق ہے جو مقتضی ہے کہ محامد تمام نعمتوں کے مقابلہ میں ہوں تو کیا وجہ ہے علامہ صدر نے مجاہد کو مختص کر دیا صرف علم شریعت کے ساتھ اور صرف اس کو محمود علیہ بنا دیا اس میں کیا نکتہ ہے ۔ جواب : شارح نے جواب دیا کہ علامہ صدر الشریعہ نعمتہ علم کومحمودعلیہ بنا کر اشارہ کر رہے ہیں عظمت و شرافت و جلالت علم کی طرف گو یا اصل نعمت یہی علم ہی ہے باقی نعمتین اس کے مقابلہ میں کالعدم ہیں۔ والشريعة تعم الفقه إلى قوله وفى هذا الكلام - غرض شارح متن کے الفاظ مخلفہ کی توضیح و تشریح الشریعہ ، سے شارح لفظ شریعت کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ شریعت سے فقط علم فقہ مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ فقہ وغیر فقہ دو نو مراد ہیں لیکن غیر فقہ سے وہ امور و مسائل مراد ہیں جو دلائل سمعیہ و دلائل نقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں جیسے مسئله رویت باری تعالی و مسئله معاد و مسئلہ کون الاجماع حجتہ وکون القياس حجتہ وہ امور جو دلائل سمعیہ سے ثابت نہیں بلکہ دلائل عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں وہ شریعت سے مراد نہیں ہیں۔ سوال! اولہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص کیوں کی گئی وہ امور جواد یہ عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں شریعت میں شامل کیوں نہیں ۔ جواب اتخصیص کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ شریعت متن میں اصول کا مضاف الیہ ہے اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اضافت تخصیص کا فائدہ دیتی ہے اب اصول شریعت کا معنی ہوگا وہ شریعت جو مستفاد و حاصل ہے اصول سے اور اصول سے مراد کتاب وسنت وغیرہ ہیں اور یہی ادلہ سمعیہ ہیں تو ادلہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص اس لیے کی گئی تا کہ وہ امور جو ثابت بالعقلیہ ہیں خارج ہو جائیں کیونکہ وہ مستفاد من الاصول نہیں بلکہ خود اصول ان سے مستفاد ہیں جیسے علم ذات باری تعالی وصفاتہ وعلم صدق المبلغ وغیرہ جن سے علم الکلام میں بحث کی جاتی ہے اصول فقہ شریعت ( کتاب وسنہ وغیرہ) ان پر موقوف ہیں ولا عکسہ نہ کہ وہ ان پر موقوف ہیں) الاصولی سے مراد ادلہ کلیہ ( کتاب سنت اجماع و قیاس) ہیں۔ و مبانی الاصول سے عقائد مراد ہیں جن پر اصول بنی ہیں مثلا ذات باری وصفات باری کا علم و نبوت کا علم معجزات کا علم وغیرہ وتمهيدها تسویتھا سے تمھید کا معنی کیا کسی شئی کا درست کرنا اس کی اصلاح کرنا تو مبانی و عقائد کا تسو یہ واصلاح کا مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ وہ عقائد موافق حق اور علی نسج الصواب ہوں ایسے عقائد نہ ہوں جو مخالف حق ہوں جیسے فلاسفہ کا عقیدہ فاسدہ ہے کہ ذات باری تعالی میں تغار حقیقی بھی نہیں ہے تغایر اعتباری بھی نہیں اسی بناء پر انہوں نے کہا کہ اللہ تعالی نے صرف عقل اول کو پیدا کیا اس نے ثانی کو اور اس نے ثالث الخ ، کیونکہ اگر تمام چیزوں کا خالق ذات باری تعالی کو تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو ذات باری تعالی میں تغایر اعتباری لازم آئے گا کیونکہ ذات اللہ بایں حیثیت کہ خالق عمرو ہے مغایر ہے اس ذات اللہ کے جو خالق بکر ہے خلاصہ اینکہ یہ بھی تو حید باری تعالی کا اثبات ہے لیکن لاعلی طریق الحق و شبح الصواب بل على طريق الغلط والفساد وفروع الشريعة سے احکام فقہیہ مفصلہ مبینہ فی علم الفقہ مراد ہیں۔ المعانی معانی فروغ سے وہ عمل جزئیہ مراد ہیں جو ہر مسئلہ فقہیہ پر قائم کی جاتی ہیں جیسے ھدایہ میں ہر مسئلہ پر دلیل و علت پیش کی جاتی ہے۔ تنبیہ شارح ! کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ معنی سے علت مراد ہے اور یہ دونوں مرادف ہیں اور یہ اصطلاح فقہاء ہے کہ وہ بجائے لفظ علت کے معنی کا لفظ بولتے ہیں وجہ احتراز یہ بیان کی گئی ہے کہ لفظ علت اہل فلاسفہ کے ہاں کثیر الاستعمال تھا اور فقہاء اصطلاحات فلسفیہ سے احتراز کرتے تھے اسی بناء پر لفظ معنی کو بجائے لفظ علت استعمال کرتے ہیں کما قال صاحب الحدایہ فصل فی المعانى الموجبة للوضوء أى فى الاسباب والعلل الخ- ودقتها كونها دقيقة کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے شارج نے فرمایا کہ وقت معانی سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ عمل کافی گہرے اور لطیف و مشکل ہیں ہر شخص ان تک رسائی با السہولت نہیں کرسکتا بلکہ مجتہد سعی بسیار کے بعد ان کا استخراج کرتا ہے۔ وجميع ذلک سے تخصیص محمود علیہ کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تمام اشیا تم من جانب اللہ ہیں شریعت بایں وجہ نعمت ہے کہ اسی کے ذریعہ سے نظام دنیا کا قیام وبقاء ہے اور اس پر ثواب عقبی کا مدار ہے۔ نیز علل کا دقیق ہونا بھی نعمت اللہ ہے کیونکہ مجتہدین ان کے استخراج و استنباط میں صعوبات و مشکلات کا سامنا کریں گے جس کے طفیل اللہ تعالی ان کے درجات کو رفعت و بلندی عطاء فرمائیں گے اور دار الجزاء میں ثواب و بدلہ عطاء فرمائیں گے۔ فائدہ ! اصول الشریعہ میں اضافت اصول
Misk al-Malih Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Translation: On that he suspends praises with some blessings to indicate the greatness of the matter of knowledge in which authorship occurred and to indicate its exalted status. And Shari'ah is general, covering fiqh and non-fiqh among matters that are proven by sam'i proofs, like the issue of vision (of Allah), and the return, and that consensus is a proof, and that analogy is a proof, and similar. And usul al-shari'ah are the general proofs. And the foundations of the usul are those upon which those usul are built: knowledge of essence, attributes, and prophethoods. And their preparation: making them straight and correcting them in accordance with truth and the path of correctness. And the branches of shari'ah are the detailed rulings of this shari'ah that are explained in the science of fiqh. And their meanings (ma'ani) are the detailed particular acts (that are established) upon each issue. And the precision of these meanings is that they are deep and subtle, such that not everyone can reach them easily. And all these are blessings that necessitate gratitude to the One. Because the system of this world and the reward of the Hereafter are dependent upon shari'ah. And due to the precision of the meanings of fiqh, the ranks of scholars are elevated and they attain reward in the abode of recompense. And in this speech there is an indication that the science of usul al-fiqh is above fiqh and below kalam. Because knowledge of particular rulings in their detailed form depends on knowledge of the states of the general proofs insofar as they lead to shar'i rulings. And that depends on knowledge of Allah Most High and His attributes, and the truthfulness of the conveyer, and the indication of his miracles, and similar matters that the science of kalam deals with, which discusses the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, and the return, and matters connected to them according to the law of Islam. His statement: 'On that he suspends the commentary etc.' The commentator's purpose is to answer an objection. The objection is that there are millions of blessings in the world, and 'mahamid' is a comprehensive plural which requires that praises be in exchange for all blessings. So why did the author (Sadr al-Shari'ah) specifically attribute 'mahamid' only to the knowledge of shari'ah and make it the praised one? What is the point? Answer: The commentator responded that Sadr al-Shari'ah made the blessing of knowledge the object of praise to indicate the greatness, honor, and exaltedness of knowledge. As if the real blessing is this knowledge, and other blessings are as nothing in comparison. And 'al-Shari'ah encompasses fiqh... to his statement 'and in this speech'. The commentator's purpose is to explain the different words of the matn. From 'al-Shari'ah', the commentator clarifies the word shari'ah, saying that by shari'ah, not only the science of fiqh is meant, but both fiqh and non-fiqh are meant. However, by non-fiqh, those matters and issues are meant that are proven by sam'i and naqli proofs, such as the issue of seeing Allah, the issue of the return, the issue that consensus is a proof, and that analogy is a proof. Those matters that are not proven by sam'i proofs but by rational proofs are not meant by shari'ah. Question: Why was the specification made for sam'i proofs? Why are matters proven by rational proofs not included in shari'ah? Answer: The reason for specification is that the word shari'ah in the text is the mudaf ilayhi of usul, and the rule is that idafah gives specification. So now the meaning of usul al-shari'ah is: that shari'ah which is derived and obtained from the usul. And by usul, the Book and Sunnah etc. are meant, and these are the sam'i proofs. So sam'i proofs were specified so that matters proven by rational proofs are excluded, because they are not derived from the usul; rather, the usul themselves are derived from them, like knowledge of the essence of Allah Most High and His attributes, and knowledge of the truthfulness of the conveyer, etc., which are discussed in kalam. The usul (i.e., the Book and Sunnah) depend on them, not the other way around. (By al-usul, the general proofs are meant: Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy.) And by mabani al-usul, the beliefs are meant upon which the usul are built, e.g., knowledge of the essence of Allah, His attributes, knowledge of prophethood, knowledge of miracles, etc. And 'tamhiduha' (their preparation) means to make something correct, to rectify it. So the purpose of preparing and correcting the foundations and beliefs is that those beliefs should be in accordance with truth and on the path of correctness, not beliefs that oppose truth, like the corrupt belief of the philosophers that there is no real distinction in the essence of Allah, nor even a conceptual distinction. Based on this, they said that Allah created only the first intellect, which created the second, and so on. Because if all things were acknowledged to be created by Allah's essence, then a conceptual distinction in Allah's essence would be necessary, because the essence of Allah in terms of being the creator of 'Amr is distinct from the essence that is the creator of Bakr. In summary, this is also an affirmation of the oneness of Allah, but not on the truthful way and the correct path; rather, on the path of error and corruption. And by 'furu' al-shari'ah', the detailed fiqh rulings explained in the science of fiqh are meant. And 'al-ma'ani' (the meanings) from 'ma'ani al-furu' are the particular causes (illal) that are established upon each fiqh issue, like in al-Hidayah where for every issue a proof and cause are presented. Note: From the commentator's expression, it becomes clear that by 'ma'na' (meaning) is intended 'illah (cause), and the two are synonymous. And this is the terminology of the fuqaha: they use the word 'ma'na' instead of 'illah. The reason for avoidance is that the word 'illah was frequently used by the philosophers, and the fuqaha avoided philosophical terminology. Therefore, they used the word 'ma'na' in place of 'illah, as the author of al-Hidayah said: 'Chapter on the meanings that necessitate wudu', i.e., the causes and reasons, etc.' And their precision: that they are subtle. Explaining that, the commentator said that by 'precision of the meanings' it is meant that these causes are deep, subtle, and difficult; not everyone can easily access them; rather, the mujtahid extracts them after great effort. And 'all of that' - clarifying the specification of the praised one, the commentator says that all these things are from Allah. Shari'ah is a blessing because through it the system of this world is established and sustained, and upon it depends the reward of the Hereafter. Also, the precision of the causes is a blessing of Allah, because the mujtahids will face hardships and difficulties in extracting and deriving them, through which Allah will elevate their ranks and grant them reward in the abode of recompense. Benefit: In usul al-shari'ah, the idafah of usul...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the opening lines of Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah. The commentator begins by translating the matn, then answers a potential objection: why does the author specifically associate 'praises' with the blessing of knowledge of Shari'ah, when there are countless blessings? The answer is that knowledge is the greatest blessing; all others are insignificant in comparison. Next, the commentator defines 'Shari'ah' broadly: it includes both fiqh (positive law) and non-fiqh matters (like beliefs about the Beatific Vision, Resurrection, and the authority of consensus and analogy) that are proven by transmitted (sam'i) proofs. Matters proven solely by rational proofs, such as the existence of God or the truthfulness of prophets, are not part of Shari'ah in this technical sense. Why? Because the phrase 'usul al-shari'ah' in the matn uses idafah (construct state), which implies specification: Shari'ah is that which is derived from the usul (the primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, etc.), and those sources are sam'i. Rational matters are not derived from them; rather, the usul themselves depend on rational proofs for their validation (e.g., proving the existence and attributes of God, the truth of prophethood). Hence, Shari'ah in this context is restricted to sam'i matters. The commentator then defines the key terms of the science: 'al-usul' are the general proofs (kulliyat: Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogy); 'mabani al-usul' (foundations of the usul) are the creedal beliefs (such as knowledge of God's essence and attributes, prophethood, miracles) upon which the validity of the usul rests; 'furu' al-shari'ah' are the detailed fiqh rulings; and 'ma'ani' (meanings) are the specific causes (illal) that ground each fiqh ruling—the term 'ma'na' is used by Hanafi fuqaha instead of 'illah to avoid philosophical terminology, as exemplified by the Hidayah's chapter on 'meanings that necessitate wudu'. The commentator emphasizes the precision (diqqa) of these causes: they are deep and subtle, accessible only to mujtahids through strenuous effort. Finally, he reiterates that all these—Shari'ah, its precision, the effort of scholars—are divine blessings that necessitate gratitude, for through them worldly order and otherworldly reward are achieved. This passage thus establishes the epistemological hierarchy: knowledge of usul al-fiqh sits between fiqh (which it serves) and kalam (which provides its foundational premises).

Key Terms
الشريعة (al-shari'ah): The divine law that includes both fiqh and non-fiqh matters proven by transmitted (sam'i) proofs.
أصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The general proofs (kulliyat) from which Shari'ah is derived: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator specify that Shari'ah includes only matters proven by sam'i proofs and not those proven by rational proofs alone?
A) Because rational proofs are weaker than sam'i proofs.
B) Because Shari'ah, in the context of 'usul al-shari'ah', refers to that which is derived from the usul (Book and Sunnah), and those usul are sam'i; rational proofs are not derived from them but rather are used to validate the usul themselves.
C) Because the author of the matn only wanted to discuss fiqh rulings.
D) Because the commentator considered rational proofs to be invalid in Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Shari'ah is the greatest blessing, and Shari'ah in usul al-fiqh includes only matters proven by transmitted proofs from the usul, excluding purely rational matters.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
Key Terms in Usul al-Fiqh: Usul, Mabani, Furu', and Ma'ani
Commentator defines the key terms and hierarchy of usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define usul al-shari'ah, mabani al-usul, furu' al-shari'ah, and ma'ani (as 'illah), and explain the hierarchy that places usul al-fiqh between fiqh and kalam.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is an intermediate discipline: it provides the tools to derive fiqh from sources, while depending on kalam for foundational beliefs.

After defining Shari'ah, the commentator clarifies the technical vocabulary of usul al-fiqh. Understanding terms like usul, mabani, furu', and ma'ani is essential for navigating any classical usul text. This passage also reveals the epistemological hierarchy in which usul al-fiqh sits between the detailed rulings of fiqh and the theological foundations of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Define usul al-shari'ah
The commentator explains that 'al-usul' are the general proofs (kulliyat) from which Shari'ah is derived: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. These are the sources of law.
They are called 'usul' because they are the foundations upon which fiqh rulings are built.
2
Understand mabani al-usul
These are the foundational beliefs upon which the usul rest: knowledge of God's existence, attributes, prophethood, miracles, etc. They are the subject of kalam.
Mabani are not part of usul al-fiqh but are prerequisites.
3
Define furu' al-shari'ah
These are the detailed fiqh rulings (positive law) that are the branches of Shari'ah, as found in fiqh books.
Furu' are the output of applying usul to specific cases.
4
Define ma'ani (meanings)
The commentator clarifies that 'ma'na' in this context means the cause ('illah) for a ruling. Fuqaha use 'ma'na' instead of 'illah to avoid philosophical terminology. These causes are precise and subtle, accessible only to mujtahids through effort.
Example: in the Hidayah, 'chapter on the meanings that necessitate wudu' refers to the causes of wudu.
5
Recognize the hierarchy
The passage indicates that usul al-fiqh is above fiqh (because it provides the method) and below kalam (because it depends on theological premises). This hierarchy explains the prerequisites for studying usul.
One must first know kalam (to establish the sources), then usul (to derive rulings), then fiqh (the rulings themselves).
