ترجمہ ! علی ان جعل یہ معلق کرتا ہے محامد کو بعض نعمتوں کے ساتھ اشارہ کرنے کے لئے علم کے امر کے عظیم ہونے کی طرف جسمیں تصنیف واقع ہوئی ہے اور دلالت کرنے کے لئے اسکی جلالت قدر پر اور شریعت عام ہے فقہ اور غیر فقہ کو ان امور سے جو ثابت ہیں ادلہ سمعیہ کے ساتھ مثل مسئلہ رویت کے اور معاد اور اجماع کے حجت ہونے کے اور قیاس کے حجت ہونے کے اور اس کے مشابہ اور اصول شریعت وہ ادلہ کلیہ ہیں اور مبانی اصول وہ ہیں جس پر وہ اصول بنی ہوں علم ذات اور صفات اور نبوات سے اور ان کی تمہیدان کو برابر کرنا اور ان کی اصلاح کرنا حق کے موافق اور صواب کے طریق اور فروع شریعت اس شریعت کے احکام ہیں تفصیلی جو بیان کئے گئے ہیں علم الفقہ میں۔ اور ان کے معانی وہ عمل جزئیہ تفصلیہ ہیں پر مسئلہ پر اور ان معانی کا دقیق ہونا ان کا گہرا اور باریک ہوتا ہے کہ ان تک ہر ایک سہولت کیساتھ نہیں پہنچ سکتا اور یہ تمام نعمتیں ہیں جو شکر وحد کو واجب کرتی ہیں اس لئے کہ شریعت کے ساتھ ہی دنیا کا نظام ہے اور آخرت کا ثواب ہے اور فقہ کے معانی کے دقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے علماء کے درجات کی بلندی ہے اور ثواب کو حاصل کرتا ہے دار الجزاء میں اور اس کلام میں اشارہ ہے اس بات کی طرف کہ علم اصول فقہ فقہ سے اوپر اور کلام سے کم ہے اس لئے کہ احکام جزئیہ کی معرفت اولہ تفصیلیہ کے ساتھ موقوف ہے ادلہ کلیہ کے احوال کی معرفت پر اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ پہنچا دیں احکام شرعیہ تک اور وہ موقوف ہے باری تعالیٰ اور اسکی صفات کی معرفت پر اور صدق مبلغ اور اسکے معجزات کی دلالت پر اور اسکی مثل پر ان چیزوں میں سے جن پر علم کلام مشتمل ہے جو بحث کرنے والا ہے صانع نبوت امامت معاد کے احوال سے اور ان چیزوں سے جو ان کیساتھ متصل ہو قانون اسلام کے مطابق۔
قوله على أن جعل التعليق الخ غرض شارح ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے اشکال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ دنیا میں کروڑوں نعم ہیں اور محامد جمع مستغرق ہے جو مقتضی ہے کہ محامد تمام نعمتوں کے مقابلہ میں ہوں تو کیا وجہ ہے علامہ صدر نے مجاہد کو مختص کر دیا صرف علم شریعت کے ساتھ اور صرف اس کو محمود علیہ بنا دیا اس میں کیا نکتہ ہے ۔ جواب : شارح نے جواب دیا کہ علامہ صدر الشریعہ نعمتہ علم کومحمودعلیہ بنا کر اشارہ کر رہے ہیں عظمت و شرافت و جلالت علم کی طرف گو یا اصل نعمت یہی علم ہی ہے باقی نعمتین اس کے مقابلہ میں کالعدم ہیں۔ والشريعة تعم الفقه إلى قوله وفى هذا الكلام - غرض شارح متن کے الفاظ مخلفہ کی توضیح و تشریح الشریعہ ، سے شارح لفظ شریعت کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ شریعت سے فقط علم فقہ مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ فقہ وغیر فقہ دو نو مراد ہیں لیکن غیر فقہ سے وہ امور و مسائل مراد ہیں جو دلائل سمعیہ و دلائل نقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں جیسے مسئله رویت باری تعالی و مسئله معاد و مسئلہ کون الاجماع حجتہ وکون القياس حجتہ وہ امور جو دلائل سمعیہ سے ثابت نہیں بلکہ دلائل عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں وہ شریعت سے مراد نہیں ہیں۔ سوال! اولہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص کیوں کی گئی وہ امور جواد یہ عقلیہ سے ثابت ہیں شریعت میں شامل کیوں نہیں ۔ جواب اتخصیص کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ شریعت متن میں اصول کا مضاف الیہ ہے اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ اضافت تخصیص کا فائدہ دیتی ہے اب اصول شریعت کا معنی ہوگا وہ شریعت جو مستفاد و حاصل ہے اصول سے اور اصول سے مراد کتاب وسنت وغیرہ ہیں اور یہی ادلہ سمعیہ ہیں تو ادلہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص اس لیے کی گئی تا کہ وہ امور جو ثابت بالعقلیہ ہیں خارج ہو جائیں کیونکہ وہ مستفاد من الاصول نہیں بلکہ خود اصول ان سے مستفاد ہیں جیسے علم ذات باری تعالی وصفاتہ وعلم صدق المبلغ وغیرہ جن سے علم الکلام میں بحث کی جاتی ہے اصول فقہ شریعت ( کتاب وسنہ وغیرہ) ان پر موقوف ہیں ولا عکسہ نہ کہ وہ ان پر موقوف ہیں) الاصولی سے مراد ادلہ کلیہ ( کتاب سنت اجماع و قیاس) ہیں۔ و مبانی الاصول سے عقائد مراد ہیں جن پر اصول بنی ہیں مثلا ذات باری وصفات باری کا علم و نبوت کا علم معجزات کا علم وغیرہ وتمهيدها تسویتھا سے تمھید کا معنی کیا کسی شئی کا درست کرنا اس کی اصلاح کرنا تو مبانی و عقائد کا تسو یہ واصلاح کا مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ وہ عقائد موافق حق اور علی نسج الصواب ہوں ایسے عقائد نہ ہوں جو مخالف حق ہوں جیسے فلاسفہ کا عقیدہ فاسدہ ہے کہ ذات باری تعالی میں تغار حقیقی بھی نہیں ہے تغایر اعتباری بھی نہیں اسی بناء پر انہوں نے کہا کہ اللہ تعالی نے صرف عقل اول کو پیدا کیا اس نے ثانی کو اور اس نے ثالث الخ ، کیونکہ اگر تمام چیزوں کا خالق ذات باری تعالی کو تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو ذات باری تعالی میں تغایر اعتباری لازم آئے گا کیونکہ ذات اللہ بایں حیثیت کہ خالق عمرو ہے مغایر ہے اس ذات اللہ کے جو خالق بکر ہے خلاصہ اینکہ یہ بھی تو حید باری تعالی کا اثبات ہے لیکن لاعلی طریق الحق و شبح الصواب بل على طريق الغلط والفساد وفروع الشريعة سے احکام فقہیہ مفصلہ مبینہ فی علم الفقہ مراد ہیں۔ المعانی معانی فروغ سے وہ عمل جزئیہ مراد ہیں جو ہر مسئلہ فقہیہ پر قائم کی جاتی ہیں جیسے ھدایہ میں ہر مسئلہ پر دلیل و علت پیش کی جاتی ہے۔ تنبیہ شارح ! کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ معنی سے علت مراد ہے اور یہ دونوں مرادف ہیں اور یہ اصطلاح فقہاء ہے کہ وہ بجائے لفظ علت کے معنی کا لفظ بولتے ہیں وجہ احتراز یہ بیان کی گئی ہے کہ لفظ علت اہل فلاسفہ کے ہاں کثیر الاستعمال تھا اور فقہاء اصطلاحات فلسفیہ سے احتراز کرتے تھے اسی بناء پر لفظ معنی کو بجائے لفظ علت استعمال کرتے ہیں کما قال صاحب الحدایہ فصل فی المعانى الموجبة للوضوء أى فى الاسباب والعلل الخ- ودقتها كونها دقيقة کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے شارج نے فرمایا کہ وقت معانی سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ عمل کافی گہرے اور لطیف و مشکل ہیں ہر شخص ان تک رسائی با السہولت نہیں کرسکتا بلکہ مجتہد سعی بسیار کے بعد ان کا استخراج کرتا ہے۔ وجميع ذلک سے تخصیص محمود علیہ کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تمام اشیا تم من جانب اللہ ہیں شریعت بایں وجہ نعمت ہے کہ اسی کے ذریعہ سے نظام دنیا کا قیام وبقاء ہے اور اس پر ثواب عقبی کا مدار ہے۔ نیز علل کا دقیق ہونا بھی نعمت اللہ ہے کیونکہ مجتہدین ان کے استخراج و استنباط میں صعوبات و مشکلات کا سامنا کریں گے جس کے طفیل اللہ تعالی ان کے درجات کو رفعت و بلندی عطاء فرمائیں گے اور دار الجزاء میں ثواب و بدلہ عطاء فرمائیں گے۔ فائدہ ! اصول الشریعہ میں اضافت اصول
Misk al-Malih Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Translation: On that he suspends praises with some blessings to indicate the greatness of the matter of knowledge in which authorship occurred and to indicate its exalted status. And Shari'ah is general, covering fiqh and non-fiqh among matters that are proven by sam'i proofs, like the issue of vision (of Allah), and the return, and that consensus is a proof, and that analogy is a proof, and similar. And usul al-shari'ah are the general proofs. And the foundations of the usul are those upon which those usul are built: knowledge of essence, attributes, and prophethoods. And their preparation: making them straight and correcting them in accordance with truth and the path of correctness. And the branches of shari'ah are the detailed rulings of this shari'ah that are explained in the science of fiqh. And their meanings (ma'ani) are the detailed particular acts (that are established) upon each issue. And the precision of these meanings is that they are deep and subtle, such that not everyone can reach them easily. And all these are blessings that necessitate gratitude to the One. Because the system of this world and the reward of the Hereafter are dependent upon shari'ah. And due to the precision of the meanings of fiqh, the ranks of scholars are elevated and they attain reward in the abode of recompense. And in this speech there is an indication that the science of usul al-fiqh is above fiqh and below kalam. Because knowledge of particular rulings in their detailed form depends on knowledge of the states of the general proofs insofar as they lead to shar'i rulings. And that depends on knowledge of Allah Most High and His attributes, and the truthfulness of the conveyer, and the indication of his miracles, and similar matters that the science of kalam deals with, which discusses the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, and the return, and matters connected to them according to the law of Islam. His statement: 'On that he suspends the commentary etc.' The commentator's purpose is to answer an objection. The objection is that there are millions of blessings in the world, and 'mahamid' is a comprehensive plural which requires that praises be in exchange for all blessings. So why did the author (Sadr al-Shari'ah) specifically attribute 'mahamid' only to the knowledge of shari'ah and make it the praised one? What is the point? Answer: The commentator responded that Sadr al-Shari'ah made the blessing of knowledge the object of praise to indicate the greatness, honor, and exaltedness of knowledge. As if the real blessing is this knowledge, and other blessings are as nothing in comparison. And 'al-Shari'ah encompasses fiqh... to his statement 'and in this speech'. The commentator's purpose is to explain the different words of the matn. From 'al-Shari'ah', the commentator clarifies the word shari'ah, saying that by shari'ah, not only the science of fiqh is meant, but both fiqh and non-fiqh are meant. However, by non-fiqh, those matters and issues are meant that are proven by sam'i and naqli proofs, such as the issue of seeing Allah, the issue of the return, the issue that consensus is a proof, and that analogy is a proof. Those matters that are not proven by sam'i proofs but by rational proofs are not meant by shari'ah. Question: Why was the specification made for sam'i proofs? Why are matters proven by rational proofs not included in shari'ah? Answer: The reason for specification is that the word shari'ah in the text is the mudaf ilayhi of usul, and the rule is that idafah gives specification. So now the meaning of usul al-shari'ah is: that shari'ah which is derived and obtained from the usul. And by usul, the Book and Sunnah etc. are meant, and these are the sam'i proofs. So sam'i proofs were specified so that matters proven by rational proofs are excluded, because they are not derived from the usul; rather, the usul themselves are derived from them, like knowledge of the essence of Allah Most High and His attributes, and knowledge of the truthfulness of the conveyer, etc., which are discussed in kalam. The usul (i.e., the Book and Sunnah) depend on them, not the other way around. (By al-usul, the general proofs are meant: Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy.) And by mabani al-usul, the beliefs are meant upon which the usul are built, e.g., knowledge of the essence of Allah, His attributes, knowledge of prophethood, knowledge of miracles, etc. And 'tamhiduha' (their preparation) means to make something correct, to rectify it. So the purpose of preparing and correcting the foundations and beliefs is that those beliefs should be in accordance with truth and on the path of correctness, not beliefs that oppose truth, like the corrupt belief of the philosophers that there is no real distinction in the essence of Allah, nor even a conceptual distinction. Based on this, they said that Allah created only the first intellect, which created the second, and so on. Because if all things were acknowledged to be created by Allah's essence, then a conceptual distinction in Allah's essence would be necessary, because the essence of Allah in terms of being the creator of 'Amr is distinct from the essence that is the creator of Bakr. In summary, this is also an affirmation of the oneness of Allah, but not on the truthful way and the correct path; rather, on the path of error and corruption. And by 'furu' al-shari'ah', the detailed fiqh rulings explained in the science of fiqh are meant. And 'al-ma'ani' (the meanings) from 'ma'ani al-furu' are the particular causes (illal) that are established upon each fiqh issue, like in al-Hidayah where for every issue a proof and cause are presented. Note: From the commentator's expression, it becomes clear that by 'ma'na' (meaning) is intended 'illah (cause), and the two are synonymous. And this is the terminology of the fuqaha: they use the word 'ma'na' instead of 'illah. The reason for avoidance is that the word 'illah was frequently used by the philosophers, and the fuqaha avoided philosophical terminology. Therefore, they used the word 'ma'na' in place of 'illah, as the author of al-Hidayah said: 'Chapter on the meanings that necessitate wudu', i.e., the causes and reasons, etc.' And their precision: that they are subtle. Explaining that, the commentator said that by 'precision of the meanings' it is meant that these causes are deep, subtle, and difficult; not everyone can easily access them; rather, the mujtahid extracts them after great effort. And 'all of that' - clarifying the specification of the praised one, the commentator says that all these things are from Allah. Shari'ah is a blessing because through it the system of this world is established and sustained, and upon it depends the reward of the Hereafter. Also, the precision of the causes is a blessing of Allah, because the mujtahids will face hardships and difficulties in extracting and deriving them, through which Allah will elevate their ranks and grant them reward in the abode of recompense. Benefit: In usul al-shari'ah, the idafah of usul...
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the opening lines of Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah. The commentator begins by translating the matn, then answers a potential objection: why does the author specifically associate 'praises' with the blessing of knowledge of Shari'ah, when there are countless blessings? The answer is that knowledge is the greatest blessing; all others are insignificant in comparison. Next, the commentator defines 'Shari'ah' broadly: it includes both fiqh (positive law) and non-fiqh matters (like beliefs about the Beatific Vision, Resurrection, and the authority of consensus and analogy) that are proven by transmitted (sam'i) proofs. Matters proven solely by rational proofs, such as the existence of God or the truthfulness of prophets, are not part of Shari'ah in this technical sense. Why? Because the phrase 'usul al-shari'ah' in the matn uses idafah (construct state), which implies specification: Shari'ah is that which is derived from the usul (the primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, etc.), and those sources are sam'i. Rational matters are not derived from them; rather, the usul themselves depend on rational proofs for their validation (e.g., proving the existence and attributes of God, the truth of prophethood). Hence, Shari'ah in this context is restricted to sam'i matters. The commentator then defines the key terms of the science: 'al-usul' are the general proofs (kulliyat: Book, Sunnah, consensus, analogy); 'mabani al-usul' (foundations of the usul) are the creedal beliefs (such as knowledge of God's essence and attributes, prophethood, miracles) upon which the validity of the usul rests; 'furu' al-shari'ah' are the detailed fiqh rulings; and 'ma'ani' (meanings) are the specific causes (illal) that ground each fiqh ruling—the term 'ma'na' is used by Hanafi fuqaha instead of 'illah to avoid philosophical terminology, as exemplified by the Hidayah's chapter on 'meanings that necessitate wudu'. The commentator emphasizes the precision (diqqa) of these causes: they are deep and subtle, accessible only to mujtahids through strenuous effort. Finally, he reiterates that all these—Shari'ah, its precision, the effort of scholars—are divine blessings that necessitate gratitude, for through them worldly order and otherworldly reward are achieved. This passage thus establishes the epistemological hierarchy: knowledge of usul al-fiqh sits between fiqh (which it serves) and kalam (which provides its foundational premises).

Key Terms
أصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The general proofs (kulliyat) from which Shari'ah is derived: the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy.
مباني الأصول (mabani al-usul): The foundational beliefs upon which the usul depend, such as knowledge of God's existence, attributes, prophethood, and miracles.
فروع الشريعة (furu' al-shari'ah): The detailed fiqh rulings that are the branches of Shari'ah, as explained in fiqh books.
المعنى (al-ma'na): The cause ('illah) for a fiqh ruling, used by fuqaha to avoid philosophical terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct ordering of disciplines according to the hierarchy mentioned in the passage?
A) Fiqh, then Usul al-Fiqh, then Kalam
B) Kalam, then Usul al-Fiqh, then Fiqh
C) Usul al-Fiqh, then Fiqh, then Kalam
D) Kalam, then Fiqh, then Usul al-Fiqh

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh provides the principles to derive fiqh from the sources, depends on kalam for its foundations, and uses the term 'ma'na' for the causes of rulings.

Method of Learning

Defining the Components of Usul al-Fiqh: Usul, Mabani, Tamhid, Furu', and Ma'ani
Commentary defining key usul terms and their interrelationships

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define and distinguish between usul al-sharia, mabani al-usul, tamhid, furu' al-sharia, and ma'ani, and explain their interrelationships as per Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh rests on theological foundations (mabani) and yields detailed rulings (furu'), while ma'ani (causes) are subtle chains linking evidence to ruling.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih clarifies five key terms that form the conceptual backbone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Understanding these terms is essential before you can navigate the relationship between foundational proofs, theological prerequisites, and derived rulings. The commentator also highlights a distinctive Hanafi terminological choice: using 'ma'na' instead of 'illa' to avoid philosophical overtones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five terms
Locate in the passage the definitions of usul al-sharia, mabani al-usul, tamhid, furu' al-sharia, and ma'ani. Note how each is introduced and the context of the discussion.
These are not random; they form a hierarchy from foundations to branches.
2
Distinguish usul from mabani
Usul al-sharia refers to the derived sharia from the primary sources (Book, Sunnah, etc.), while mabani al-usul are the theological beliefs (like knowledge of Allah) upon which the acceptance of those sources depends. Understand that usul al-fiqh depends on mabani, not vice versa.
Mabani belong to 'ilm al-kalam, not usul al-fiqh proper.
3
Understand the purpose of tamhid
Tamhid means correcting and reforming the foundational beliefs so they align with truth. The commentator contrasts correct 'aqida with the corrupt beliefs of philosophers to illustrate the stakes.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on sound theology as a prerequisite for legal reasoning.
4
Differentiate furu' from usul
Furu' al-sharia are the detailed fiqh rulings (branches) derived from the usul (roots). The relationship is one of deduction: the general proofs give rise to specific rules.
The idafa (construct) in 'furu' al-sharia' is part-to-whole, while in 'usul al-sharia' it is evidence-to-signified.
5
Analyze the term ma'ani
Ma'ani are the 'causes' (illa) behind fiqh rulings. The commentator explains that Hanafi jurists deliberately use 'ma'na' instead of 'illa' to avoid philosophical baggage. These causes are subtle (dha'iqat) and require deep investigation by the mujtahid.
This terminological choice is a hallmark of Hanafi legal methodology.

ہے کہ اضافت تخصیص کا فائدہ دیتی ہے اب اصول شریعت کا معنی ہوگا وہ شریعت جو مستفاد و حاصل ہے اصول سے اور اصول سے مراد کتاب وسنت وغیرہ ہیں اور یہی ادلہ سمعیہ ہیں تو ادلہ سمعیہ کی تخصیص اس لیے کی گئی تا کہ وہ امور جو ثابت بالا ولہ التقلیہ ہیں خارج ہو جائیں کیونکہ وہ مستفاد من الاصول نہیں بلکہ خود اصول ان سے مستفاد ہیں جیسے علم ذات باری تعالی وصفاتہ وعلم صدق المبلغ وغیرہ جن سے علم الکلام میں بحث کی جاتی ہے اصول فقہ شریعت ( کتاب وسنہ وغیرہ) ان پر موقوف ہیں ولا عکسہ نہ کہ وہ ان پر موقوف ہیں) الاصولی سے مراد ادلہ کلیہ ( کتاب سنت اجماع و قیاس) ہیں۔ و مبانی الاصول سے عقائد مراد ہیں جن پر اصول بنی ہیں مثلا ذات باری وصفات باری کا علم و نبوت کا علم معجزات کا علم وغیرہ وتمهيدها تسویتھا سے تمھید کا معنی کیا کسی شئی کا درست کرنا اس کی اصلاح کرنا تو مبانی و عقائد کا تسو یہ واصلاح کا مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ وہ عقائد موافق حق اور علی نسج الصواب ہوں ایسے عقائد نہ ہوں جو مخالف حق ہوں جیسے فلاسفہ کا عقیدہ فاسدہ ہے کہ ذات باری تعالی میں تغار حقیقی بھی نہیں ہے تغایر اعتباری بھی نہیں اسی بناء پر انہوں نے کہا کہ اللہ تعالی نے صرف عقل اول کو پیدا کیا اس نے ثانی کو اور اس نے ثالث الخ ، کیونکہ اگر تمام چیزوں کا خالق ذات باری تعالی کو تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو ذات باری تعالی میں تغایر اعتباری لازم آئے گا کیونکہ ذات اللہ بایں حیثیت کہ خالق عمرو ہے مغایر ہے اس ذات اللہ کے جو خالق بکر ہے خلاصہ اینکہ یہ بھی تو حید باری تعالی کا اثبات ہے لیکن لاعلی طریق الحق و شبح الصواب بل على طريق الغلط والفساد وفـــــــروع الشريعة سے احکام فقہیہ مفصلہ مبینہ فی علم الفقہ مراد ہیں۔ المعانی معانی فروغ سے وہ عمل جزئیہ مراد ہیں جو ہر مسئلہ فقہیہ پر قائم کی جاتی ہیں جیسے ھدایہ میں ہر مسئلہ پر دلیل و علت پیش کی جاتی ہے۔ تنبیہ شارح ! کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ معنی سے علت مراد ہے اور یہ دونوں مرادف ہیں اور یہ اصطلاح فقہاء ہے کہ وہ بجائے لفظ علت کے معنی کا لفظ بولتے ہیں وجہ احتراز یہ بیان کی گئی ہے کہ لفظ علت اہل فلاسفہ کے ہاں کثیر الاستعمال تھا اور فقہاء اصطلاحات فلسفیہ سے احتراز کرتے تھے اسی بناء پر لفظ معنی کو بجائے لفظ علت استعمال کرتے ہیں کما قال صاحب الحدایہ فصل فی المعانى الموجبة للوضوء أى فى الاسباب والعلل الخ- ودقتها كونها دقيقة کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے شارج نے فرمایا کہ وقت معانی سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ عمل کافی گہرے اور لطیف و مشکل ہیں ہر شخص ان تک رسائی با السہولت نہیں کرسکتا بلکہ مجتہد سعی بسیار کے بعد ان کا استخراج کرتا ہے۔ وجميع ذلک سے تخصیص محمود علیہ کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے شارح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تمام اشیا تم من جانب اللہ ہیں شریعت بایں وجہ نعمت ہے کہ اسی کے ذریعہ سے نظام دنیا کا قیام وبقاء ہے اور اس پر ثواب عقبی کا مدار ہے۔ نیز علل کا دقیق ہونا بھی نعمت اللہ ہے کیونکہ مجتہدین ان کے استخراج و استنباط میں صعوبات و مشکلات کا سامنا کریں گے جس کے طفیل اللہ تعالی ان کے درجات کو رفعت و بلندی عطاء فرمائیں گے اور دار الجزاء میں ثواب و بدلہ عطاء فرمائیں گے۔ فائدہ ! اصول الشریعہ میں اضافت اصول الى الشريعة من تبیل اضافت الدلیل الی مدلولہ ہے اور فروعھا میں اضافت فروع الى الشريعة من قبيل اضافة الجزء الی الکل
Miskulmaleehurdu Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: That the construct idafa gives the benefit of specification (takhsis). Now usul al-sharia means the sharia derived and obtained from usul, and usul refers to the Book and Sunnah etc., and these are the sam'i evidences. The specification of sam'i evidences is done so that matters proven by primary rational proofs are excluded, because they are not derived from usul, but rather usul themselves are derived from them, such as knowledge of the Essence of Allah Most High and His attributes, and knowledge of the truthfulness of the messenger, etc., which are discussed in 'ilm al-kalam. Usul al-fiqh (i.e., the sharia of the Book and Sunnah) are dependent on them, not the opposite. Al-usuli (that which pertains to usul) means the general proofs (Book, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas). And mabani al-usul (foundations of usul) refers to beliefs upon which usul are built, e.g., knowledge of the Essence of Allah and His attributes, knowledge of prophethood, knowledge of miracles, etc. And tamhiduha taswiyatuha: tamhid means correcting something, reforming it. So the purpose of taswiyah and reform of the mabani and beliefs is that these beliefs be in accordance with truth and correct methodology, not opposing truth like the corrupt belief of the philosophers that there is no real distinction in the Essence of Allah, nor even a conceptual distinction. On this basis they said that Allah created only the First Intellect, which created the second, and so on, because if Allah were accepted as the Creator of all things, then there would be a necessary conceptual distinction in the Essence, for the essence of Allah as Creator of Amr is different from the essence of Allah as Creator of Bakr. Summary: this is also an affirmation of tawhid, but not upon the way of truth and correctness, but upon the way of error and corruption. And furu' al-sharia refers to detailed fiqh rulings explained in the science of fiqh. Al-ma'ani: ma'ani furu' refers to those partial actions that are established for every fiqh issue, as in Hidayah where each issue is presented with its evidence and cause. Warning: From the commentator's expression it is understood that 'meaning' (ma'na) is intended as 'cause' ('illa), and both are synonymous. This is the terminology of the fuqaha: they use the word 'ma'na' in place of 'illa'. The reason for avoidance is that the word 'illa' was widely used by the philosophers, and the fuqaha avoided philosophical terminology. Hence they use 'ma'na' for 'illa', as the author of Hidayah said: 'Chapter on the ma'ani that necessitate wudu', i.e., the causes and reasons etc.' And her dha'iqatuha (its subtlety): explaining that 'ma'ani' refers to actions that are deep, subtle, and difficult; not everyone can access them easily, but the mujtahid extracts them after great effort. And jami'u dhalik: explaining the commendable specification, the commentator says: All these things are from Allah. The sharia is a blessing because by means of it the system of this world is established and sustained, and upon it depends the reward of the Hereafter. Also, the subtlety of causes is a blessing of Allah, because the mujtahids will face difficulties and hardships in extracting and deducing them, through which Allah Most High will raise their ranks and give them reward in the Abode of Recompense. Benefit: In usul al-sharia, the idafa of usul to sharia is of the type of idafa of the evidence to its signified, while in its furu', the idafa of furu' to sharia is of the type of idafa of the part to the whole.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining key terms of usul al-fiqh as presented in al-Tawdih. The author begins by clarifying that the construct (idafa) in 'usul al-sharia' serves to specify the sources. The term 'usul' here refers to the primary textual sources—Qur'an and Sunnah—collectively called 'sam'i evidences'. These are distinguished from matters established by pure reason (like knowledge of Allah's existence) because the latter are foundations (mabani) upon which the authority of the revealed sources depends. Thus, 'usul al-fiqh' denotes the general proofs (the four sources), while 'mabani al-usul' refers to the theological beliefs (like tawhid, prophethood) that underpin the acceptance of these sources. The commentator then discusses the purpose of 'tamhid' (preparation) of these foundations, ensuring they are correct (e.g., the contrast with philosophers who deny conceptual distinction in Allah, leading to erroneous conclusions). Next, 'furu' al-sharia' are the detailed rulings of fiqh. Finally, 'ma'ani' is explained as an synonym for 'illa' (cause or ratio legis), a deliberate terminological choice by Hanafi jurists to avoid the philosophical connotations of 'illa'. The subtlety of these causes is highlighted—they require deep reflection and are not easily accessible, rewarding the mujtahid's effort. The passage concludes by noting that all this is a divine blessing, and the idafa in 'usul al-sharia' indicates the relationship of evidence to its signified, while in 'furu' al-sharia' it indicates part to whole.

Key Terms
اصول الشریعہ (usul al-sharia): The Sharia that is derived from the sources (usul) which are the Book and Sunnah.
مبانی الاصول (mabani al-usul): The foundational beliefs (like knowledge of Allah and prophethood) upon which the authority of usul rests.
تمهید (tamhid): The preparation or correction of foundational beliefs to be in accordance with truth.
فروع الشریعہ (furu' al-sharia): The detailed fiqh rulings that are the branches derived from usul.
معانی (ma'ani): In this context, meanings are the causes (illa) behind fiqh rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Hanafi jurists prefer the word 'ma'na' over 'illa'?
A) Because 'illa' does not capture the full meaning of cause
B) Because 'illa' was heavily used by philosophers and they sought to avoid philosophical terminology
C) Because 'ma'na' is more precise in Arabic grammar
D) Because 'illa' is a derivative of a weak root

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul al-fiqh distinguishes between theological foundations (mabani), primary sources (usul), derived rulings (furu'), and the subtle causes (ma'ani) that link evidence to ruling.

The Hierarchical Order of the Three Islamic Sciences: Kalam, Usul, Fiqh
Argues the superiority of kalam over usul and usul over fiqh, with objections answered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of kalam, usul al-fiqh, and fiqh, and classify the type of dependency (tawaqquf) used to argue for this hierarchy.

Core Idea
Knowledge of particular rulings depends on general proofs, which depend on theological truths — a three-level hierarchy of dependency.

In this passage, the commentator (following Sadr al-Shari'ah) argues for a clear hierarchy among the three foundational Islamic sciences: Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh. The argument hinges on a careful classification of dependency (tawaqquf). Understanding this hierarchy helps you see the logical order of study and the foundational role of theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
State the commentator's claim: Kalam is higher than Usul, and Usul is higher than Fiqh. Ask what 'higher' means in this context.
The passage later clarifies that 'higher' refers to priority in the order of learning (tahsil wa talab).
2
Trace the proof structure
The proof uses the concept of mawquf 'alayh (the thing depended upon). Kalam is mawquf 'alayh for Usul because the sources (Book and Sunnah) depend on theological truths. Usul is mawquf 'alayh for Fiqh because particular rulings depend on general proofs studied in Usul.
The principle: 'the depended-upon is higher than the dependent.'
3
Analyze the objection
The objection gives a counterexample: prayer (salat) depends on wudu', but wudu' is not higher than prayer. This challenges the principle that all depended-upon things are higher.
4
Classify the types of dependency
The commentator distinguishes three types: instrumental (e.g., merchant on Allah), conditional (e.g., prayer on wudu'), and root-branch (e.g., branch on root). Only the third type requires the depended-upon to be higher.
The dependency in the hierarchy of sciences is of the root-branch type.
5
Apply the classification and note the clarification
Apply the classification: Kalam is the root for Usul, Usul is the root for Fiqh, so the hierarchy holds. Also note that superiority is about order of study, not honor, so the prayer/wudu' objection is irrelevant.

وفى هذا الكلام اشاره فرض شارح علوم ثلاثہ ( علم کلام اصول فقہ وعلم الفقہ ) کے مراتب کو بیان کرنا ہے حاصل اینکه مصنف صدر الشریعہ کی عبارت سے اشارہ ہے کہ علم الکلام اعلی ہے اصول فقہ سے اور اصول فقہ اعلی ہے فقہ سے علم الکلام اس لئے اعلی ہے کہ اس کو مبانی اصول قرار دیا ہے اور منی شئی کا اعلی ہوتا ہے اور اصول فقہ اس لیے اعلیٰ ہے کہ اس کو اصل فقہ کہا اور اصل شئی فرع پر فائق ہوتا ہے. لان معرفۃ الاحکام الجزیہ سے اسی دعوی مذکور کی دلیل پیش کی کہ احکام جزئیہ کی معرفتہ بادل تھا تفصیلیہ اولہ کلیہ کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے من حیث انھا توصل الی الاحکام الشریعۃ اور اس کی بحث اصول فقہ میں ہوتی ہے تو اصول فقہ فقہ کیلئے موقوف علیہ بن گیا اور موقوف علیہ فائق واعلی من الموقوف ہوتا ہے پھر ادلہ کلیہ یعنی کتاب وسنت موقوف ہیں معرفت ذات وصفات باری تعالی و صدق المبلغ و غیرہ پر جن کی بحث علم کلام میں کی جاتی ہے کیونکہ علم الکلام وہ ہے جس میں احوال صانع و نبوت و امامت و معاد وغیرہ سے بحث کی جاتی ہے اور یہ بحث علی قانون اسلام ہوتی ہے لاعلیٰ طریق الحكمة الأهمية تو علم کلام اصول فقہ کیلئے موقوف علیہ بن گیا اور موقوف علیہ اعلی من الموقوف ہوتا ہے تو علم کلام کا ارفع ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ سوال یہ توقف مسلم ہے مگر کبری تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ کل موقوف علیہ اعلی من الموقوف مثلا صلوۃ موقوف على الوضوء ہے لیکن موقوف علیہ ( وضوء ) اعلی نہیں ہے بلکہ بر عکس ہے ۔ جواب !(۱) توقف تین اقسام پر ہے (۱) توقف ذی آلہ علی الآلہ کتوقف التجار علی الله (۲) توقف مشرو على شرط مثل توقف الصلوة على الوضوء ان دونوں قسموں میں موقوف علیہ کا اعلی من الموقوف ہونا ضروری اور شرط نہیں ہے (۳) توقف فرع علی الاصل اس میں موقوف علیہ کا اعلی من الموقوف ہونا ضروری اور شرط ہے اور یہاں پر توقف از قبیل قسم ثالث ہے لھذا کلام تفتازانی درست ہے۔ جواب ! (۲) یہاں فوقیت سے فوقیت باعتبار شرافت مراد نہیں ہے تا کہ اعتراض بسابق لازم آئے بلکہ فوقیت باعتبار تحصیل وطلب مراد ہے کہ اولا طلب علم کلام و ثانیا طلب اصول فقہ اور آخر میں طلب فقہ ضروری ہے۔
And in this speech there is an indication that the commentator considered the ranks of the three sciences (ilm al-kalam, usul al-fiqh, and ilm al-fiqh). The conclusion is that the statement of the author (Sadr al-Shari'ah) indicates that ilm al-kalam is higher than usul al-fiqh, and usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh. Ilm al-kalam is higher because it is made the foundation (mabani) of usul, and the foundation of a thing is higher. Usul al-fiqh is higher because it is called the root (asl) of fiqh, and the root is superior to the branch. Because knowledge of particular rulings (ahkam juz'iyyah) depends on knowledge of detailed or general proofs, from the aspect that they lead to the rulings of shari'ah; and its discussion is in usul al-fiqh. So usul al-fiqh became the thing upon which fiqh depends (mawquf 'alayh), and that upon which something depends is higher and superior than the dependent. Then the general proofs, i.e., the Book and Sunnah, depend on knowledge of the Essence and attributes of Allah Most High and the truthfulness of the messenger, etc., which are discussed in ilm al-kalam. Because ilm al-kalam is that in which the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, and the resurrection are discussed, and this discussion is according to the law of Islam, not according to the method of prime philosophy. So ilm al-kalam became that upon which usul al-fiqh depends, and that upon which something depends is higher than the dependent. Thus the superiority of ilm al-kalam is established. Objection: This dependency is accepted, but the major premise is not granted: that every dependent-upon thing is higher than the dependent. For example, prayer depends on wudu', but wudu' is not higher; rather the opposite. Answer (1): Dependency is of three types: (i) dependency of an instrument on the instrumental means, like the dependency of a merchant on Allah; (ii) dependency of a conditioned thing on a condition, like prayer on wudu'; in these two types, it is not necessary that the dependent-upon be higher than the dependent; (iii) dependency of a branch on the root. In this type, it is necessary and a condition that the dependent-upon be higher than the dependent. Here, the dependency is of the third type, so Taftazani's statement is correct. Answer (2): Here superiority is not meant in terms of honor, so that the previous objection would follow; rather it is superiority in terms of acquisition and pursuit: that first the pursuit of ilm al-kalam is necessary, then the pursuit of usul al-fiqh, and finally the pursuit of fiqh.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a rational argument establishing the hierarchical relationship among the three Islamic sciences: kalam, usul al-fiqh, and fiqh. The commentator, following Sadr al-Shari'ah, asserts that kalam is the highest because it provides the foundational beliefs (mabani) for usul. Then usul al-fiqh is higher than fiqh because it is the root (asl) from which fiqh rules are derived. The proof: knowledge of particular fiqh rulings depends on knowledge of the general proofs (the sources), which is the subject of usul; therefore usul is mawquf 'alayh (the thing depended upon) and fiqh is mawquf (dependent). Similarly, the sources themselves depend on theological truths (like knowing Allah and the truthfulness of prophets), which are discussed in kalam. Hence kalam is mawquf 'alayh for usul. The principle 'the depended-upon is higher' is then defended against an objection using prayer's dependence on wudu' as a counterexample. The commentator distinguishes three types of dependency: instrumental (alat), conditional (shart), and root-branch (asl-far'). Only the third type requires the depended-upon to be higher. Here the dependency is of the third type, so the hierarchy holds. A second answer clarifies that the superiority is not of honor but of sequential learning: one must study kalam first, then usul, then fiqh.

Key Terms
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayh): The thing upon which another thing depends; the foundation or prerequisite.
توقف (tawaqquf): Dependency or reliance of one thing on another.
فوقیت (fawqiyyah): Superiority, here understood as priority in order of learning (tahsil wa talab).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of dependency (tawaqquf) is used to argue that ilm al-kalam is higher than usul al-fiqh?
A) Dependency of an instrument on its user.
B) Dependency of a conditioned thing on its condition.
C) Dependency of a branch on its root.
D) All dependencies imply superiority of the depended-upon.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of kalam, usul, and fiqh is established by a root-branch dependency, where the root (kalam) must be studied first, then usul, then fiqh.

Hierarchy of Islamic Sciences and Types of Dependency
Explaining the superiority of Kalam over Usul and Usul over Fiqh with dependency typology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi hierarchy of Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, and Fiqh, and classify types of tawaqquf to determine when the depended-upon is superior.

Core Idea
Only branch-root dependency implies the superiority of the foundation over the derived branch.

This passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih clarifies the relative superiority of the three core Islamic sciences. The commentator uses the concept of dependency (tawaqquf) to argue that Kalam is superior to Usul al-Fiqh, and Usul al-Fiqh is superior to Fiqh. When confronted with a counterexample from prayer and ablution, he introduces a three-part typology of dependency to defend the claim. Understanding this typology is essential for grasping how Islamic disciplines are epistemologically ordered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its proof structure
The commentator claims Kalam > Usul > Fiqh. The proof relies on the idea that the depended-upon (mawquf 'alayh) is superior to the dependent (mawquf). Notice the chain: Fiqh depends on Usul (for general evidence), and Usul depends on Kalam (for foundational truths).
The Arabic phrase 'موقوف علیہ اعلی من الموقوف' encapsulates the major premise.
2
Recognize the objection
The objector denies the major premise by pointing to prayer depending on ablution, where ablution is not superior. This challenges the universality of the claimed principle.
The objection is valid only if the dependency type is the same.
3
Analyze the response: three types of tawaqquf
The commentator introduces three types: (1) instrument on tool, (2) conditioned on condition, (3) branch on root. Only the third type carries the implication of superiority.
Memorize the Arabic: توقف ذی آلہ علی الآلہ, توقف مشروط علی شرط, توقف فرع علی الأصل.
4
Classify the dependencies in the hierarchy
The dependency of Fiqh on Usul and Usul on Kalam is branch-root, not condition. Therefore, the superiority claim holds for the hierarchy.
Contrast with prayer-ablution which is condition type.
5
Clarify the nature of superiority
The commentator clarifies that superiority here refers to the order of acquisition (تحصیل وطلب), not inherent honor. One must study Kalam first, then Usul, then Fiqh.
This avoids objections about Kalam being 'more honorable' than Fiqh.

شرح التوضيح و
الى الشريعة من تبیل اضافت الدلیل الی مدلولہ ہے اور فروعھا میں اضافت فروع الى الشريعة من قبيل اضافة الجزء الی الکل ہے وفى هذا الكلام اشاره فرض شارح علوم ثلاثہ ( علم کلام اصول فقہ وعلم الفقہ ) کے مراتب کو بیان کرنا ہے حاصل اینکه مصنف صدر الشریعہ کی عبارت سے اشارہ ہے کہ علم الکلام اعلی ہے اصول فقہ سے اور اصول فقہ اعلی ہے فقہ سے علم الکلام اس لئے اعلی ہے کہ اس کو مبانی اصول قرار دیا ہے اور منی شئی کا اعلی ہوتا ہے اور اصول فقہ اس لیے اعلیٰ ہے کہ اس کو اصل فقہ کہا اور اصل شئی فرع پر فائق ہوتا ہے. لان معرفۃ الاحکام الجزیہ سے اسی دعوی مذکور کی دلیل پیش کی کہ احکام جزئیہ کی معرفتہ بادل تھا اتفصیلیہ اولہ کلیہ کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے من حیث انھا توصل الی الاحکام الشریعۃ اور اس کی بحث اصول فقہ میں ہوتی ہے تو اصول فقہ فقہ کیلئے موقوف علیہ بن گیا اور موقوف علیہ فائق واعلی من الموقوف ہوتا ہے پھر ادلہ کلیہ یعنی کتاب وسنت موقوف ہیں معرفت ذات وصفات باری تعالی و صدق المبلغ و غیرہ پر جن کی بحث علم کلام میں کی جاتی ہے کیونکہ علم الکلام وہ ہے جس میں احوال صانع و نبوت و امامت و معاد وغیرہ سے بحث کی جاتی ہے اور یہ بحث علی قانون اسلام ہوتی ہے لاعلیٰ طریق الحكمة الأهمية تو علم کلام اصول فقہ کیلئے موقوف علیہ بن گیا اور موقوف علیہ اعلی من الموقوف ہوتا ہے تو علم کلام کا ارفع ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ سوال یہ توقف مسلم ہے مگر کبری تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ کل موقوف علیہ اعلی من الموقوف مثلا صلوۃ موقوف على الوضوء ہے لیکن موقوف علیہ ( وضوء ) اعلی نہیں ہے بلکہ بر عکس ہے ۔ جواب !(۱) توقف تین اقسام پر ہے (۱) توقف ذی آلہ علی الآلہ کتوقف التجار علی الله (۲) توقف مشرو على شرط مثل توقف الصلوة على الوضوء ان دونوں قسموں میں موقوف علیہ کا اعلی من الموقوف ہونا ضروری اور شرط نہیں ہے (۳) توقف فرع علی الاصل اس میں موقوف علیہ کا اعلی من الموقوف ہونا ضروری اور شرط ہے اور یہاں پر توقف از قبیل قسم ثالث ہے لھذا کلام تفتازانی درست ہے۔ جواب ! (۲) یہاں فوقیت سے فوقیت باعتبار شرافت مراد نہیں ہے تا کہ اعتراض بسابق لازم آئے بلکہ فوقیت باعتبار تحصیل وطلب مراد ہے کہ اولا طلب علم کلام و ثانیا طلب اصول فقہ اور آخر میں طلب فقہ ضروری ہے۔
Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih: 'Ila al-shari'a min tabyil idafat al-dalil ila madlulihi' and in its branches, the addition of branches to the shari'a is of the type of adding a part to the whole. In this speech, there is an indication of an assumption of the commentator regarding the three sciences (Kalam, Usul al-Fiqh, Fiqh) to explain their ranks. The summary is that there is an indication from the expression of the author Sadr al-Shari'ah that the science of Kalam is superior to Usul al-Fiqh, and Usul al-Fiqh is superior to Fiqh. The science of Kalam is superior because it has been made the foundations of usul, and a thing's foundations are superior. And Usul al-Fiqh is superior because it is called the root of Fiqh, and the root surpasses the branch. 'Because the knowledge of particular rulings' — from this, he presents a proof for the mentioned claim: that the knowledge of particular rulings, by detailed evidence, is dependent on the knowledge of general evidence, insofar as they lead to the rulings of the Shari'ah. And its discussion occurs in Usul al-Fiqh. So Usul al-Fiqh became the thing on which Fiqh depends, and that on which something depends is superior and higher than the dependent. Then the general evidences, i.e., the Book and Sunnah, depend on the knowledge of the essence and attributes of Allah Most High, the truthfulness of the messenger, and other things, whose discussion is in the science of Kalam. Because the science of Kalam is that in which discussion is made about the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, resurrection, etc. And this discussion occurs according to the law of Islam, not according to the way of fundamental philosophy. So Kalam became the thing on which Usul al-Fiqh depends, and that on which something depends is higher than the dependent. Thus the elevation of Kalam is established. Objection: This dependency is granted, but the major premise that every thing depended upon is higher than the dependent is not granted. For example, prayer depends on ablution, but ablution is not higher; rather, it is the opposite. Response (1): Dependency is of three types: (1) dependency of an instrument on the instrument, like the dependence of trade on the tool [؟]; (2) dependency of a conditioned thing on a condition, like the dependence of prayer on ablution. In these two types, the depended-upon being higher than the dependent is not necessary or required. (3) dependency of a branch on the root. In this type, the depended-upon being higher than the dependent is necessary and required. And here the dependency is of the third type. Therefore, the speech of Taftazani is correct. Response (2): Here, superiority does not mean superiority in honor, so that the previous objection would apply. Rather, superiority in terms of acquisition and seeking is intended: that seeking the science of Kalam is first, then seeking Usul al-Fiqh, and finally seeking Fiqh is necessary.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih concerning the hierarchy of Islamic sciences. The commentator explains that the author Sadr al-Shari'ah indicated that the science of Kalam (theology) is superior to Usul al-Fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), and Usul al-Fiqh is superior to Fiqh (jurisprudence). The reasoning is that Kalam provides the foundational beliefs (e.g., existence and attributes of God, prophethood) upon which the general evidences (Quran and Sunnah) rely. Usul al-Fiqh then provides the methods for deriving particular rulings from those general evidences. The commentator explains the concept of dependency (tawaqquf) and classifies it into three types: (1) dependency of an instrument on its tool, (2) dependency of a conditioned thing on its condition, and (3) dependency of a branch on its root. Only the third type implies that the depended-upon is superior. The objection regarding prayer and ablution does not apply because that is a condition-type dependency. Finally, the commentator clarifies that the superiority here is not in inherent honor but in the order of acquisition: one must first learn Kalam, then Usul, then Fiqh.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Dependency or reliance of one thing on another; classified into three types: instrument, condition, and branch-root.
موقوف علیہ (mawquf 'alayh): That upon which something depends; the thing that is relied upon.
موقوف (mawquf): The dependent thing; that which relies on something else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of dependency (tawaqquf) implies that the depended-upon (mawquf 'alayh) is superior to the dependent (mawquf)?
A) Dependency of an instrument on a tool
B) Dependency of a conditioned thing on a condition
C) Dependency of a branch on a root
D) All types of dependency

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul recognizes three types of dependency; only branch-root dependency implies the superiority of the foundation over the derived branch.

Defining 'Asl' in Usul al-Fiqh: The Hanafi Approach to Terminological Precision
Beginning the definition of usul al-fiqh via the relational definition and analysis of 'asl'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'asl' (that upon which something else is built) and explain why the definition 'that which is needed by another' (Imam al-Razi) is rejected as not muttarid.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'asl' is defined as that which something else is built upon, not merely what is needed.

This lesson begins the actual subject matter of usul al-fiqh. Sadr al-Shari'ah first defines usul al-fiqh via two approaches: the idafi (relational) and haqiqi (real) definitions. He then dissects the word 'asl', the plural of which is 'usul'. Understanding this foundational term is critical because the entire discipline of usul al-fiqh is built upon the concept of evidence (dalil) being the 'asl' for rulings. The passage also critiques a competing definition from Imam al-Razi, highlighting the Hanafi insistence on precision and completeness in definitions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two approaches to defining 'usul al-fiqh'
The author first introduces the idafi definition (defining mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately) and the haqiqi definition (defining the composite as a discipline title). Identify these two approaches in the opening lines.
The idafi definition is a preparatory step before the haqiqi definition.
2
Isolate the definition of 'asl'
The key definition: 'asl' is 'ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh' (that upon which something else is built). Write this down verbatim.
This is the core lexical definition that underlies all usages in Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish between sensory and rational building (ibtina')
The building can be sensory (roof on wall) or rational (evidence supporting a ruling). Both are covered by the term 'ibtina''. Note the author's example of 'al-hukm 'ala al-dalil'.
This dual coverage is a strength of the Hanafi definition; it is not limited to physical foundations.
4
Evaluate Imam al-Razi's definition
Imam al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed by another'. Sadr al-Shari'ah rejects this as not muttarid (not inclusive and exclusive). Think why: a wall is needed by the roof, but the wall is the 'asl' (the roof is built on it), so the definition wrongly includes the needed thing as asl and fails to exclude mere need without building.
The term 'muttarid' is key: a valid definition must include all intended instances and exclude all non-instances.
5
Understand the classification of definitions and essences
The passage ends with a preface: definitions can be haqiqiyya (revealing real essence) or i'tibariyya (conceptual composite by convention), and essences similarly. This is preparatory for evaluating the definition of 'asl' as i'tibari.
The definition of 'asl' is i'tibari because it is a conventional construct coined by scholars, not a real essence like humanity.

ھو تخصيل مفهوم الشئي الغير الحاصل في القوة المدركة تعریف آئی یہ ہے کہ ایک مفہوم مرتب کو قوت مدر کہ میں حاصل کیا جاتا ہے مثلا واضع چند امور مرکبہ متیرونی الذہن ( تیار شدہ ) ( بقول حضرت شیخ الحدیث مولانا علی محمد صاحب) کا اعتبار کر کے ان کے مقابلہ میں ایک اسم وضع کر دیتا ہے وہ اہم موضوع اور امور و اجزاء مرکبہ ومشیرہ موضع لہ ہوتے ہیں جب بھی اس اسم کے بارے میں سوال کیا جائے گا۔ جواب ! The text of al-Tanqih with al-Tawdih: 'These are usul al-fiqh'. The author explains the construction. He mentions two probabilities: it is a predicate of an omitted subject 'these' (i.e. these are usul al-fiqh) (2) or an omitted subject with predicate (i.e. what is usul al-fiqh?). Since this is an interrogative sentence, the author answers by mentioning a definition. Thus he says: 'We will first define it by way of addition (idafa)'. The meaning of the phrase is that two definitions of usul al-fiqh will be mentioned: (1) the idafi definition, (2) the haqiqi definition. The idafi definition: to define the mudaf and mudaf ilayh separately. The haqiqi definition: to define the mudaf and mudaf ilayh as a composite, because that composite has become the title of a science. Sadr al-Shari'ah says: 'First we will mention the idafi definition, then the haqiqi.' While mentioning the idafi definition, he investigates the word 'usul'. 'Usul' is the plural of 'asl'. The meaning of 'asl' is 'that upon which something else is built.' Then he clarifies that building (ibtina') is of two types: (1) sensory building, (2) rational building. The word 'ibtina' includes both. The first example is the building of the roof on the wall; the second example the author gives is the ordering of a ruling upon evidence. 'And its definition as 'that which is needed by another' is not inclusive and exclusive (muttarid). Imam al-Razi defined it thus in al-Mahsul.' The author's purpose is to refute Imam al-Razi: Imam al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed by another' (al-asl huwa al-muhtaj ilayh). Sadr al-Shari'ah refutes him saying that this definition is not correct because it is not muttarid (excluding what should be excluded). 'And know that the definition is either haqiqi...' Before explaining the previous objection, Sadr al-Shari'ah presents a preface. Its detail is that the essence of a thing consists of the parts from which the thing is composed; if any part is missing, the essence is not realized (from Taysir al-Mantiq). Essence (mahiyya) is of two types: (1) real essence (mahiyya haqiqiyya), (2) conventional essence (mahiyya i'tibariyya). Real essence is that which is not subject to the consideration of any considerer; rather it is realized and established in reality, whether the intellect considers it or not, such as human essence, horse essence, etc. Conventional essence is that which is subject to the consideration of a considerer; it is not established in reality, such as the essence of the word 'asl', the essence of 'fiqh', 'jins', and 'naw'. These are not real essences, but considered by the considerers. In other words, the terminological meaning of a word is called conventional essence. Just as essence has two types, similarly according to the author, definition also has two types: (1) haqiqi definition, (2) i'tibari definition. Haqiqi definition is that which informs about the essence and reality of a thing; in other words, it is the acquisition of the reality of a thing not already present in the perceiving faculty. The 'i'tibari definition is the acquisition of the concept of a thing not already present in the perceiving faculty. For example, the assigner (wadi') considers several composite matters prepared in the mind, and then coins a name for them. Those matters are the subject and the composite parts are the object for which the name is placed. Whenever that name is asked about, the answer will mention that composite meaning. For example, the word 'asl' was coined corresponding to the composite meaning that a thing exists upon which something else is built. Similarly, the word 'fiqh' was coined for specific issues. Similarly, the word 'jins' (genus) was coined as a universal predicated of many differing in reality in answer to 'what is it?'. Similarly, the word 'naw' (species) is a universal... (cut off).
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the actual subject matter of usul al-fiqh. The author, Sadr al-Shari'ah, starts by explaining the definition of 'usul al-fiqh' through two approaches: first, the 'idafi (relational) definition where 'usul' and 'fiqh' are defined separately, and then the haqiqi (real) definition where the composite is taken as the title of a discipline. He then analyzes the word 'asl' (plural: usul). He defines 'asl' as that upon which something else is built, and distinguishes between sensory building (like a wall supporting a roof) and rational building (like evidence supporting a ruling). He then critiques Imam al-Razi's definition from al-Mahsul (that 'asl' is that which is needed by another) because it is not muttarid—it fails to exclude things that are not 'asl'. Finally, the author provides a detailed clarification on the nature of definitions: haqiqi definitions reveal the essence of a thing as it is in reality, while i'tibari definitions create a conceptual composite by convention. Examples are given: 'asl', 'fiqh', 'jins', and 'naw' are conventional definitions coined by scholars. This foundational discussion sets the stage for understanding the terminology of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): that upon which something else is built (ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh)
ابتناء (ibtina'): building upon, foundation; includes both sensory and rational relations
ماہیت (mahiyya): essence or quiddity of a thing; divided into real (haqiqiyya) and conventional (i'tibariyya)
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): a definition that informs about the essence and reality of a thing
تعریف آئی (ta'rif i'tibari): a definition that provides a conceptual composite (conventional) rather than the real essence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Sadr al-Shari'ah reject Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'that which is needed by another'?
A) It is too broad (not muttarid).
B) It is too narrow.
C) It is circular.
D) It is not found in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the precise definition of 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built' is foundational, and any definition failing to include all cases and exclude non-cases (muttarid) is rejected.

Method of Learning
intermediate

Why Definition and Subject Must Precede Study
Commentary establishing a methodological principle and a Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a student must know the definition and subject of any science before studying its details, and evaluate the Hanafi dispute about which definition of uṣūl al-fiqh should be presented first.

Core Idea
Before studying any science, know its definition and subject – or risk losing the goal.

Every science is a set of many issues (masā'il) unified under a single aspect. The student who seeks to master those issues must first grasp that unifying aspect – the science's definition (ta'rīf) and subject (mawḍū'). This lesson unpacks that principle from Taftāzānī's commentary on al-Tawḍīḥ, and then examines a subtle Hanafi ikhtilāf: when defining uṣūl al-fiqh itself, should one give the iḍāfī definition (component by component) or the laqabī definition (as a title)? Two proofs are offered for prioritising the iḍāfī definition.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the general rule (al-dābiṭa)
The author states: whoever seeks many things that all relate to a single aspect must know that aspect first. The example given is a person seeking students of religion; they need a definition (beard, turban, etc.) to distinguish students from merchants. This illustrates the universal principle.
2
Apply the rule to any science
Every science has many issues unified by its definition and subject. Therefore, the student must learn the science's definition and subject before tackling its details. The definition distinguishes the science in the student's mind; the subject distinguishes it in itself from other sciences.
This prevents confusion between intended and unintended knowledge.
3
Identify the two definitions of uṣūl al-fiqh
The term 'uṣūl al-fiqh' can be understood in two ways: (i) as a genitive construction (iḍāfī), requiring separate definition of 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh', and (ii) as a title (laqabī) for the discipline as a whole. Each yields a different definition.
The iḍāfī definition is considered the original; the laqabī definition is transferred from it.
4
Analyse the dispute on order of presentation
Some scholars present the iḍāfī definition first; others present the laqabī first. The author's group (including the author of al-Tawḍīḥ) argues for iḍāfī first using two proofs: (1) the original takes precedence over the transferred, and (2) presenting laqabī first forces a redundant redefinition of fiqh. Understand the arguments and the practical difference (thamarah) in teaching sequence.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilāf within the Hanafi school.

ضرور کرنا پڑے گی پھر اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) تعریف میں لفظ فقہ اور اسکی تعریف دونوں ذکر کی جائیں عبارت یوں ہوگی ھو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها الى الفقه الذي هو معرفة
Detailed: Why is it necessary to explain the subject, and why must we know these two things before the objectives? He states that the principle is: Whoever seeks multiplicity, i.e., wants to seek many things, and those many things are all contained under a single aspect (jiha wāhida), meaning all those things have a connection to one single thing, and that single thing is common among them all, then it is necessary for such a seeker of multiplicity that when he seeks the many things, at the time of seeking he must consider that aspect and know that aspect before seeking the many things and acquire knowledge of it; otherwise there is a risk that he will miss the intended goal and become preoccupied with the unintended, and he will not distinguish between the intended and unintended. For example, a person seeks students of religion; students of religion are many but they are contained under a single aspect. So it is necessary for this person to acquire knowledge of that single aspect. That single aspect will be the definition of these students: that a student is one who studies religion and has a beard, turban, cap, etc. After knowing this single aspect, the seeker of multiplicity will attain his sought and intended, and distinguish the intended from the unintended. If this aspect were not known, then the distinction between intended and unintended, sought and unsought, could not be made. Instead of students of religion, it is possible that the seeker of multiplicity would consider merchants as students of religion and become occupied in serving them; thus the intended would be lost. Since it is established that it is necessary for the seeker of multiplicity to acquire knowledge of the single aspect first, it should also be known that every science consists of many issues, and those many issues are related, contained, and shared under a single aspect, and that single aspect is the definition (ta'rīf) and subject (mawḍū') of that science. Therefore, it is necessary for the student of knowledge that before learning the many issues of any science, he knows its definition and its subject; thus he will be secure and safe from missing the intended and from engaging in the unintended. By knowing the definition of the science, that desired science becomes distinguished from other sciences in the mind of the student, not in itself and in its essence; and by means of the subject, it becomes distinguished in itself and in its essence from other sciences. Hence, before the objectives, it is necessary to know the definition and subject of a science; otherwise seeking the unknown would become necessary, and the distinction between intended and unintended could not be made. Question: In the introduction, three things are mentioned: (1) definition, (2) subject, (3) purpose and goal. From the commentator's phrase, it appears that the author mentioned definition and subject but did not mention purpose and goal. What is the reason? Answer: The purpose is generally known from the definition or from the subject. This is also the case here, because the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh is: 'It is knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh.' From this it is known that the goal of this science is reaching fiqh. For this reason, the author did not mention it separately and independently. Then when the soul of the listener became eagerly desirous—the goal of the commentator Taftāzānī is to explain the text. The author mentioned in the text two syntactical possibilities of 'uṣūl al-fiqh': (1) 'uṣūl al-fiqh' is the predicate of an omitted subject 'hādhihi'; (2) 'uṣūl al-fiqh' is the subject and the sentence is completed with a past tense verb. Taftāzānī, while clarifying the first syntactical possibility, says: When the listener/student knew that the distinction of a science is by its definition and subject, the soul and heart of the student of uṣūl al-fiqh became desirous and awaiting that he would learn the definition of this art so that it would be distinguished from other sciences. But while the listener/student was preparing to ask, the author, before the question, seeing the eagerness of the desirous listener, himself said: 'O this which we have mentioned is uṣūl al-fiqh', and then began the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh so that the listener/student would not need to ask. In other words, the author answered the student's implied question. And 'qāla 'an al-thānī' clarifies the second syntactical possibility: that the author, acting as the representative of the desirous listener, himself asks: 'What is uṣūl al-fiqh?' and then in answer begins its definition: 'wa-uṣūl al-fiqh is a title for this art...' The goal of the commentator Taftāzānī is to explain the text. He says that uṣūl al-fiqh is the title of this particular art; it was transferred from a genitive construction (iḍāfī), meaning originally it was a genitive compound (murakkab iḍāfī), then it was transferred from that and made a title of this art. After the transfer, the composition is not considered. Therefore, there will be two considerations: (1) the consideration of iḍāfa, (2) the consideration of being a title. Hence, there will also be two definitions: one according to the consideration of iḍāfa, i.e., separately for the muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh, and the other according to the consideration of being a title. The first is called the iḍāfī definition, and the second the laqabī definition. 'Some scholars present the laqabī definition first.' The goal of the commentator is to mention the difference of authors. Previously it was known that uṣūl al-fiqh has two definitions: one iḍāfī definition and the other laqabī definition. But authors differ as to which definition should be presented first. Some scholars present the iḍāfī definition first; some present the laqabī definition first. The first group, which includes the author, gives two proofs: (1) The laqabī definition is transferred from the iḍāfī, and the iḍāfī is the original from which it is transferred. The principle is that the original (manqūl 'anhu) takes precedence over the transferred (manqūl). Therefore, the iḍāfī definition should take precedence over the laqabī. (2) The second proof is that if the laqabī definition is presented first, then unnecessary repetition in the definition of fiqh would be required, because the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh is 'It is knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh.' Then fiqh is mentioned in the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh, and the laqabī definition of uṣūl al-fiqh cannot be complete without defining fiqh, because for a complete clarification of the defined term, it is necessary to define its constituent parts; otherwise ignorance in the definition would arise. Therefore, when mentioning the laqabī definition, one must necessarily define fiqh. Then there are two scenarios: (1) In the definition, both the word 'fiqh' and its definition are mentioned; the phrase would be: 'It is knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh, which is knowledge of...'
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharḥ) of al-Tawḍīḥ by Taftāzānī establishes a methodological principle for studying any science. The author begins by stating a general rule: anyone who seeks many things that share a common aspect must first know that aspect. This is illustrated with an example: someone looking for students of religion needs a definition (beard, turban, etc.) to distinguish them from merchants. Similarly, every science has many issues (masā'il) that are unified under a single aspect—its definition (ta'rīf) and subject (mawḍū'). Therefore, before studying the details of a science, the student must learn its definition and subject. The definition distinguishes the science in the student's mind, while the subject distinguishes it in itself from other sciences. This prevents the student from missing the intended goal or becoming preoccupied with irrelevant material. The text then addresses a question: why did the author of al-Tawḍīḥ (al-Maḥbūbī) mention only definition and subject, omitting the purpose (gharaḍ)? The answer is that the purpose is implied in the definition; for uṣūl al-fiqh, the definition 'knowledge of the principles by which one reaches fiqh' already shows that its purpose is to reach fiqh. Next, the commentator discusses the two syntactical possibilities for the phrase 'uṣūl al-fiqh' in the original text. The first takes it as a predicate (khabar) of an omitted subject, treating the statement as a response to a student's unasked question. The second treats it as a subject (mubtada') followed by a predicate, as if the author asks 'What is uṣūl al-fiqh?' and then answers. Both interpretations show the author's pedagogical sensitivity. Finally, the text delves into the nature of the term 'uṣūl al-fiqh' as a title (laqab) transferred from its original genitive construction (iḍāfī). Because it is now a proper name, two definitions are possible: one considering the original iḍāfa (definition of 'uṣūl' and 'fiqh' separately) and one considering it as a title (laqabī). A dispute among scholars arises: which definition should be presented first? The author's group (which includes the author of al-Tawḍīḥ) prefers the iḍāfī definition first, offering two arguments: 1) the original (iḍāfī) takes precedence over the derived (laqabī), and 2) presenting the laqabī first would require repeating the definition of fiqh within the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh, leading to unnecessary redundancy.

Key Terms
اصول الفقه (Uṣūl al-Fiqh): Knowledge of the principles (qawāʿid) by which one reaches fiqh (العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه).
تعریف اضافی (Taʿrīf Iḍāfī): Definition based on the original genitive construction, i.e., defining each part (uṣūl and fiqh) separately.
تعریف لقمی (Taʿrīf Laqabī): Definition considering the term as a title (laqab) for the discipline, without analyzing its parts.
موضوع (Mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science; that by which a science is distinguished in itself from other sciences (تمتاز به فی حد ذاتها وفی نفسها عن باقی العلوم).
غرض و غایت (Gharad wa Ghāyah): The purpose and goal of a science; for uṣūl al-fiqh it is reaching fiqh (التوصل إلى الفقه).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author of al-Tawḍīḥ not mention the purpose (gharaḍ) of uṣūl al-fiqh separately?
A) He considered it unnecessary to state the purpose at all.
B) The purpose is derived from the definition of uṣūl al-fiqh itself.
C) He forgot to include it in the introduction.
D) He discussed the purpose later in the chapter.

Key Takeaway
Before studying any science, the student must first know its definition and subject; for uṣūl al-fiqh, the iḍāfī definition is favoured to start with due to its originality and to avoid redundancy.

Method of Learning
beginner
8 min
Three Types of Definition and Conditions of Real Definition
Classifying definitions and setting conditions for real definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal, descriptive, and real definitions and list the five conditions for a valid real definition.

Core Idea
Real definition reveals essence through genus and differentia; mere synonyms are not enough.

In this lesson, we explore the classical classification of definitions as presented by the scholars of usul. Understanding these types is foundational for precise legal reasoning, as definitions set the terms for debate and derivation. We will also examine the five conditions that a real definition must satisfy to be complete and effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of definition
Read the passage and list the three types: verbal (lafzi), descriptive (rasmi), and real (haqiqi). Understand what each type offers in explaining a thing.
Verbal definition uses a synonymous word; descriptive uses a distinctive property; real uses genus and differentia.
2
Understand the distinctions between them
Compare the examples given for each type. Note that verbal definitions are merely synonyms, descriptive definitions pick a unique feature, and real definitions capture the essence.
The example for real definition of man is 'a body that grows, moves by will, and is rational'.
3
Memorize the five conditions of real definition
From the list, commit to memory: (1) include all essential parts, (2) general precedes specific, (3) proximate genus over remote, (4) avoid strange words, (5) avoid ambiguous terms.
These conditions ensure the definition is complete, ordered, and clear.
