Misk al-Maleeh
and al-Alawi
Sharh al-
The author is explaining his phrase: that the term 'qawa'id' in the definition refers to universal propositions which lead to fiqh, and their leading to fiqh is close, called 'close leading'. The meaning is that those universal propositions lead to fiqh directly without any intermediary. 'And we only said' from the author explains the benefit of 'close leading': this qualification is made so that other sciences which are of the rank of principles, like Arabic sciences (sarf, nahw, lugha, ma'ani wa bayan, badi', and kalam) are excluded from the definition, even though they also lead to fiqh, but not close leading (i.e., without intermediary) but indirectly. 'And our saying: on the basis of verification' explains the benefit of the second qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq': that it is intended to exclude the science of khilaf and jadal, even though in the science of khilaf such universal propositions exist that are conductive to the issues of fiqh and the leading is also close, but it is not on the basis of verification nor intended per se; rather, the purpose is to rearrange the opponent's proofs and through them establish an objection against the opponent. So the main purpose and intention is this objection; if proof of fiqh occurs it is incidental. And such rules are mentioned in Irshad and the book Muqaddimah so that disputed issues can be based on them. 'And we mean by universal propositions, etc.' The author says: In the definition of usul al-fiqh, by the term 'qawa'id' universal propositions were intended. Not every type of universal proposition is meant, but those propositions by which evidence is established for the issues of fiqh in the form of a syllogism, becoming one of the two premises, i.e., the major premise. These very propositions that become the major of the proof—their knowledge is called usul al-fiqh, and it is these that are mentioned in usul al-fiqh. 'That is, when you infer from the rules leading to the issues of fiqh, etc.' He further explains: When a ruling of fiqh is inferred using the first figure, the two propositions in the first figure will either be in the form of conjunctive qiyas or exceptive qiyas. If the two propositions are in the form of conjunctive qiyas, then whichever of the two becomes the major will be from among those universal propositions mentioned in usul al-fiqh. For example: 'This ruling is established' is the claim. Its proof in the first figure in the form of qiyas is presented as: 'Because it is a ruling that indicates its establishment by qiyas' (minor) and 'Every ruling that indicates its establishment by qiyas is established' (major). This major is the proof of the claim, and this major is that universal proposition which is mentioned in usul al-fiqh, and this is called usul al-fiqh. And if the inference is in the form of exceptive qiyas (universal concomitants), where the existence of the desired thing establishes the existence of the necessary thing, then this universal concomitant (called 'universal concomitant' meaning the mutual entailment between antecedent and consequent) will be among those propositions mentioned in usul al-fiqh. For example, one says: 'This ruling is established' is the claim. Its proof in the form of a universal concomitant is presented as: 'Because whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, this ruling is established; but qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling; therefore this ruling is established.' So the conclusion is: because when the exception is exactly the antecedent, the conclusion is exactly the consequent. So in this form, the universal concomitant 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of a ruling, the ruling is established' is that universal proposition which is mentioned in usul al-fiqh. 'And know that it is possible that this universal proposition itself...' With this phrase the author answers a doubt. The statement of the doubt is: You said that in conjunctive qiyas, the universal proposition which becomes the major is mentioned and ready in usul al-fiqh, and its knowledge is usul al-fiqh. Similarly in exceptive qiyas, the proposition in the form of concomitant is also ready in usul al-fiqh and mentioned therein. Yet sometimes the universal proposition that is the major or the universal concomitant is not mentioned at all in usul al-fiqh. For example: 'This action is obligatory because it indicates obligation by qiyas, and every action that indicates obligation by qiyas is obligatory.' Now this major is nowhere mentioned in usul al-fiqh. So how can it be called usul al-fiqh, and how is it correct to say that this universal proposition (major) is ready in usul al-fiqh? Answer! The author replies that these universal propositions are mentioned in usul al-fiqh in two ways: (1) Sometimes the universal proposition that occurs as the major or the universal concomitant is mentioned explicitly in usul al-fiqh. (2) Sometimes it is not mentioned explicitly, but it enters usul al-fiqh implicitly within and under another universal proposition. Therefore it is correct to say that it is included in usul al-fiqh and mentioned in it. For example, the universal proposition: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation in a case of dispute, obligation is established.' (The qualification 'in a case of dispute' is accidental and irrelevant because qiyas only occurs in cases of dispute.) This universal concomitant is not explicitly present in usul al-fiqh. However, it is included in another universal proposition that is broader and is explicitly mentioned in usul al-fiqh, namely: 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling that has this nature, the ruling is established.' (The phrase 'this nature' refers to the conditions of the ruling.) Now the first universal concomitant ('Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established') is included in this universal proposition because the phrase 'any ruling' encompasses all its types, including obligation, recommendation, etc. So the first universal proposition that mentioned obligation is included in this general 'any ruling'. It is as if instead of 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling that has this nature' it was said: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established; whenever qiyas indicates recommendation, recommendation is established; whenever qiyas indicates prohibition, prohibition is established, etc.' All these propositions are individuals of this universal proposition, therefore they are included in it. So we say that this qiyas (universal concomitant) that occurs as the major in the two premises of the proof is mentioned in usul al-fiqh implicitly (bi-tariq al-tadamun). Thus the doubt is repelled.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the definition of usul al-fiqh, focusing on the term 'qadaya kulliya' (universal propositions). The commentator clarifies that the word 'qawa'id' in the definition refers specifically to universal propositions that directly lead to fiqh rulings (tasil qarib). This excludes auxiliary sciences like Arabic grammar and rhetoric, which lead to fiqh only indirectly. The second qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' excludes polemical sciences (khilaf and jadal), where universal propositions are used not to establish fiqh per se but to refute opponents. The core idea is that usul al-fiqh consists of those universal propositions that serve as the major premise (kubra) in a syllogism (qiyas) of the first figure, either conjunctive (iqtirani) or exceptive (istithna'i). The commentator then addresses a potential objection: not all such universal propositions are explicitly found in usul al-fiqh texts. The answer is that they may be included implicitly under broader principles. For example, a specific proposition like 'Qiyas indicating obligation establishes obligation' is not stated verbatim but is contained within the general principle 'Qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling.' Thus, all specific applications are considered part of usul al-fiqh by implication (bi-tariq al-tadamun). This reasoning ensures that usul al-fiqh provides the theoretical foundation for all qiyas-based ijtihad.

Key Terms
قضية كلية (qadiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as the major premise (kubra) in a qiyas, or as a universal concomitant in exceptive qiyas, and is used to derive fiqh rulings.
توصل قريب (tawassul qarib): Direct leading to fiqh rulings without intermediary, as opposed to indirect leading through other sciences.
قياس اقتراني (qiyas iqtirani): Conjunctive syllogism where the premises are joined by implication, producing a conclusion.
قياس استثنائي (qiyas istithna'i): Exceptive syllogism where one premise is a conditional and the other is the affirmation or negation of one part.
ملازمة كلية (mulazama kulliyya): A universal conditional proposition stating that whenever the antecedent holds, the consequent holds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' in the definition?
A) To include Arabic sciences
B) To exclude polemical sciences like khilaf and jadal
C) To ensure direct leading to fiqh
D) To define universal propositions

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is defined as the universal propositions that directly lead to fiqh rulings and are used for verification, serving as major premises in qiyas.

Qiyas in Usul al-Fiqh: Forms and Implicit Inclusion of Propositions
Explaining how specific universal propositions are implicitly part of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conjunctive (iqtirani) and exceptive (istithna'i) qiyas as used in usul al-fiqh, and explain how specific universal propositions are implicitly included under broader ones.

Core Idea
Even if a specific universal proposition is not explicitly in usul al-fiqh, it is included implicitly under a broader principle.

This part of the passage addresses a practical objection: not every universal proposition that appears in reasoning is explicitly found in usul texts. The commentator explains that they are contained within general principles. He illustrates with the example of obligation: the specific proposition 'qiyas indicating obligation establishes obligation' is an instance of the general principle 'qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling.'

Guided Path
1
Understand the two forms of qiyas
The passage explains conjunctive (iqtirani) and exceptive (istithna'i) qiyas, each using universal propositions as major.
2
Identify the doubt
The objector says that specific majors like 'every ruling indicating obligation by qiyas is obligatory' are not in usul books.
3
Apply the commentator's solution
Recognize that such specific propositions are individuals (afrad) of a more general principle.
4
Learn the term 'tadamun'
Implicit inclusion means the specific is covered under the general.

القياس على ثبوت هذا الحكم يكون بذا الحكم ثابتا لكن القياس دال على ثبوت هذا الحكم فيكون هذا
الحکم ثابتا فیکون هذا الحکم ثابتا نتیجہ ہے کیونکہ جب استثناء عین مقدم ہو تو نتیجہ عین تالی ہوتا ہے تو اس شکل میں جو ملازمہ کلیہ ہے كلما دل القياس على ثبوت الحكم يكون الحکم ثابتا یہی وہ قضیہ کلیہ ہے جو اصول فقہ میں مذکور ہوتا ہے۔ واعلم انه يمكن ان لا يكون هذا القضية الكلية بعينها الخ اس عبارت سے مصنف ایک شبہ کا جواب دے رہے ہیں شبہ کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ آپ نے یہ کہا ہے کہ قیاس اقترانی میں قضیہ کلیہ کا جو کبری ہوتا ہے وہ اصول فقہ میں مذکور اور تیار ہوتا ہے اور اس کا علم اصول فقہ ہے اسی طرح قیاس استثنائی میں جو قفہ یہ ملازمہ کی صورت میں ہوتا ہے وہ بھی اصول فقہ میں تیار ہوتا ہے اور اسی میں مذکور ہوتا ہے حالانکہ بسا اثبات قنہ کلیہ کا کبری یا ملازمہ کلیہ اصول فقہ میں بالکل مذکور ہی نہیں ہوتا مثلا هذا الحلم واجب لانہ یدل علی وجو به القیاس و کل حجم یدل علی و بنو به القیاس فوجد واجب اب یہ کبری اصول فقہ میں کہیں بھی مذکور نہیں ہے تو اس کو اصول فقہ کیسے کہا جائے گا اور یہ کہنا کیسے درست ہو گا کہ یہ قضیہ کلیہ (کبری ) اصول فقہ میں تیار ہوا ہے جواب ! مصنف جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ان قضیا یا کلیہ کے اصول فقہ میں مذکور ہونے کی دو صورتیں ہیں (1) کبھی تو قضیہ کلیہ جوشکل میں کبری واقع ہورہا ہے یا ملازمہ کلیہ ہے بعینھا اصول فقہ میں مذکور ہوگا اور کبھی بعینها اصول فقہ میں مذکور نہیں ہوگا لیکن ضمناً کسی اور قضیہ کلیہ کے ضمن میں اور اس کے تحت میں درج ہو کر اصول فقہ میں داخل ہونگے لہذا اس کے حق میں بھی یہ کہنا صحیح ہے کہ وہ اصول فقہ میں داخل ہے اور اس میں مذکور ہے مثلا یہ قضیہ کلیہ ہے کلمادل القياس على الوجوب في صورة النزاع يثبت الوجوب ( فى صورة النزاع کی قید اتفاقی ہے اس کو مقصود سے کوئی تعلق نہیں ہے کیونکہ قیاس ہوتا ہی صورۃ نزاعی میں ہے یہ ملازمہ کلیہ بعینہ اصول فقہ میں موجود نہیں ہے البتہ یہ ایک، اور قضیہ کلیہ میں مندرج ہے جو اس سے بڑا ہے اور وہ بعینہ اصول فقہ میں مذکور ہے وہ یہ ہے كلما دل القياس على ثبوت كل حكم هذا شانه يثبت الحکم (هذا شانہ سے حکم کی شرائط کی طرف اشارہ ہے ) اب پہلا ملازمہ کلیہ ( کلمادل القياس على الوجوب مثبت الوجوب ) اس قضیہ کلیہ میں مندرج ہے کیونکہ اس قضیہ کلیہ میں کل حکم کا لفظ ہے اور یہ لفظ حکم اپنی جمیع اقسام وجوب ندب وغیرہ کو شامل ہے تو پہلے والا قضیہ کلیہ جس میں وجوب مذکور تھا وہ بھی اسی کل حکم میں داخل ہو جائے گا گویا كلما دل القياس على ثبوت كل حكم هذا شانہ کی بجائے یہ کہا گیا کلما دل القیاس علی الوجوب يثبت الوجوب - وكلما دل القياس على الندب يثبت الندب وكلما دل القياس على الحرمة يثبت الحرمة وغیرہ یہ سب قضایا اسی قضیہ کلیہ کے افراد ہیں اس لئے اس میں داخل ہو نگے لہذا اس وقت یوں کہیں گے کہ یہ قیاس ( ملازمہ کلیہ ) جو دلیل کے دو مقدموں میں کبری واقع ہو رہا ہے یہ اصول فقہ میں بطریق تضمن مذکور ہے تو اشکال دفع ہو گیا۔
Misk al-Maleeh
and al-Alawi
Sharh al-
The author is explaining his phrase: that the term 'qawa'id' in the definition refers to universal propositions which lead to fiqh, and their leading to fiqh is close, called 'close leading'. The meaning is that those universal propositions lead to fiqh directly without any intermediary. 'And we only said' from the author explains the benefit of 'close leading': this qualification is made so that other sciences which are of the rank of principles, like Arabic sciences (sarf, nahw, lugha, ma'ani wa bayan, badi', and kalam) are excluded from the definition, even though they also lead to fiqh, but not close leading (i.e., without intermediary) but indirectly. 'And our saying: on the basis of verification' explains the benefit of the second qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq': that it is intended to exclude the science of khilaf and jadal, even though in the science of khilaf such universal propositions exist that are conductive to the issues of fiqh and the leading is also close, but it is not on the basis of verification nor intended per se; rather, the purpose is to rearrange the opponent's proofs and through them establish an objection against the opponent. So the main purpose and intention is this objection; if proof of fiqh occurs it is incidental. And such rules are mentioned in Irshad and the book Muqaddimah so that disputed issues can be based on them. 'And we mean by universal propositions, etc.' The author says: In the definition of usul al-fiqh, by the term 'qawa'id' universal propositions were intended. Not every type of universal proposition is meant, but those propositions by which evidence is established for the issues of fiqh in the form of a syllogism, becoming one of the two premises, i.e., the major premise. These very propositions that become the major of the proof—their knowledge is called usul al-fiqh, and it is these that are mentioned in usul al-fiqh. 'That is, when you infer from the rules leading to the issues of fiqh, etc.' He further explains: When a ruling of fiqh is inferred using the first figure, the two propositions in the first figure will either be in the form of conjunctive qiyas or exceptive qiyas. If the two propositions are in the form of conjunctive qiyas, then whichever of the two becomes the major will be from among those universal propositions mentioned in usul al-fiqh. For example: 'This ruling is established' is the claim. Its proof in the first figure in the form of qiyas is presented as: 'Because it is a ruling that indicates its establishment by qiyas' (minor) and 'Every ruling that indicates its establishment by qiyas is established' (major). This major is the proof of the claim, and this major is that universal proposition which is mentioned in usul al-fiqh, and this is called usul al-fiqh. And if the inference is in the form of exceptive qiyas (universal concomitants), where the existence of the desired thing establishes the existence of the necessary thing, then this universal concomitant (called 'universal concomitant' meaning the mutual entailment between antecedent and consequent) will be among those propositions mentioned in usul al-fiqh. For example, one says: 'This ruling is established' is the claim. Its proof in the form of a universal concomitant is presented as: 'Because whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling, this ruling is established; but qiyas indicates the establishment of this ruling; therefore this ruling is established.' So the conclusion is: because when the exception is exactly the antecedent, the conclusion is exactly the consequent. So in this form, the universal concomitant 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of a ruling, the ruling is established' is that universal proposition which is mentioned in usul al-fiqh. 'And know that it is possible that this universal proposition itself...' With this phrase the author answers a doubt. The statement of the doubt is: You said that in conjunctive qiyas, the universal proposition which becomes the major is mentioned and ready in usul al-fiqh, and its knowledge is usul al-fiqh. Similarly in exceptive qiyas, the proposition in the form of concomitant is also ready in usul al-fiqh and mentioned therein. Yet sometimes the universal proposition that is the major or the universal concomitant is not mentioned at all in usul al-fiqh. For example: 'This action is obligatory because it indicates obligation by qiyas, and every action that indicates obligation by qiyas is obligatory.' Now this major is nowhere mentioned in usul al-fiqh. So how can it be called usul al-fiqh, and how is it correct to say that this universal proposition (major) is ready in usul al-fiqh? Answer! The author replies that these universal propositions are mentioned in usul al-fiqh in two ways: (1) Sometimes the universal proposition that occurs as the major or the universal concomitant is mentioned explicitly in usul al-fiqh. (2) Sometimes it is not mentioned explicitly, but it enters usul al-fiqh implicitly within and under another universal proposition. Therefore it is correct to say that it is included in usul al-fiqh and mentioned in it. For example, the universal proposition: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation in a case of dispute, obligation is established.' (The qualification 'in a case of dispute' is accidental and irrelevant because qiyas only occurs in cases of dispute.) This universal concomitant is not explicitly present in usul al-fiqh. However, it is included in another universal proposition that is broader and is explicitly mentioned in usul al-fiqh, namely: 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling that has this nature, the ruling is established.' (The phrase 'this nature' refers to the conditions of the ruling.) Now the first universal concomitant ('Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established') is included in this universal proposition because the phrase 'any ruling' encompasses all its types, including obligation, recommendation, etc. So the first universal proposition that mentioned obligation is included in this general 'any ruling'. It is as if instead of 'Whenever qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling that has this nature' it was said: 'Whenever qiyas indicates obligation, obligation is established; whenever qiyas indicates recommendation, recommendation is established; whenever qiyas indicates prohibition, prohibition is established, etc.' All these propositions are individuals of this universal proposition, therefore they are included in it. So we say that this qiyas (universal concomitant) that occurs as the major in the two premises of the proof is mentioned in usul al-fiqh implicitly (bi-tariq al-tadamun). Thus the doubt is repelled.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the definition of usul al-fiqh, focusing on the term 'qadaya kulliya' (universal propositions). The commentator clarifies that the word 'qawa'id' in the definition refers specifically to universal propositions that directly lead to fiqh rulings (tasil qarib). This excludes auxiliary sciences like Arabic grammar and rhetoric, which lead to fiqh only indirectly. The second qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' excludes polemical sciences (khilaf and jadal), where universal propositions are used not to establish fiqh per se but to refute opponents. The core idea is that usul al-fiqh consists of those universal propositions that serve as the major premise (kubra) in a syllogism (qiyas) of the first figure, either conjunctive (iqtirani) or exceptive (istithna'i). The commentator then addresses a potential objection: not all such universal propositions are explicitly found in usul al-fiqh texts. The answer is that they may be included implicitly under broader principles. For example, a specific proposition like 'Qiyas indicating obligation establishes obligation' is not stated verbatim but is contained within the general principle 'Qiyas indicates the establishment of any ruling.' Thus, all specific applications are considered part of usul al-fiqh by implication (bi-tariq al-tadamun). This reasoning ensures that usul al-fiqh provides the theoretical foundation for all qiyas-based ijtihad.

Key Terms
قضية كلية (qadiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as the major premise (kubra) in a qiyas, or as a universal concomitant in exceptive qiyas, and is used to derive fiqh rulings.
توصل قريب (tawassul qarib): Direct leading to fiqh rulings without intermediary, as opposed to indirect leading through other sciences.
قياس اقتراني (qiyas iqtirani): Conjunctive syllogism where the premises are joined by implication, producing a conclusion.
قياس استثنائي (qiyas istithna'i): Exceptive syllogism where one premise is a conditional and the other is the affirmation or negation of one part.
ملازمة كلية (mulazama kulliyya): A universal conditional proposition stating that whenever the antecedent holds, the consequent holds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the specific universal proposition 'Qiyas indicating obligation establishes obligation' considered part of usul al-fiqh?
A) It is explicitly stated in all usul books
B) It is included implicitly under a broader principle
C) It is derived from the Quran
D) It is a matter of ijma

Key Takeaway
Specific universal propositions used in qiyas are considered part of usul al-fiqh by implicit inclusion under more general principles.

Method of Learning
beginner
6 min
Definition of Qa'ida in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Definition of qa'ida with example and prior objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qa'ida, identify its condition of universality, and apply it to derive a ruling for a particular case.

Core Idea
A qa'ida is a universal ruling that covers all its particulars, enabling derivation of their rulings when needed.

In this passage, the commentator first addresses an objection about the phrase 'ilm usul al-fiqh' and then provides a precise definition of qa'ida. Understanding this definition is foundational for grasping how Hanafi usul al-fiqh uses general principles to derive specific fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its defense
The passage begins by noting that 'ilm usul al-fiqh' might seem redundant since usul al-fiqh itself is a science. The commentator defends the usage as a clarification, analogous to 'shajarat al-arak'.
This section sets up the need for precise definitions.
2
Define qa'ida
Qa'ida is defined as a universal ruling (حكم كلي) that applies and is true for all its particulars. It must be general, not specific.
The key condition is that it covers every particular under it.
3
Understand the condition of universality
The qa'ida must logically encompass all its particulars. If even one particular is excluded, it ceases to be a qa'ida.
This distinguishes qa'ida from a specific ruling.
4
Work through the example
The commentator gives the example: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.' This is a qa'ida. Then, for a particular ruling, one can say: 'This ruling, qiyas indicates it, and every ruling that qiyas indicates is established, therefore this ruling is established.'
The example shows the logical syllogism (قياس) used to derive the particular from the general.
5
Recognize the utility
Qa'ida allows deriving rulings for new cases that fall under it, avoiding the need for separate evidence for each particular.
This efficiency is central to usul al-fiqh.

مصنف کی طرف سے اعتذار پیش کر رہے ہیں کہ یہاں اضافت کی حاجت تو نہیں تھی لیکن صرف بیان اور زیادہ وضاحت کیلئے علم کی اضافت الی اصول الفقہ کر دی گئی ہے جیسے شجرة الاراک میں شجرہ کی اضافت الی الاراک توضیح کیلئے ہے ور نہ اراک بھی ایک شجرہ ہے والقاعدۃ حکم کی غرض تعریف قاعدہ! القواعد قاعدۃ کی جمع ہے شارح قاعدہ کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں کہ قاعدہ وہ حکم ہے جو اپنے جمیع جزئیات پر منطبق اور صادق آئے تاکہ بوقت ضرورت اس حکم کلی سے جزئیات کے احکام کی معرفت حاصل کی جاسکے مثلاً کل حکم دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت یہ قاعدہ ہے اس کے ذریعہ سے جمیع احکام قیاسی کا ثبوت حاصل کیا جاسکتا ہے مثلا یوں کہا جائے گا ھذالحکم دل علیہ القیاس و کل حکم دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت تو نتیجہ نکل گا هذا الحكم ثابت والتوصل القريب مستفاد من الباء غرض جواب سوال سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے توصل سے توصل قریب مراد لیا ہے اس پر آپ کے پاس کیا دلیل ہے۔ جواب! شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ہمارے پاس دو دلیلیں ہیں (1) توصل بالباء میں باء سبب ہے اور سبب کی دو قسمیں ہیں سبب قریب اور سبب بعید اصل سبب قریب ہوتا ہے وہی متبادر الی الذہن ہوتا ہے لہذا توصل قریب مراد ہوگا (۲) دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں توصل منسوب و مضاف الی الفقہ ہے اور براہ راست فقہ تک توصل توصل قریب کے ساتھ ہی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ توصل بعید میں فقہ تک توصل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ پہلے توصل الی الواسطہ ہوتا ہے پھر واسطہ سے توصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے انہی دو دلیلوں کے تحت یہاں توصل سے توصل قریب مراد لیا گیا۔ فيخرج العلم بقواعد العربيه الخ اس عبارت میں شارح کچھ تفصیل کے ساتھ توصل قریب کا فائدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اس قید سے علم بقواعد العربیہ اور علم کلام خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ یہ مبادی اصول فقہ میں سے ہیں اور ان کے ساتھ توصل الی الفقہ توصل قریب نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے ذریعہ سے توصل الی الواسطہ (توصل بعید) ہوتا ہے پھر واسطہ سے توصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے مثلاً قواعد عربیہ سے اولا الفاظ کی جو اپنے مدلولات وضعیہ و لغویہ پر دلالت ہوتی ہے اس کی کیفیت معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ یہ کونسی دلالت ہے مطابقی ہے یا ضمنی یا التزامی پھر اس واسطہ سے کتاب و سنت سے احکام کے استنباط پر قدرت حاصل ہوتی ہے تو علم عربیت سے توصل ہوا ہے الفاظ کے مدلولات کی کیفیت کی معرفت کی طرف پھر اس کے بعد توصل ہوا ہے الی الاستنباط والفقہ تو درمیان میں واسطہ آ گیا اس لیے اس کو توصل بعید کہا جائے گا اسی طرح قواعد کلام سے اولا کتاب و سنت کا
His statement: 'after it has been established that usul al-fiqh...' An objection enters: The objection is that in previous pages it has passed that usul al-fiqh is the name of a specific science, so the meaning of being a science is understood from that itself. Therefore, the author's adding 'ilm' to usul al-fiqh is not correct; the phrase would become 'the science of science', which is mere repetition. It would have been sufficient to say 'usul al-fiqh is a science'. Apology! He offers an apology on behalf of the author: There was no need for the idafa here, but for the sake of expression and greater clarity, the idafa of 'ilm to usul al-fiqh was made, just as in 'shajarat al-arak' the idafa of shajara to al-arak is for clarification, otherwise al-arak is also a tree. And al-qa'ida: The purpose is definition of qa'ida. Al-qawa'id is the plural of qa'ida. The commentator is defining qa'ida: 'Qa'ida is a ruling that applies and is true for all its particulars so that when needed, knowledge of the rulings of the particulars can be obtained from this universal ruling.' For example: 'Every ruling that qiyas indicates is established' is a qa'ida. Through it, the establishment of all analogical rulings can be obtained. For example, it will be said: 'This ruling, qiyas indicates it, and every ruling that qiyas indicates is established.' So the conclusion is: 'This ruling is established.' And 'al-tawassul al-qareeb' is derived from the ba'? The purpose is answer to a question. The question is: You have taken 'tawassul' to mean 'tawassul qareeb' (direct means). What evidence do you have for this? Answer! The commentator is responding: We have two proofs: (1) In 'tawassul bil-ba'' the ba' is sababiyya (causal), and cause is of two types: near cause and distant cause. The original cause is the near cause, and that is what immediately comes to mind. Therefore, tawassul qareeb is intended. (2) The second proof is that here 'tawassul' is attributed and added to 'fiqh', and reaching fiqh directly is only possible through tawassul qareeb, because in tawassul ba'eed, one does not reach fiqh directly, but first reaches an intermediary, then through the intermediary reaches fiqh. Based on these two proofs, tawassul here is taken to mean tawassul qareeb. So knowledge of Arabic grammar and theology are excluded... In this expression, the commentator explains in some detail the benefit of tawassul qareeb: that this exclusion removes knowledge of Arabic grammar and theology because these are among the preliminaries of usul al-fiqh, and reaching fiqh through them is not tawassul qareeb; rather, through them one reaches an intermediary (tawassul ba'eed), then through the intermediary reaches fiqh. For example, from Arabic grammar, first the quality of how words indicate their conventional and linguistic meanings is known – whether it is by way of correspondence, inclusion, or implication. Then through this intermediary, one gains ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. So grammar provides tawassul to the knowledge of the quality of word meanings, and then subsequently tawassul occurs to derivation and fiqh. Thus an intermediary comes in between, so it is called tawassul ba'eed. Similarly, from theology first the Book and Sunnah are... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing an objection about the phrase 'علم اصول الفقه' (the science of usul al-fiqh). The objection says that since usul al-fiqh itself denotes a science, adding 'ilm' is redundant ('science of science'). The defender responds that the addition is for clarification, like saying 'شجرة الأراك' (the arak tree) even though arak is itself a tree. Then the commentator defines 'qa'ida' as a universal ruling that covers all its particulars, enabling derivation of their rulings when needed. He gives the example: 'كل حكم دل عليه القياس فهو ثابت' (every ruling indicated by qiyas is established). Next, the passage discusses the meaning of 'tawassul' in the definition of usul al-fiqh. Two proofs are given that it means 'tawassul qareeb' (direct means): (1) the ba' in 'tawassul bil-ba'' is sababiyya, and the immediate cause is what is understood; (2) 'tawassul' is added to 'fiqh' directly, implying direct access. Finally, the passage explains that this excludes auxiliary sciences like Arabic grammar and theology (kalam) because they are only preliminaries (mabadi) and provide indirect means (tawassul ba'eed) by first reaching an intermediary before fiqh. The example of grammar shows that one learns how words convey meanings, then uses that to derive fiqh rulings, making grammar an intermediary.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'ida): A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, used to derive their rulings.
توصل قريب (tawassul qareeb): Direct means of reaching fiqh rulings without intermediate steps.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition for something to be a qa'ida?
A) It must be derived from Quran or Sunnah.
B) It must apply to all its particulars.
C) It must be a single fiqh ruling.
D) It must be agreed upon by all schools.

Key Takeaway
A qa'ida is a universal ruling that covers all its particulars, enabling efficient derivation of fiqh rulings through syllogistic reasoning.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Tawassul Qareeb: The Direct Means to Fiqh
Explanation of tawassul qareeb with proofs and exclusion of auxiliary sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two proofs that 'tawassul' in usul al-fiqh refers to direct means (tawassul qareeb) and distinguish between direct and indirect means using the examples of grammar and theology.

Core Idea
Tawassul in usul al-fiqh is direct (qareeb), meaning it gives immediate access to fiqh without intermediaries.

After defining qa'ida, the commentator addresses a question about the term 'tawassul' in the definition of usul al-fiqh. Is it direct or indirect? Two proofs are provided to show it is direct (tawassul qareeb), which then excludes auxiliary sciences that provide only indirect access.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question about tawassul
The implicit question: why is 'tawassul' interpreted as direct means? The commentator anticipates this query and provides evidence.
This step sets up the reasoning.
2
First proof: the ba' is sababiyya
In 'tawassul bil-ba'' (or similar), the ba' indicates causation. The direct cause (sabab qareeb) is what immediately comes to mind. Therefore, tawassul here means direct means.
This relies on linguistic usage: the default interpretation of sabab is the immediate cause.
3
Second proof: idafa to fiqh
'Tawassul' is in idafa (construct) to 'fiqh', implying direct relation. If it were indirect, it would be added to the intermediary, not to fiqh.
The idafa signals a direct link.
4
Exclusion of auxiliary sciences
Because tawassul is direct, auxiliaries like Arabic grammar and theology (kalam) are excluded. They are only preliminaries (mabadi) that provide indirect means (tawassul ba'eed) through an intermediary.
This clarifies the scope of usul al-fiqh.
5
Example with Arabic grammar
From grammar, one first learns how words convey meanings (intermediary), then uses that to derive fiqh from texts. This two-step process is tawassul ba'eed, not qareeb.
The example solidifies the distinction.

Source Text

Definition of Qa'ida in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Definition of qa'ida within the commentary's expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'qa'ida' (general rule) in Hanafi usul and distinguish it from a specific fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
A qa'ida is a general ruling that applies to all its particulars, enabling derivation of fiqh rulings.

Usul al-fiqh relies on general principles (qawa'id) to derive rulings for new cases. In this passage, the commentator explains what constitutes a qa'ida, giving a clear definition and an example. Understanding this definition is essential for grasping how Hanafi scholars use usul to derive fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The commentator defines 'al-qa'ida'. Note its plural 'qawa'id'. Recognize that it is a singular feminine noun denoting a principle.
The term appears in the context of defining usul al-fiqh itself.
2
Analyze the definition
The definition states it is a 'ḥukm kullī' (general ruling). 'Kullī' means it applies to every particular that falls under it. Contrast with a 'ḥukm juz'ī' (specific ruling).
General does not mean vague; it means inclusive of all instances.
3
Consider the purpose
The purpose of a qa'ida is to obtain knowledge of rulings of particulars from this general ruling when needed. It is a tool for istinbat (derivation).
This makes qawa'id methodological, not substantive.
4
Study the example
The example: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.' Apply it: if we know a particular ruling is indicated by qiyas, we can conclude it is established by that qa'ida.
The example shows how a qa'ida functions as a major premise in a syllogism.

ہر عمل سے کوئی نہ کوئی حکم متعلق ہوتا ہے تو اس سے ہمیں چند قضایا حاصل ہو گئے ان کا موضوع افعال مکلفین میں سے کوئی فعل ہو گا اور محمول ا کام شرع میں سے کوئی حکم ( تفصیلی احکام ) ہوگا مثلا الصلوۃ واجبہ، انج واجب ، الزنا حرام وغیرہ پھر ان قضایا کا جوعلم ادلہ سے حاصل ہو گا اس کا نام علم الفقہ ہے۔ یہاں تک تو حاجت الی الفقہ کا بیان تھا آگے حاجت الی اصول الفقہ کا بیان ہے پھر فقہاء نے اولہ اور احکام میں غور و فکر کیا ان کی تفاصیل میں گئے اور ان میں تقسیم کی تو ادلہ کا رجوع اقسام اربعہ کی طرف ہوا کتاب ستہ اجماع، قیاس اور احکام کا رجوع اقسام ستہ کی طرف ہوا وجوب ندب اباحت حرمت کراہت وغیرہ پھر فقہاء نے ان ادلہ سے جو احکام پر استدلال کیا جاتا ہے اس استدلال کی کیفیت میں تامل کیا بشر طیکہ وہ استدلال اجمانی ہو مع قطع النظر عن التفصیل پھر ان کو اور قضایا کلیہ حاصل ہو گئے جو استدلال اجمالی کی کیفیت سے متعلق تھے من غير تفصيل الاعلى ارادة المثال مثلاً یوں کہا جائے الامر للوجوب پھر اس کی تفصیل بطور مثال بیان کی جائے الصلوہ واجبہ لقولہ تعالی واقیمو الصلوۃ اسی طرح ان کو قضایا کلیہ حاصل ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ وہ شراکا اور طرق بھی معلوم ہو گئے جن کے ذریعہ سے ان قضایا کو اسنباط احکام کیلئے وسیلہ اور ذریعہ بنایا جا سکے لہذا انہوں نے ان قضایا کو بمع طرق و شرائط ضبط اور مدون کیا اور ان کے ساتھ مزید لواحق و متممات کا بھی اضافہ کر دیا اور مناسب اختلافات کو ذکر کر دیا اور اس سب مجموعہ کا نام اصول فقہ رکھد یا تو اصول فقہ نام ہو گیا ان قواعد قضایا کلیہ کا جو موصل الی الفقہ ہوں شارح و لفظ القواعدہ سے وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ ہم نے استدلال کے ساتھ جوا جمال کی قید لگائی ہے لفظ قواعد اس پر دال ہے کیونکہ قواعد میں اجمال ہی ہوتا ہے وزاد المصنف قيد التحقیق سے علی وجد اتحقیق کی قید کا فائدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اس سے علم الجدل والخلاف نے احتر از مقصود ہے کما مر تفصیلہ فی توضیح المتن - ولقائل ان يمنع كون قواعده غرض شارح اعتراض علی المصنف ! اعتراض یہ ہے کہ قید علی وجہ اتحقیق مستدرک اور بے کار ہے کیونکہ اس سے علم الخلاف (علم مناظرہ) کو خارج کرنا مقصود ہے اور وہ بتوصل بھا الی الفقہ سے خارج ہو چکا ہے کیونکہ قواعد علم
His statement: After it was established that usul al-fiqh is the title of a specific science, the meaning of being a science is understood from it itself. Therefore, the author's addition of 'ilm (science) to usul al-fiqh is incorrect, as it becomes tautology: 'science of the science of fiqh'. Only saying 'usul al-fiqh is a science' would suffice. Apology: There was no need for the addition, but it was done for clarification and explanation, like the addition of 'shajarah' to 'al-arak' in 'shajarat al-arak' for clarification, otherwise 'arak' is itself a tree. And al-Qa'ida: definition of Qa'ida. Al-Qawa'id is plural of Qa'ida. The commentator defines Qa'ida: A Qa'ida is a general ruling that applies to all its particulars, so that when needed, knowledge of the rulings of particulars can be obtained from this general ruling. For example, 'Every ruling that is indicated by qiyas is established' is a Qa'ida. Through it, all rulings derived by qiyas can be established. For example, it is said: 'This ruling is indicated by qiyas, and every ruling indicated by qiyas is established', so the conclusion is 'This ruling is established'. And the near means (al-tawassul al-qarib) is taken from the ba (preposition). Purpose: answer to a question. The question is: You have taken 'tawassul' as near tawassul, what is your evidence? Answer: The commentator gives two evidences: (1) The ba in 'tawassul biha' is for cause, and cause has two types: near cause and far cause. The original cause is near cause, which is what comes to mind, so near tawassul is intended. (2) The second evidence: Here 'tawassul' is attributed and added to fiqh, and direct tawassul to fiqh can only be via near tawassul, because in far tawassul, tawassul to fiqh does not occur directly, but first tawassul to the intermediary, then from the intermediary to fiqh. Based on these two evidences, 'tawassul' here is taken as near tawassul. Then the commentator explains in detail the benefit of the condition 'near tawassul', saying that through this condition, the science of Arabic rules and theology (kalam) are excluded, because they are among the preliminaries of usul al-fiqh, and tawassul to fiqh through them is not near, but through them tawassul to the intermediary (far tawassul) occurs, then from the intermediary to fiqh. For example, from Arabic rules, first the quality of how words indicate their stipulated and linguistic meanings is known: whether it is mutabaqah (correspondence), tadammun (implication), or iltizam (requirement). Then through this intermediary, one gains the ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Thus, from Arabic grammar, tawassul leads to knowledge of the quality of indications, and then tawassul leads to istinbat and fiqh, so an intermediary comes in between, hence it is called far tawassul. Similarly, from the rules of kalam, first the establishment of the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness is obtained, then through that intermediary tawassul to fiqh occurs, so this too is not near tawassul. Therefore, both are excluded from usul al-fiqh. And the verification in this place: Man was not created in vain. Purpose: the commentator explains the need and necessity for fiqh and usul al-fiqh. The commentator says: Man was not created useless and futile, but for every action there is some ruling from the Lawgiver, e.g., this action is wajib, this is mandub, this is haram, etc. Then that ruling is connected to some specific evidence. The reason why the ruling is connected to evidence is that encompassing all particulars is impossible, so when needed, the ruling is derived from that evidence, and analogous rulings are obtained through qiyas. When it is established that every action of man has a ruling, we obtain several propositions. Their subject will be some action of the actions of the legally responsible person, and their predicate will be some ruling from the legal rulings (detailed rulings), e.g., prayer is obligatory, pilgrimage is obligatory, adultery is forbidden, etc. Then the collection of these propositions obtained from the evidences is called the science of fiqh. So far, the need for fiqh was explained. Next, the need for usul al-fiqh is explained. Then the jurists pondered over the rulings and their details, and they divided them. The evidences were classified into four types: Book, Sunnah, consensus, qiyas; and the rulings into six types: obligation, recommendation, permissibility, prohibition, etc. Then the jurists considered the quality of reasoning (istidlal) from these evidences to rulings, provided that reasoning is brief (ijmali) and without considering details. Then they obtained general propositions related to the quality of brief reasoning, e.g., 'Command implies obligation', and then its detail by way of example: 'Prayer is obligatory because of His statement: 'Establish prayer''. Similarly, along with the general propositions, they also learned the ways and conditions through which these propositions can be utilized for deriving rulings. Hence, they compiled these propositions along with their ways and conditions, added further appendices and completions, mentioned relevant differences, and named this entire collection usul al-fiqh. So usul al-fiqh became the name for those general rules and propositions that lead to fiqh. The commentator clarifies with the word 'al-qawa'id': The condition of 'ijmal' (briefness) that we attached to 'istidlal' is indicated by the word 'qawa'id', because qawa'id are inherently brief. And the author added the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' (on a verified basis). Its benefit is to exclude the science of dialectic (jadal) and disagreement (khilaf), as detailed in the commentary of the text. And someone might deny that his rules... Purpose: objection against the author. The objection is that the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is redundant, because its purpose is to exclude the science of disagreement (munazarah), but that has already been excluded by 'tawassul biha ila al-fiqh', because the rules of the science...
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a commentator's expansion on the definition of usul al-fiqh from the matn. It begins by addressing an objection: if usul al-fiqh is itself a science, adding the word 'science' before it creates a tautology. The commentator offers an apology, explaining that the addition is for clarification, similar to saying 'the tree of al-arak' even though al-arak is itself a tree. This is a standard Hanafi usul point: language permits such attributive constructions for emphasis or elucidation. Next, the commentator defines 'qa'ida' (plural: qawa'id) — a general rule that applies to all its particulars, such as 'every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.' This is a foundational concept in Hanafi usul: qawa'id are the general propositions that serve as tools for deriving fiqh rulings. The passage then discusses the term 'tawassul' (means) in the definition of usul al-fiqh. Two proofs are given that it refers to 'near means' (tawassul qarib) as opposed to 'far means' (tawassul ba'id). The first proof relies on the preposition 'ba' indicating causation, where the near cause is the default understanding. The second proof points out that tawassul is directly attributed to fiqh, so the means must be direct; far means involve an intermediary, such as Arabic grammar or theology, which only lead to fiqh indirectly. Thus, sciences like Arabic grammar and kalam are excluded from usul al-fiqh proper; they are merely preliminaries. The commentator then explains the necessity of fiqh and usul al-fiqh: humans are created with purpose, and every act has a legal ruling, but rulings are derived from evidence. Since encompassing all details is impossible, general rules (qawa'id) are needed for deriving rulings. The jurists compiled these rules into usul al-fiqh, adding conditions like 'on a verified basis' to exclude dialectics. The passage ends with another objection: the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is redundant because its purpose (excluding jadal and khilaf) is already achieved by the requirement of near tawassul. The text cuts off at 'qawa'id al-ilm'.

Key Terms
قاعدة (Qāʿida): A general ruling (حكم كلي) that applies to all its particulars, such as 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.'
توصل قریب (Tawassul Qarīb): Direct means that lead to fiqh without an intermediary.
توصل بعید (Tawassul Baʿīd): Means that reach fiqh through an intermediary step.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a 'qa'ida' (plural: qawa'id) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh?
A) A specific legal ruling derived from the Quran.
B) A general ruling that applies to all its particulars, used to derive rulings for new cases.
C) A theological principle about the attributes of God.
D) A rule of Arabic grammar.

Key Takeaway
A qa'ida is a general rule that governs all its particulars, forming the foundation for istinbat in Hanafi usul.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
Tawassul Qarib and the Scope of Usul al-Fiqh
Explanation of tawassul qarib and the exclusion of other sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between near and far means (tawassul qarib/ba'id) and explain why Arabic grammar and kalam are not part of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh includes only direct means to derive rulings; indirect means like grammar are mere preliminaries.

The definition of usul al-fiqh includes the term 'tawassul' (means). A question arises: does this mean direct or indirect means? The commentator provides two proofs that it refers to direct means (tawassul qarib), thereby excluding sciences like Arabic grammar and theology that only lead to fiqh through an intermediary. This distinction is crucial for defining the proper scope of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
The passage addresses a question: why is 'tawassul' taken as near tawassul? Understand that this is an objection to the definition of usul al-fiqh.
The question presupposes that the definition needs clarification.
2
Examine the first proof
The preposition 'ba' in 'tawassul biha' indicates causation. Cause has two types: near and far. The near cause is the default (mubādir ilā al-dhihn), so near tawassul is intended.
This proof relies on linguistic principle: the default is the near cause.
3
Examine the second proof
Tawassul is directly attributed (muḍāf) to fiqh. If it were far tawassul, it would first need to reach an intermediary, contradicting the direct attribution.
The grammatical construction of idāfah indicates direct connection.
4
Apply to Arabic grammar
Arabic grammar first leads to understanding how words indicate meanings (mutabaqah, tadammun, iltizam), then through that to fiqh. Hence it is a far means.
Grammar is a preliminary (mabda’) not part of usul.
5
Apply to kalam (theology)
Kalam first establishes the truthfulness of revelation, then through that to fiqh. Again, an intermediary step, so it is a far means.
Kalam is also a preliminary, not directly leading to fiqh.

میں علم کی اضافت اصول فقہ کی طرف کرنا یہ درست نہیں ہے گویا عبارت یوں ہوگی علم العلم یہ تو تکرار محض ہے صرف اصول الفقہ ھو علم کہنا کافی تھا۔ اعتذار! مصنف کی طرف سے اعتذار پیش کر رہے ہیں کہ یہاں اضافت کی حاجت تو نہیں تھی لیکن صرف بیان اور زیادہ وضاحت کیلئے علم کی اضافت الی اصول الفقہ کر دی گئی ہے جیسے شجرة الا راک میں شجرہ کی اضافت الی الا راک توضیح کیلئے ہے ور نہ اراک بھی ایک شجرہ ہے والقاعدۃ حکم کی غرض تعریف قاعدہ ! القواعد قاعدۃ کی جمع ہے شارح قاعدہ کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں کہ قاعدہ وہ حکم کی ہے جو اپنے جمیع جزئیات پر منطبق اور صادق آئے تاکہ بوقت ضرورت اس حکم کلی سے جزئیات کے احکام کی معرفت حاصل نتیجہ نکل گا هذا الحكم ثابت والتوصل القريب مستفاد من الباء غرض جواب سوال سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے توصل سے توصل قریب مراد لیا ہے اس پر آپ کے پاس کیا دلیل ہے۔ جواب ! شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ہمارے پاس دو دلیلیں ہیں (1) توصل بھا میں باد سبیہ ہے اور سبب کی دو قسمیں ہیں سبب قریب اور سبب بعید اصل سبب قریب ہوتا ہے وہی متبادر الی الذہن ہوتا ہے لہذا توصل قریب مراد ہوگا (۲) دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں توصل منسوب و مضاف الی الفقہ ہے اور براہ راست فقہ تک توصل توصل قریب کے ساتھ ہی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ توصل بعید میں فقہ تک توصل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ پہلے توصل الی الواسطہ ہوتا ہے پھر واسطہ سے توصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے انہی دو دلیلوں کے تحت یہاں توصل سے تو ضل قریب مراد لیا گیا۔ فيخرج العلم بقواعد العربيه الخ اس عبارت میں شارح کچھ تفصیل کے ساتھ توصل قریب کا فائدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اس قید سے علم بقواعد العربیہ اور علم کلام خارج ہو گئے کیونکہ یہ مبادی اصول فقہ میں سے ہیں اور ان کے ساتھ توصل الی الفقہ تو صل قریب نہیں ہے بلکہ ان کے ذریعہ سے توصل الی الواسطہ ( توصل بعید ) ہوتا ہے پھر واسطہ سے توصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے مثلاً قواعد عربیہ سے اولا الفاظ کی جو اپنے مدلالات وضعیہ ولغو یہ پر دلالت ہوتی ہے اس کی کیفیت معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ یہ کونسی دلالت ہے مطابقی ہے یا ضمنی یا التزامی پھر اس واسطہ سے کتاب دستہ سے احکام کے استنباط پر قدرت حاصل ہوتی ہے تو علم عربیت سے توصل ہوا ہے الفاظ کے مدلولات کی کیفیت کی معرفت کی طرف پھر اس کے بعد توصل ہوا ہے الی الاستنباط والفقہ تو درمیان میں واسطہ آ گیا اس لیے اس کو تو صل بعید کہا جائے گا اسی طرح قواعد کلام سے اولا کتاب وسیہ کا ثبوت اور ان کے صدق کا وجوب حاصل ہوتا ہے پھر اس واسطہ سے فقہ تک توصل ہوتا ہے تو یہ بھی توصل قریب نہیں ہے لہذا یہ دونوں اصول فقہ سے خارج ہیں و التحقيق في هذا المقام انا الانسان لم يخلق عبثا غرض شارح بيان حاجت وضرورت ! الی الفقہ والی اصول فقہ وتد و نھا اس کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے شارح کہتے ہیں کہ انسان کو بے کار اور مہمل (سدی) نہیں پیدا کیا گیا بلکہ اس کے ہر عمل کے ساتھ شارع کی طرف سے کوئی نہ کوئی حکم متعلق ہوتا ہے مثلاً هذ العمل واجب هذا العمل مندوب هذا العمل حرام وغیرہ پھر وہ کم کسی نہ کسی دلیل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوتا ہے جو دلیل اس حکم کے ساتھ خاص ہوتی ہے دلیل کے ساتھ حکم کے متعلق ہونے کہ وجہ یہ بیان کی کہ تمام جزئیات کا احاطہ متعذر ہے تو بوقت حاجت اس دلیل سے حکم مستقبط کر لیا جائے گا اور اس کے جو مناسب احکام ہو نگے ان کو قیاس کر لیا جائے گا جب ثابت ہوا کہ انسان کے ہر عمل سے کوئی نہ کوئی حکم متعلق ہوتا ہے تو اس سے ہمیں چند قضایا حاصل ہو گئے ان کا موضوع افعال مکلفین میں سے کوئی فعل ہو گا اور محمول ا کام شرع میں سے کوئی حکم ( تفصیلی احکام ) ہوگا مثلا الصلوۃ واجبہ، انج واجب ، الزنا حرام وغیرہ پھر ان قضایا کا جوعلم ادلہ سے حاصل ہو گا اس کا نام علم الفقہ ہے۔ یہاں تک تو حاجت الی الفقہ کا بیان تھا آگے حاجت الی اصول الفقہ کا بیان ہے پھر فقہاء نے اولہ اور احکام میں غور و فکر کیا ان کی تفاصیل میں گئے اور ان میں تقسیم کی تو ادلہ کا رجوع اقسام اربعہ کی طرف ہوا کتاب ستہ اجماع، قیاس اور احکام کا رجوع اقسام ستہ کی طرف ہوا وجوب ندب اباحت حرمت کراہت وغیرہ پھر فقہاء نے ان ادلہ سے جو احکام پر استدلال کیا جاتا ہے اس استدلال کی کیفیت میں تامل کیا بشر طیکہ وہ استدلال اجمانی ہو مع قطع النظر عن التفصیل پھر ان کو اور قضایا کلیہ حاصل ہو گئے جو استدلال اجمالی کی کیفیت سے متعلق تھے من غير تفصيل الاعلى ارادة المثال مثلاً یوں کہا جائے الامر للوجوب پھر اس کی تفصیل بطور مثال بیان کی جائے الصلوہ واجبہ لقولہ تعالی واقیمو الصلوۃ اسی طرح ان کو قضایا کلیہ حاصل ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ وہ شراکا اور طرق بھی معلوم ہو گئے جن کے ذریعہ سے ان قضایا کو اسنباط احکام کیلئے وسیلہ اور ذریعہ بنایا جا سکے لہذا انہوں نے ان قضایا کو بمع طرق و شرائط ضبط اور مدون کیا اور ان کے ساتھ مزید لواحق و متممات کا بھی اضافہ کر دیا اور مناسب اختلافات کو ذکر کر دیا اور اس سب مجموعہ کا نام اصول فقہ رکھد یا تو اصول فقہ نام ہو گیا ان قواعد قضایا کلیہ کا جو موصل الی الفقہ ہوں شارح و لفظ القواعدہ سے وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ ہم نے استدلال کے ساتھ جوا جمال کی قید لگائی ہے لفظ قواعد اس پر دال ہے کیونکہ قواعد میں اجمال ہی ہوتا ہے وزاد المصنف قيد التحقیق سے علی وجد اتحقیق کی قید کا فائدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ اس سے علم الجدل والخلاف نے احتر از مقصود ہے کما مر تفصیلہ فی توضیح المتن - ولقائل ان يمنع كون قواعده غرض شارح اعتراض علی المصنف ! اعتراض یہ ہے کہ قید علی وجہ اتحقیق مستدرک اور بے کار ہے کیونکہ اس سے علم الخلاف (علم مناظرہ) کو خارج کرنا مقصود ہے اور وہ بتوصل بھا الی الفقہ سے خارج ہو چکا ہے کیونکہ قواعد علم
His statement: After it was established that usul al-fiqh is the title of a specific science, the meaning of being a science is understood from it itself. Therefore, the author's addition of 'ilm (science) to usul al-fiqh is incorrect, as it becomes tautology: 'science of the science of fiqh'. Only saying 'usul al-fiqh is a science' would suffice. Apology: There was no need for the addition, but it was done for clarification and explanation, like the addition of 'shajarah' to 'al-arak' in 'shajarat al-arak' for clarification, otherwise 'arak' is itself a tree. And al-Qa'ida: definition of Qa'ida. Al-Qawa'id is plural of Qa'ida. The commentator defines Qa'ida: A Qa'ida is a general ruling that applies to all its particulars, so that when needed, knowledge of the rulings of particulars can be obtained from this general ruling. For example, 'Every ruling that is indicated by qiyas is established' is a Qa'ida. Through it, all rulings derived by qiyas can be established. For example, it is said: 'This ruling is indicated by qiyas, and every ruling indicated by qiyas is established', so the conclusion is 'This ruling is established'. And the near means (al-tawassul al-qarib) is taken from the ba (preposition). Purpose: answer to a question. The question is: You have taken 'tawassul' as near tawassul, what is your evidence? Answer: The commentator gives two evidences: (1) The ba in 'tawassul biha' is for cause, and cause has two types: near cause and far cause. The original cause is near cause, which is what comes to mind, so near tawassul is intended. (2) The second evidence: Here 'tawassul' is attributed and added to fiqh, and direct tawassul to fiqh can only be via near tawassul, because in far tawassul, tawassul to fiqh does not occur directly, but first tawassul to the intermediary, then from the intermediary to fiqh. Based on these two evidences, 'tawassul' here is taken as near tawassul. Then the commentator explains in detail the benefit of the condition 'near tawassul', saying that through this condition, the science of Arabic rules and theology (kalam) are excluded, because they are among the preliminaries of usul al-fiqh, and tawassul to fiqh through them is not near, but through them tawassul to the intermediary (far tawassul) occurs, then from the intermediary to fiqh. For example, from Arabic rules, first the quality of how words indicate their stipulated and linguistic meanings is known: whether it is mutabaqah (correspondence), tadammun (implication), or iltizam (requirement). Then through this intermediary, one gains the ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Thus, from Arabic grammar, tawassul leads to knowledge of the quality of indications, and then tawassul leads to istinbat and fiqh, so an intermediary comes in between, hence it is called far tawassul. Similarly, from the rules of kalam, first the establishment of the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness is obtained, then through that intermediary tawassul to fiqh occurs, so this too is not near tawassul. Therefore, both are excluded from usul al-fiqh. And the verification in this place: Man was not created in vain. Purpose: the commentator explains the need and necessity for fiqh and usul al-fiqh. The commentator says: Man was not created useless and futile, but for every action there is some ruling from the Lawgiver, e.g., this action is wajib, this is mandub, this is haram, etc. Then that ruling is connected to some specific evidence. The reason why the ruling is connected to evidence is that encompassing all particulars is impossible, so when needed, the ruling is derived from that evidence, and analogous rulings are obtained through qiyas. When it is established that every action of man has a ruling, we obtain several propositions. Their subject will be some action of the actions of the legally responsible person, and their predicate will be some ruling from the legal rulings (detailed rulings), e.g., prayer is obligatory, pilgrimage is obligatory, adultery is forbidden, etc. Then the collection of these propositions obtained from the evidences is called the science of fiqh. So far, the need for fiqh was explained. Next, the need for usul al-fiqh is explained. Then the jurists pondered over the rulings and their details, and they divided them. The evidences were classified into four types: Book, Sunnah, consensus, qiyas; and the rulings into six types: obligation, recommendation, permissibility, prohibition, etc. Then the jurists considered the quality of reasoning (istidlal) from these evidences to rulings, provided that reasoning is brief (ijmali) and without considering details. Then they obtained general propositions related to the quality of brief reasoning, e.g., 'Command implies obligation', and then its detail by way of example: 'Prayer is obligatory because of His statement: 'Establish prayer''. Similarly, along with the general propositions, they also learned the ways and conditions through which these propositions can be utilized for deriving rulings. Hence, they compiled these propositions along with their ways and conditions, added further appendices and completions, mentioned relevant differences, and named this entire collection usul al-fiqh. So usul al-fiqh became the name for those general rules and propositions that lead to fiqh. The commentator clarifies with the word 'al-qawa'id': The condition of 'ijmal' (briefness) that we attached to 'istidlal' is indicated by the word 'qawa'id', because qawa'id are inherently brief. And the author added the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' (on a verified basis). Its benefit is to exclude the science of dialectic (jadal) and disagreement (khilaf), as detailed in the commentary of the text. And someone might deny that his rules... Purpose: objection against the author. The objection is that the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is redundant, because its purpose is to exclude the science of disagreement (munazarah), but that has already been excluded by 'tawassul biha ila al-fiqh', because the rules of the science...
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a commentator's expansion on the definition of usul al-fiqh from the matn. It begins by addressing an objection: if usul al-fiqh is itself a science, adding the word 'science' before it creates a tautology. The commentator offers an apology, explaining that the addition is for clarification, similar to saying 'the tree of al-arak' even though al-arak is itself a tree. This is a standard Hanafi usul point: language permits such attributive constructions for emphasis or elucidation. Next, the commentator defines 'qa'ida' (plural: qawa'id) — a general rule that applies to all its particulars, such as 'every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.' This is a foundational concept in Hanafi usul: qawa'id are the general propositions that serve as tools for deriving fiqh rulings. The passage then discusses the term 'tawassul' (means) in the definition of usul al-fiqh. Two proofs are given that it refers to 'near means' (tawassul qarib) as opposed to 'far means' (tawassul ba'id). The first proof relies on the preposition 'ba' indicating causation, where the near cause is the default understanding. The second proof points out that tawassul is directly attributed to fiqh, so the means must be direct; far means involve an intermediary, such as Arabic grammar or theology, which only lead to fiqh indirectly. Thus, sciences like Arabic grammar and kalam are excluded from usul al-fiqh proper; they are merely preliminaries. The commentator then explains the necessity of fiqh and usul al-fiqh: humans are created with purpose, and every act has a legal ruling, but rulings are derived from evidence. Since encompassing all details is impossible, general rules (qawa'id) are needed for deriving rulings. The jurists compiled these rules into usul al-fiqh, adding conditions like 'on a verified basis' to exclude dialectics. The passage ends with another objection: the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' is redundant because its purpose (excluding jadal and khilaf) is already achieved by the requirement of near tawassul. The text cuts off at 'qawa'id al-ilm'.

Key Terms
قاعدة (Qāʿida): A general ruling (حكم كلي) that applies to all its particulars, such as 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.'
توصل قریب (Tawassul Qarīb): Direct means that lead to fiqh without an intermediary.
توصل بعید (Tawassul Baʿīd): Means that reach fiqh through an intermediary step.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which two proofs does the commentator give to show that 'tawassul' in the definition of usul al-fiqh means near means (tawassul qarib)?
A) The word 'tawassul' is derived from 'wasila', and the default is near; and the preposition 'ba' indicates nearness.
B) The preposition 'ba' indicates causation, and the near cause is the default; and the attribution of 'tawassul' to fiqh requires directness.
C) The Prophet said 'tawassulu bi al-ilm' and the companions understood it as near; and the logical analysis shows it must be near.
D) The context of usul al-fiqh requires near means; and the majority of scholars agree.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh concerns only direct means (tawassul qarib); indirect sciences like grammar are preliminaries, not part of usul.

Method of Learning

The Four Figures of Syllogism in Usul al-Fiqh: Universal Premises as Core
Explaining the logical structure of usul al-fiqh via syllogistic figures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four figures of categorical syllogism, classify the example of Hajj being wajib into the first figure, and explain how universal premises (qawa'id kulliyya) form the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh provides the universal premises that, when combined with specific cases, yield fiqh rulings through the first figure of syllogism.

This lesson introduces the logical framework underlying Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The passage you will read explains the four figures of categorical syllogism and then demonstrates how the definition of usul al-fiqh as 'the rules by which fiqh is derived' refers to universal propositions that serve as major premises. By understanding this logical structure, you will see how usul al-fiqh is not a random collection of rules but a coherent deductive system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four figures
Distinguish the position of the middle term (hadd awsat) in each figure as described in the text. Note that the passage may have some numbering confusion; focus on the standard classification: first figure: M-P in major, S-M in minor; second figure: P-M, S-M; third figure: M-P, M-S; fourth figure: P-M, M-S.
The text's description: (1) middle term predicate in minor, subject in major (first figure); (2) opposite (fourth figure); (3) predicate in both (second figure); (4) subject in both (third figure).
2
Parse the example
Take the example 'Hajj is wajib because it is commanded by the Lawgiver and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib.' Identify the minor premise, major premise, middle term, and conclusion. Determine which figure it belongs to.
The middle term is 'commanded by the Lawgiver' (مأمور الشارع). It is predicate in the minor and subject in the major, so first figure.
3
Connect to usul al-fiqh
Understand that the major premise ('Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib') is a universal rule (qa'ida kulliyya) that is the product of usul al-fiqh. The minor premise ('Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver') is obtained from the specific texts.
This illustrates how usul al-fiqh provides the major premise for legal deduction.
4
Reflect on the definition
The passage states that the 'rules' in the definition of usul al-fiqh refer specifically to these universal propositions in the first figure. Discuss why the first figure is prioritized: it is the only figure that yields a certain conclusion directly.
In Aristotelian logic, only the first figure is perfect; the others require reduction.
5
Recognize the scope
Note that acquiring these universal rules requires studying proofs, conditions, and restrictions, all of which belong to usul al-fiqh. Thus, usul al-fiqh includes not only the universal premises themselves but also the discussions that establish them.
This broadens the scope of usul to include methodology and conditions.

He is explaining the four: (1) If the middle term is the predicate in the minor premise and the subject in the major premise, it is called the first figure. (2) If the opposite, i.e., subject in the minor and predicate in the major, it is called the fourth figure. (3) If the middle term is the predicate in both, it is the third figure? Actually, the text says 'khali' (empty) but standard: third figure has middle as subject in both? Wait, the passage says: (3) If the middle term is predicate in both, it is called the third figure (khali? actually should be second? But text says 'shakl khali'? Possibly a corruption). (4) If the middle term is subject in both, it is called the second figure? The text says 'shakl thalith'. There's confusion. The example given: 'Hajj is wajib because it is commanded by the Lawgiver, and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib.' The middle term 'commanded by the Lawgiver' is predicate in the minor and subject in the major, so first figure. Then: 'So the universal premises that lead to fiqh are the universal propositions.' After explaining the terms, the commentator Taftazani now states the intended meaning regarding the definition of usul al-fiqh: that the 'qawa'id' mentioned in its definition refer to those universal propositions that serve as the major premise of the first figure. When deducing fiqh issues via the first figure, the minor premise is readily obtained, and the major is the universal proposition prepared in usul al-fiqh, which contains the desired conclusion. As in the previous example, 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib' is the major, and this is among the propositions of usul al-fiqh. The goal is to combine this universal rule (prepared in usul al-fiqh) with the readily obtained minor to actualize our desired fiqh ruling from potentiality to actuality. This is called 'at-tawassul ila al-fiqh'. However, acquiring this universal rule is not easy; it depends on discussing the circumstances of proofs and rulings, their conditions and restrictions that are considered in this universal rule. Therefore, just as the universal rule is among the topics and discussions of usul al-fiqh, so too the discussions related to it, conditions, restrictions, etc., are among the discussions of usul al-fiqh. And all of them fall under the knowledge of the universal rule. The author's explanation is sufficient; no further clarification needed.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the logical structure underlying usul al-fiqh. It begins by outlining the four figures of categorical syllogism, focusing on the position of the middle term (حد وسط). The commentator then applies this to a fiqh example: the ruling that Hajj is wajib. The minor premise is 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' (obtained from the revealed texts), and the major premise is 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is wajib' (a universal rule from usul al-fiqh). The conclusion 'Hajj is wajib' follows in the first figure. This illustrates how usul al-fiqh provides the universal premises (القواعد الكلية) that serve as the major premise in analogical deduction. The passage then clarifies that the definition of usul al-fiqh as 'the rules by which fiqh is derived' refers specifically to these universal propositions in the first figure. It emphasizes that acquiring these universal rules requires detailed study of the proofs and rulings, including their conditions and qualifications. All such discussions fall within the scope of usul al-fiqh. This logical framework is foundational to Hanafi usul methodology, which often employs Aristotelian logic to structure legal reasoning.

Key Terms
حد أوسط (hadd awsat): The middle term in a syllogism, shared between both premises, allowing the conclusion.
قاعدة كلية (qa'ida kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as a major premise in the first figure, forming the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.
صغرى (sughra): The minor premise in a syllogism, containing the subject of the conclusion.
كبرى (kubra): The major premise in a syllogism, containing the predicate of the conclusion.
شكل أول (shakl awwal): The first figure of categorical syllogism, where the middle term is subject in the major and predicate in the minor.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal premises that, when combined with specific textual evidence in the first figure of syllogism, yield fiqh rulings.

Two Interpretations of 'Mutawassal' in Usul al-Fiqh Definition
Explaining two possible referents of 'mutawassal'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two possible referents of 'mutawassal' in the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and explain how each interpretation affects the inclusion of taqlid discussions.

Core Idea
The definition of usul al-fiqh can include or exclude the muqallid depending on how we interpret 'mutawassal'.

The definition of usul al-fiqh as 'the principles by which one arrives at fiqh' hinges on the word 'mutawassal' (the one who arrives). Who exactly is this person? Only the mujtahid who derives rulings directly from the four proofs, or also the muqallid who follows a mujtahid? This lesson unpacks the two interpretations presented in the commentary and their implications for the scope of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Locate 'mutawassal' in the definition
The word 'tawassul' (reaching) appears in the definition of usul al-fiqh. The passive participle 'mutawassal' refers to the one who reaches fiqh through these principles. Identify which part of the definition is under scrutiny.
The precise wording is: 'al-qawa'id allati yutawassalu biha ila al-fiqh'.
2
State the first interpretation (mujtahid only)
According to the first view, 'mutawassal' refers exclusively to the mujtahid. Because fiqh is defined as knowledge of rulings from the four proofs, and only a mujtahid can derive rulings directly from those proofs. A muqallid relies on the mujtahid's statement, not the proofs themselves.
This view is the basis for the standard Hanafi position that taqlid and istifta discussions are not part of usul al-fiqh.
3
State the second interpretation (both mujtahid and muqallid)
A second view broadens 'mutawassal' to include the muqallid. The muqallid also 'arrives' at fiqh, but through the mujtahid's statement as his proof. This requires two modifications to the definition: (1) generalizing the source of rulings beyond the four proofs, and (2) replacing 'fiqh' with 'masa'il al-fiqh' to cover the muqallid's knowledge.
This view accommodates scholars who include taqlid and istifta chapters in usul works.
4
Analyze the 'tahqiq' objection and resolution
A doubt arises: the definition includes 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' (on the basis of investigation), which seems to exclude taqlid. The author resolves this by showing that both mujtahid and muqallid perform investigation, but their objects differ: the mujtahid investigates the four proofs, the muqallid investigates the mujtahid's statement and believes it to be true.
Thus, 'tahqiq' is preserved for both, maintaining the definition's inclusivity.

And our statement 'by which one arrives at it' etc. After explaining the principles, they are explaining the investigation of 'tawassul'. The author says: In the definition of usul al-fiqh, the word 'tawassul' appears. Who is the 'mutawassal'? There are two probabilities: (1) The mutawassal refers only to the mujtahid, because in usul al-fiqh, those universal principles and propositions are discussed by which only the mujtahid can arrive at fiqh. So the mutawassal ila al-fiqh is only the mujtahid, because fiqh is the knowledge of rulings from proofs, and by proofs is meant the four proofs. And attaining knowledge of rulings from the four proofs is the work of only the mujtahid, not the muqallid, because the muqallid's knowledge of rulings is obtained from the statement of the mujtahid, not from the four proofs. (On this basis, the discussions of taqlid and istifta are not included in our books of usul al-fiqh.) (2) 'It is not far to say' presents the second probability: it is not far-fetched that mutawassal be kept general, meaning both mujtahid and muqallid. In this case, two changes must be made in the definition of usul al-fiqh. One change: from 'the first' does not refer only to the four proofs, but rather generalizes, whether knowledge of rulings is obtained from the four proofs or from some other proof besides them. So this definition will include both the mujtahid and the muqallid. Now the mujtahid will obtain knowledge of rulings from the four proofs, but the muqallid will not obtain knowledge of rulings from the four proofs; rather his knowledge will be obtained from another proof, and that proof is the statement of the mujtahid. From it he will obtain knowledge of rulings. For example, he will establish a ruling thus: 'This ruling is established for me because the opinion of Abu Hanifa has reached me, and everything that the opinion of Abu Hanifa reaches is established for me.' Now the second proposition 'everything that the opinion of Abu Hanifa reaches' is from the principles of fiqh. On this basis, some scholars have mentioned the discussions of taqlid and istifta in the books of usul al-fiqh. 'Based on this' mentions the second change: according to this probability, in the definition, the word 'masa'il' must be added before 'al-fiqh'. The definition would be: 'by which one arrives at the issues of fiqh', because when this definition includes both mujtahid and muqallid, the change is inevitable. Because if 'tawassul ila al-fiqh' is said, then tawassul would become specific to the mujtahid, because fiqh is called knowledge of rulings from the four proofs, and that is with the mujtahid. So the word 'masa'il' will be added, and 'tawassul ila masa'il al-fiqh' is general, including both mujtahid and muqallid. And his statement 'on the basis of investigation' is intended to remove a doubt. The doubt is that although you have generalized the mutawassal and included the muqallid, but with 'ala wajh al-tahqiq', the knowledge of the muqallid would become excluded, because his tawassul to the issues of fiqh is not on the basis of investigation, but on the basis of taqlid. There is a contrast between investigation and taqlid. The author removes this doubt: this condition is not contrary to the muqallid, because the muqallid's tawassul is also on the basis of investigation, but the investigation of the two differs. The mujtahid's tawassul on the basis of investigation is that he has tawassul to fiqh with the four proofs, and the muqallid's tawassul on the basis of investigation is that he has tawassul with the statement of the mujtahid, and he believes in the reality of his statement.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of usul al-fiqh, specifically analyzing the word 'tawassul' (reaching). The author, Sharh al-Tawdih, presents two possible interpretations of 'mutawassal' (the one who reaches). The first restricts it to the mujtahid alone, since fiqh is knowledge of rulings from the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), and only a mujtahid can derive rulings directly from these sources. A muqallid (follower) relies on the mujtahid's statement, not the proofs themselves. Consequently, Hanafi usul works omit discussions of taqlid and istifta. The second interpretation broadens 'mutawassal' to include both mujtahid and muqallid. This requires two modifications to the definition: first, expanding 'proofs' to include the mujtahid's statement as a proof for the muqallid; second, changing 'fiqh' to 'masa'il al-fiqh' (issues of fiqh) to encompass the muqallid's knowledge. The author then addresses a doubt: the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' (on the basis of investigation) might exclude the muqallid, but he clarifies that both reach rulings through investigation, though their methods differ. The mujtahid investigates the four proofs, while the muqallid investigates the mujtahid's statement, believing it to be true. This preserves the definition's generality.

Key Terms
متوصل (mutawassal): The one who reaches or arrives at fiqh through the principles of usul al-fiqh
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of legal rulings derived from specific proofs (the four proofs)
تقلید (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without knowing the detailed proof
تحقیق (tahqiq): Investigation or verification; reaching a ruling through personal inquiry into proofs

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation of 'mutawassal', why are taqlid and istifta not discussed in Hanafi usul al-fiqh books?
A) Because taqlid is forbidden in the Hanafi madhhab.
B) Because the muqallid does not derive rulings from the four proofs directly, so his method is not part of usul al-fiqh.
C) Because the mujtahid's statements are not considered proof.
D) Because the Hanafi school follows only the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The definition of usul al-fiqh can be interpreted narrowly (mujtahid only) or broadly (including muqallid), each with implications for what topics belong in the discipline.
